title": "Chicken bog recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken bog recipe Meat, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #bacon #chickenbogrecipe #broth #rice #butter #simmer #onion #boil #fat #spices \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Chicken bog is a pilau dish made of rice, chicken, celery, spices, and often sausage\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4296\n|PortionCalories = 429\n|DatePublished=6th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Chicken bog recipe 1\n |Servings = Serves 10\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Chicken bog recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Wasn't sure what this would be like</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but it's nice - rather like a very good chicken soup.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Chicken]] bog is a pilau dish made of [[Rice|rice]], chicken, [[Celery|celery]], [[Spices|spices]], and often [[Sausage|sausage]]. Loris, South Carolina celebrates an annual festival called the \"Loris Bog-Off\". \n\nChicken bog is made in different ways in different places, but it is perhaps found most often in the Pee Dee and Low country regions of South Carolina.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 very large whole [[Chicken|chicken]] 2.2kg to 2.7 kg (5lb to 6 lb)\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]]\n| 1 green [[Sweet pepper|sweet pepper]]\n| 110g (4 oz) [[Butter|butter]]\n| 900 g (2 lb) long [[Grain|grain]] [[White rice|white rice]] ([[Basmati rice|basmati rice]] is good)\n| 110g (4 oz) [[Bacon|bacon]]\n| 6 cups (1.5 litres / 2.6 pints) [[chicken stock]] / chicken broth\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Parson's nose|Remove the parson's nose]] from the chicken.\n| Use a heavy pot with lid (use lid while cooking for all steps except the [[Bacon|bacon]].)\n| Put [[Chicken|chicken]] in pot and cover with hot water. Be sure there is enough water so that there will be at least six cups of [[Broth|broth]] after cooking chicken. \n| Bring to a [[Boil|boil]], then reduce heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] until chicken is very tender (an hour or more).\n| While the [[Chicken|chicken]] is cooking: Slice and chop one [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] into very small pieces. Put 4 cups of [[Rice|rice]] into a bowl, cover with cold water and let soak.\n| When [[Chicken|chicken]] is very tender, remove pot from stove and let cool until the chicken can be handled.\n| Take [[Chicken|chicken]] from pot, and pull [[Meat|meat]] from [[bones]] in large pieces; do not cut it up. Discard any [[Fat|fat]] heavy skin.\n| Pour [[Broth|broth]] from pot into a bowl (if [[Chicken|chicken]] was very [[Fat|fat]] and broth is very fat, pour off about 1 cup of fat from broth).\n| Wash pot, then put [[Bacon|bacon]] in pot and cook slowly until bacon is crisp.\n| Take [[Bacon|bacon]] from pot and drain; leave bacon grease in pot.\n| Put in chopped [[Onion|onion]], [[Green pepper|green pepper]] and [[Brown|brown]] slightly.\n| Add 6 cups [[Chicken|chicken]] [[Broth|broth]] to pot, and season to taste with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] (at least a tablespoon of each -- use a heavy [[Hand|hand]] since [[Rice|rice]] will absorb salt).\n| Increase heat, bring [[Broth|broth]] to a [[Boil|boil]], and put [[Chicken|chicken]] in pot.\n| Drain [[Rice|rice]] and put rice in pot.\n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] and mix well. Reduce heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] very slowly for about an hour.\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse 225 g (8 oz) of [[spicy sausages]] or [[smoked sausages]] instead of the [[bacon]].\n==See also==\n* {{See also - Jointing a chicken}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #bacon #chickenbogrecipe #broth #rice #butter #simmer #onion #boil #fat #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Chicken jambalaya",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken jambalaya, | Cajun recipes from the cook's Wiki\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chickenjambalaya #chicken #stock #onion #bayleaf #celery #rice #worchestersauce #ham #butter #parsley \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Jambalaya always brings to mind the Carpenters song; Jambalaya (On the Bayou) - this is what they were singing about\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1847\n|PortionCalories = 307\n|DatePublished=2nd January 2013\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Chicken jambalaya with chorizo\n|Servings = 6 people\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes<br />(includes cooking a chicken)\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Chicken jambalaya recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">So this is what it is</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Until I first made this I had no idea what Jambalaya was.  It's nice - a one-pot rice dish.  Simples!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nJambalaya always brings to mind the Carpenters song; ''Jambalaya (On the Bayou)''  Not a Carpenters song but a dish traditionally made in one pot, with [[Meats|meats]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It is completed by adding [[Stock|stock]] and [[Rice|rice]].  Looking at various recipes in more detail, this strikes me now as a typical leftover dish.  Cooking up what you have around at the time.\n===Making this your own recipe===\nWhen I made this for the first time, not having the slightest idea what jambalaya was, it looked quite complex, however, having made it many times now I now think it is probably one of the easiest recipes around. It is also a brilliant recipe to adapt to your own personal taste.  It is also an excellent recipe for using up leftovers.\n\nJust follow a few basic steps and you will be able to make you own version of this recipe.\n* Rinse the rice in cold running water first.\n* Fry the onions, garlic and vegetables first, plus any meat that might need more cooking than the rice does.\n* Ensure the rice is well coated in the oil before adding any stock.\n* Measure the stock by doubling the volume of the rice (4 cups of water to 2 cups of rice, etc.)\n* Don't add all of the stock at once, add more if it looks as though it will dry out before the rice is done.\n* If you have ingredients that don't need much cooking (prawns etc.) or vegetables that you want to serve with a bit of a crunch then add them during the last five minutes of cooking.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 x 2kg (4 lb) [[Chicken|chicken]], [[Parson's nose|parson's nose removed]]\n| A few [[Bay leaf|bay leaves]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], unpeeled, chopped into quarters\n| About 200 g from one or more of cooked meat\n| 40 g (1 &frac12; oz) [[Butter|butter]], [[ghee]] or [[olive oil]]\n| 4 to 7 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 6 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 2 sticks of [[Celery|celery]], 'strings' removed with a [[Mandoline|mandoline]] and chopped into moons\n| 3 or 4 sweet [[Bell peppers|bell peppers]], any colour, deseeded and chopped\n| 3 teaspoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[dried oregano]] or [[dried mixed herbs]]\n| 2 tablespoons fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], chopped, if available\n| 1 large can [[Plum|plum]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped\n| 500ml to 600 ml of the water the [[Chicken|chicken]] was [[Boiled|boiled]] in\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcester sauce|Worcester sauce]]\n| [[Chillies]], [[chilli sauce]] or [[chilli powder]] to add warmth, not heat.\n|* I used: 1 teaspoon chili guajillo (powder), 2 teaspoons pasilla chili (diced), 1/2 a teaspoon of chipotle chillies (diced)\n|* Suggested alternative if using sauce: 1 to 2 tablespoons [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]] (or to taste)\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 400 g (14 oz) [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]] ([[Long grain rice|long grain rice]])\n}}\n''' Garnish'''\n* Finely chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Remove any giblets, cut off and discard the [[Parson's nose]].\n| Wash the [[Chicken|chicken]] under cold running water, inside and out\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] in a large pot and pour over just enough [[Boiling|boiling]] water to cover\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and [[Boil|boil]] for about 1 hour or until tender\n| Set the [[Chicken|chicken]] to one side, reserve the [[Stock|stock]] and discard the [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]] and [[Onion|onion]] quarters\n| Once chicken has cooled discard skin and bone\n| Heat the [[Butter|butter]] in a large pan and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] for a few minutes\n| Add the [[Ham|ham]], [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Celery|celery]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Saut\u00e9|saut\u00e9]] for 5 minutes\n| Rinse rice under cold running water for a few minutes until the water runs clear\n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a minute so the grains are coated by the oil\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]] (about 500 ml to start), [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Spices|spices]], [[Worcester sauce|Worcester sauce]], [[Hot pepper sauce|hot pepper sauce]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| Stir well, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] on a very low hob until the liquid has gone and the [[Rice|rice]] is cooked.  Add a little more water if it dries out before the rice is done.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken jambalaya in pot.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken jambalaya, ready to cook\nImage:Chicken jambalaya boil.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken, ready to boil\n</gallery>\n===Variations===\nI raided the garden for anything to add to the chicken boil: a few [[carrots]], some [[leeks]] a few spare sticks of [[celery]] and bunches of [[parsley]].\n===Chef's notes===\nI have doubled the rice quantity from the original recipe as there was so little rice.  I have not quite doubled the stock quantity so keep an eye on the water level to ensure that it does not dry out.\n\nRather than using [[chili sauce]] for the heat I used a mixture of my [[Exotic chili powders]] to add more than just heat.  The quantities I used did not make this hot (like a chili), just a little warmth.\n\nThe [[stock]] left from cooking the chicken is really good quality so whatever you don't use, freeze in bags or cups far later use.\n\n==See also==\n* http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jambalaya\n* http://www.bbcgoodfood.com/recipes/1167651/chicken-and-chorizo-jambalaya\n* http://www.deliaonline.com/recipes/type-of-dish/one-pot-meals/chicken-jambalaya.html\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Indian recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chickenjambalaya #chicken #stock #onion #bayleaf #celery #rice #worchestersauce #ham #butter #parsley </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Chicken jambalaya (TM)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chicken jambalaya - A Thermomix recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #sauce #bayleaf #rice #onion #thermomix #parsley #bacon #garlic #springonions #celery \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is a chicken jamabalaya recipe for the Thermomix. The chicken is steamed in the Varoma basket, but can also be poached in the bowl at 90\u00b0\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1430\n|PortionCalories = 357\n|DatePublished=20th October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 45 minutes \n|PrepTime = 25 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour 20 minutes \n|Image = [[Image:Chicken jambalaya (TM) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Just like the song</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but Thermy-made!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is a [[Chicken|chicken]] jamabalaya recipe for the [[Thermomix]].  The chicken is [[Steamed|steamed]] in the Varoma basket, but can also be [[Poached|poached]] in the bowl at 90\u00b0.\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n| 1 x 1.3kg [[Chicken|chicken]], [[parson's nose]] removed\n| 1 small [[Onion|onion]], cut into quarters\n| 1 [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]\n| [[Garlic]], to taste, peeled\n| 30g [[Butter|butter]], [[Ghee|ghee]] or [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 100g cooked [[Bacon|bacon]]\n| 4 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n| 2 sticks of [[Celery|celery]], chopped into half-moons\n| 2 [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], any colour, deseeded and chopped\n| 200g [[Basmati rice|basmati rice]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]] or [[Dried mixed herbs|dried mixed herbs]]\n| 2 tablespoons fresh [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], chopped, if available\n| 1 400g tin [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]], chopped\n| 1 tablespoon Worcester [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| [[Chillies]], [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] or [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] - I used 1 teaspoon extra [[Hot chilli powder|hot chilli powder]] and 1 tablespoon Nando's Piri-Piri [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| [[Parsley]], chopped (optional)\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Fill the TM bowl with 1.2kg water and add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]].\n| Place the [[Chicken|chicken]] in the Varoma basket '''30 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 2'''. \n| Turn [[Chicken|chicken]] over and continue cooking for another 30 minutes. \n| Check for done-ness and cook for longer if necessary. \n| Remove the basket and allow to cool, reserving the [[Steaming|steaming]] water and discarding the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Bay leaf|bay leaf]]. \n| Remove the [[Meat|meat]] from the [[bones]]. \n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] to the bowl and chop '''5 seconds / Speed 5''' then scrape down the inside of the bowl. \n| Add the [[Butter|butter]] or [[Oil|oil]], [[Bacon|bacon]], [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Celery|celery]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] and saut\u00e9e '''10 minutes / Temp. Varoma / Speed 1 / MC off'''. \n| Add the [[Rice|rice]] and cook for '''1 minute / Temp. Varoma / Speed 1 / MC off'''. \n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Spices|spices]], [[Herbs|herbs]], Worcester [[Sauce|sauce]], [[Hot pepper sauce|hot pepper sauce]] and [[Chicken|chicken]]. \n| Fill the bowl with the reserved [[Steaming|steaming]] water until you reach the 2 litre mark in the bowl.\n| Cook '''15 minutes  / 90\u00b0  / Speed Spoon / Reverse Blade''' or until the liquid has gone and the [[Rice|rice]] is cooked - it may help to remove the MC for part of the cooking time.\n| Add a little more water if it dries out before the [[Rice|rice]] is done. \n| Serve and garnish with the finely chopped [[Parsley|parsley]] if desired.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* Adapted for [[Thermomix]] from [[User:Chef|Chef's]]'s recipe for [[Chicken jambalaya]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Jambalaya]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #sauce #bayleaf #rice #onion #thermomix #parsley #bacon #garlic #springonions #celery </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chili con carne a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beef #chocolate #onion #tomatoes #rice #vegetables #garlic #simmer #frying #tortillas #dried \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is the recipe my husband and I developed over time and it's very tasty and fairly healthy\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2146\n|PortionCalories = 357\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 hour\n|Image = [[Image:Chilli Con Carne recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Like mama used to make</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.35</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Specially with the chockolate</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is the recipe my husband and I developed over time and it's very tasty and fairly healthy.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500g best mince (ground [[Beef|beef]])\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 1 - 2 [[Garlic|garlic]] cloves\n| [[Extra virgin olive oil|extra virgin olive oil]]\n| [[Vegetables]] as available ([[Mushrooms|mushrooms]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Carrots|carrots]], [[Courgettes|courgettes]], for instance), chopped or sliced\n| 400g can chopped [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 400g can [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]] in unsalted water, drained\n| 1 - 2 [[green chillies]], deseeded and chopped\n| 1 - 2 teaspoons [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] (freshly ground is best)\n| 1 - 2 teaspoons [[Dried|dried]] [[Oregano|oregano]]\n| 1 square of Lindt 85% [[Chocolate|chocolate]], or equivalent dark chocolate: ([[Green & Blacks Organic Chocolate]])\n| 100ml [[Beef|beef]] [[Stock|stock]] (can be made from a cube if necessary)\n| [[Salt]] & [[Pepper]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat a couple of tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]] in a saucepan.  [[Fry]] [[Onion|onion]].  After a few minutes add Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]].  Cover and continue [[Frying|frying]] until [[Onions|onions]] are translucent.\n| Add [[Meat|meat]] and [[Brown|brown]].\n| Add remaining ingredients and seasoning.\n| Bring to [[Boil|boil]].  Lower heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for  30mins to 1 hour, depending on how much you've made.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[Tortillas|tortillas]], [[Rice|rice]] or crusty [[Bread|bread]] and a side [[Salad|salad]].\n\n===Variations===\n\nBy increasing the proportion of [[Beans|beans]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]], one pack of [[Meat|meat]] can be stretched to ten or twelve servings.  If you do this, increase the proportion of [[Herbs|herbs]], [[Spices|spices]] and [[Chocolate|chocolate]] accordingly.  If you don't want to use chocolate (which really is the secret ingredient), you can substitute a little [[White sugar|white sugar]] to bring out the flavour of the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n\nIf you don't like food too spicy, cut down the green [[Chili|chili]] content.  I make it for my young son in this way and he loves it with [[Rice|rice]].\n\n===Chef's tip===\n\nI make a big pot a couple of times a year and each time freeze 15 - 18 double portions that can be microwaved quickly to give us a hot meal in about 15 mins at the end of the working day.  \n\nIf you use low-[[Fat|fat]] [[Beef|beef]], this meal is a healthy option, as it has no other source of [[saturated fat]] apart from the small amount of [[Chocolate|chocolate]].\n\n==See also==\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beef #chocolate #onion #tomatoes #rice #vegetables #garlic #simmer #frying #tortillas #dried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

One of the features of this recipe is the 'just-cooked' [[Garlic|garlic]], added at the last minute.\n\nThis is the recipe for their best selling [[Chili|chili]] - make this famous restaurant chili at home!\n\nThe recipe here has is the version I made to suit my tastes and ingredients available. The original recipe and ingredient quantities can be found in the [[Talk:Chili_con_carne_numero_uno|comments section]].\n''1 cup in this recipe represents 237 ml''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#188; cup of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Freshly [[ground black pepper]]\n| 2 large [[Onions|onions]] peeled and roughly chopped (4 cups)\n| 675 g (1.5 lb) [[Minced beef|minced beef]] (''[[Ground beef|ground beef]]'')\n| 675 g (1.5 lb) [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] (''[[Ground|ground]] pork'')\n| 2 teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 4 heaped tablespoons of unsmoked [[paprika powder]]\n| 2 scant tablespoons fresh [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Toasted|toasted]] and [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| 2 scant tablespoons [[Dried|dried]] [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 2 tablespoons unsweetened [[Cocoa powder|cocoa powder]] (Green & Black's or similar quality product)\n| 1/2 to 1 tablespoons of [[Ground cinnamon|ground cinnamon]] powder\n| 2 teaspoons of [[hot chilli powder]]\n| 1.5 teaspoons of [[chilli flakes]]\n| Good shake of [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]]\n| Good shake of [[lime juice]]\n| 4 cups [[Passata]]\n| 3 cups [[Beef Stock|beef stock]]\n| 8 [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 to 3 tablespoons of coarse [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] for thickening\n| 2 cans [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]]\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chili con carne numero uno and rice.jpg|Chili con carne numero uno, [[homemade tortilla chips]], [[plain rice]], [[soured cream]] and [[orange]] slices\nImage:Chili con carne numero uno ready.jpg|Chili con carne numero uno ready to serve\nImage:The Manhattan chili co dry.jpg|Before the stock and passata\nImage:The Manhattan chili co ingredients.jpg|Chili con carne numero uno, the ingredients\nImage:Manhattan Chili Co - Goodbye.jpg|The Manhattan Chili Co is now closed.\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a [[Wok|wok]] or large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], heat the [[Oil|oil]] and add a grind of black pepper then gently cook the [[Onions|onions]] for 20 minutes until soft - don't [[Brown|brown]] them.\n| Meantime, in a separate pan, add a small amount of the [[Oil|oil]] from the [[Onions|onions]], just to prevent the [[Meat|meat]] from sticking and add the [[Pork|pork]], [[Beef|beef]] and [[salt]]. Cook for 20 minutes also.\n| Drain the meat of any excess fat.\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] to the [[Casserole|casserole]] and mix with the [[Meat|meat]].\n| Stir in the [[Chili powder|chili powder]], [[hot pepper sauce]], [[paprika powder]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Oregano|oregano]], [[Cocoa powder|cocoa powder]] and [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]].  Cook for 5 minutes, stirring often.\n| Add the [[Beef Stock|beef stock]] and [[Tomato juice|tomato juice]], bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce the heat, cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1 hour.\n| Taste and adjust for seasoning and then [[Simmer|simmer]] for a further 30 minutes.\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and thicken with [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] if required. Add the [[Beans|beans]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 5 minutes then serve.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nAs I did not have quite enough [[minced]] [[beef]] and [[minced]] [[pork]], I chopped up a large [[chicken breast]]6 and added that, cooking at the same time as the other meats.\n\nThe Manhattan Chili Co. has now closed, see image above. title": "Chilli cin carne numero uno (sous vide recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Chili con carne numero uno a sous vide beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#leeks #pork #onions #beefstock #passata #cocoapowder #exoticchillipowders #paprikapowder #ground #beans #cumin \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A sous-vide version of The Numero Uno chili recipe from the Manhattan Chili Co Southwest-American Cookbook\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1943\n|PortionCalories = 323\n|DatePublished=30th September 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = The Manhattan Chili Co.\n |Servings = 6 to 8\n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 24 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 24 hours\n |Image = [[Image:The Manhattan chili co logo.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Yuk!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">2</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Keep your ideas to yourself - this is rubbish.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nOk, I had better fess up, this is another of my experiments, documented so it can be easily replicated if it is a success. This recipe is not cooked [[sous-vide]] in the way you would normally.  I don't have a 6 litre sous-vide cooker, I've used my [[home-made sous-vide cooker]] and instead of cooking in a vacuum sealed bag, I've just used the slow cooker with scrunched up baco-foil to provide a better seal.  This could be simply replicated in a slow cooker that has a very accurate temperature setting, should such a thing exist outside of my house!\n\nIf you are luck enough to have a sous-vide cooker that can accomodate 6 litres I would be inclined to premix everything in a bowl first and vacuum seal but manually seal the container before liquid is drawn into the [[vacuum sealer]]. \n\nThe recipe is very similar to the original , The Manhattan Chili Co's famous \u200e[[Chili con carne numero uno]].  The main differences are that I've used [[leeks]] instead of onions and altered the cooking method .\n\n''This was not very successful - the prolonged cooking time make the oregano and cinnamon far too strong - stick to the [[Chili con carne numero uno|original]] - it's far better!''\n\n''1 cup in this recipe represents 237 ml''\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| &#188; cup of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Freshly [[ground black pepper]]\n| 4 large [[leeks]], trimmed and chopped (4 cups)\n| 500 g (1 lb 2 oz) [[Minced beef|minced beef]] (''[[Ground beef|ground beef]]'')\n| 500 g (1lb 2 oz) [[Minced|minced]] [[Pork|pork]] (''[[Ground|ground]] pork'')\n| 2 teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 4 heaped tablespoons of unsmoked [[paprika powder]]\n| 2 scant fresh [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Toasted|toasted]] and [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| 2 scant tablespoons [[Dried|dried]] [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 2 tablespoons unsweetened [[Cocoa powder|cocoa powder]] (Green & Black's or similar quality product)\n| 1 large whole stick of [[cinnamon]] bark to be removed and discarded after cooking\n| 1.5 teaspoons of [[Exotic chilli powders|ancho chilli powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[Exotic chilli powders|chilli chipotle flakes]]\n| Good shake of [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]]\n| Good shake of [[lime juice]]\n| 4 cups [[Passata]] (tomato)\n| 3 cups [[Beef Stock|beef stock]]\n| 8 [[Garlic cloves, peeled and crushed|garlic cloves, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 to 3 tablespoons of coarse [[Yellow cornmeal|yellow cornmeal]] for thickening\n| 2 cans [[Red kidney beans|red kidney beans]], drained\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chili con carne numero uno and rice.jpg|Chili con carne numero uno, [[homemade tortilla chips]], [[plain rice]], [[soured cream]] and [[orange]] slices\nImage:Chili con carne numero uno sous-vide.jpg|Home-made sous-vide cooker (and sous-vide ''bag''!)\nImage:The Manhattan chili co ingredients.jpg|Chili con carne numero uno, the ingredients\nImage:Manhattan Chili Co - Goodbye.jpg|The Manhattan Chili Co is now closed.\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| In a [[Wok|wok]] or large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], heat the [[Oil|oil]] and add a grind of black pepper then gently cook the [[leeks]] for 20 minutes until soft - don't brown them.\n| Meantime, in a separate pan, add a small amount of the [[Oil|oil]] from the [[Onions|onions]], just to prevent the [[Meat|meat]] from sticking and add the [[Pork|pork]], [[Beef|beef]] and [[salt]]. Saute for 10 minutes, draining any liquid after cooking.\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and meat to the [[sous-vide]] or [[slow cooker]].\n| Stir in the [[Chili powder|chili]], [[hot pepper sauce]], [[paprika powder]], [[Cumin|cumin]], [[Oregano|oregano]], [[Cocoa powder|cocoa powder]] and [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]], [[beans]] and crushed [[garlic]], [[Beef Stock|beef stock]] and [[passata]], set the cooker to 65\u00b0 C [149\u00b0 F], seal as best you can and cook for 24 hours.\n| Taste for seasoning and thicken with [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] if required.\n}}\n\n===serving suggestions===\nI'm using this as the basis for [[Frito pie]].\n==See also==\n* The Manhattan Chili Co. has now closed, see image above. Feb 2016. ''The url was www.manhattanchili.com.''\n* [[Chili con carne|Our other chili con carne recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#leeks #pork #onions #beefstock #passata #cocoapowder #exoticchillipowders #paprikapowder #ground #beans #cumin </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

just make sure it's not too wet or you'll get soggy [[tortilla chips]].\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 large pack lightly [[Salted|salted]] [[Tortilla chips|tortilla chips]]\n| 1 560g can of [[Hot dogs|hot dogs]] (large)\n| Splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 2 small white [[Onions|onions]], peeled an finely chopped\n| 4 fresh [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 180g mature [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| Pinch of [[Mixed herbs|mixed herbs]]\n| [[Chilli sauce]] to serve\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add a splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to a large [[Baking tray|baking tray]]\n| Sprinkle with [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Finely chop the [[Onions|onions]] and arrange half in the base of the tray\n| Chop half of the [[Hot dogs|hot dogs]] into small pieces and scatter over the [[Onions|onions]]\n| Roughly chop half of the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and add to the [[Onions|onions]] & [[Hot dogs|hot dogs]]\n| Tip the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] [[Chip|chip]] into the tray and top with the remaining chopped [[Hot dogs|hot dogs]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| Sprinkle with a good pinch of [[Mixed herbs|mixed herbs]] (and [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] if using)\n| Cover with [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| [[Bake]] in the [[Oven|oven]] for about 20 minutes until the [[Cheese|cheese]] is bubbling and the dogs are cooked.\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse canned [[Chilli|chilli]] dogs instead of [[Frankfurters|frankfurters]]\n\n<YouTube>https://youtu.be/QV0O2LQlccg</YouTube>\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #hotdogs #chillisauce #tomatoes #oliveoil #mixedherbs #cheddarcheese #chillidogfritopie #chilli #tortillachips #tortilla </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

gas 6) Grease a 23 cm (9 \") [[baking tray]] with melted [[Butter|butter]] or [[Ghee|ghee]]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large bowl, mix all the ingredients together except for the [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]] kernels.  Continue mixing until you have a smooth, even [[batter]]\n| Drain the [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]], add to the mixture and mix well to combine the kernels\n| Pour into the greased pan and [[Bake|bake]] for about 20 minutes at the top of the oven\n| It should be golden [[Brown|brown]] and springy to the touch\n| Allow to cool for 15 minutes before attempting to cut\n}}\n===Variations===\nFor a hot cheesy [[Cornbread|cornbread]], add 110 g (4 oz) of [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Cheddar]] or [[Monterey Jack|Monterey Jack cheese]] and a big handful of drained, [[pickled jalape\u00f1o chillies]] - yum!\n==See also==\n*[[Quick cornbread]] - 25 minutes from larder to table - from Nik and Edwina's Cookbook\n*[[Cheese and chilli cornbread]] - The perfect combination\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:North African recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sweetcorn #ghee #cornbread #butter #batter #bakingpowder #miseenplace #montereyjack #masaharina #quickcornbread #gumbo </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

But not everyday or my waistline would suffer.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThese corned beef fritters are really easy to make and even easier if you have an [[electric mixer]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tin [[Spam]], cut into 10 mm (1/2\" slices) or thinner\n| [[Oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n}}\n\n'''[[Batter]] mix'''\n* 60 g [[Self-raising flour|self-raising flour]]\n* 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n* Splash of [[Guinness]], [[Bitter|bitter]] or if you must, [[Milk|milk]] and water mixed (about 35 to 40 ml of liquid is required)\n* Splash of [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]] or [[Tabasco sauce]] (to taste)\n* Pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n* A little plain flour to dust before battering.\n\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add all of the dry [[batter]] ingredients to a bowl, then whisking well, add just enough fluid ([[Guinness]], [[Bitter|bitter]], or the [[Milk|milk]]/water mix) to make a thick batter. Add the egg and mix it in extremely well.\n| Rest the batter in the [[refrigerator]] for 20 minutes if you can\n| Dip each piece of spam in a saucer of plain flour and knock off any excess (this helps the batter mix to stick)\n| Dip each piece of spam in the batter \n| Heat a shallow [[Frying pan|frying pan]] with a little [[Oil|oil]]. When it has just started to smoke, reduce the heat a little and [[Fry|fry]] the fritters a few at a time for 3 minutes a side\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Baked beans|baked beans]], [[Chips|chips]] and [[Branston pickle]] or [[OK Sauce]]\n=== Tip ===\n\nTo make it easier to dip the pieces of spam in the batter, use a fork and spear the slice about 1 cm from its end. Have the bowl of batter as close to the frying pan as possible, then dip the Spam and transfer into the hot oil immediately. Slide the fritter off the fork with a knife or other metal implement. '''Do not use your fingers at any point - severe burns can occur!!'''\n\nAlternatively, if you're handy with a pair of chopsticks, you can grip the end of the Spam with them and do the dipping and transferring that way. For me, the only disadvantage of this method is that there is always a 'naked' uncovered bit on the fritter. Forking it is the only way!!!\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with beer]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cornedbeeffritters #guinness #bitter #batter #tabascosauce #electricmixer #branstonpickle #bakedbeans #fry #egg #refrigerator </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Cover and simmer until the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are cooked\n| Remove from the heat and leave to stand for 1 hour\n| Blend about a quarter of the chowder until smooth and mix back into the pan\n| Reheat and serve, garnished with the [[Fried|fried]] [[Bacon|bacon]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nStir in a little [[Double cream|double cream]] for a really luxurious chowder\nAdd [[Smoked fish|smoked fish]], [[Crab|crab]], [[Crayfish|crayfish]], or [[Clams|clams]] for a nice fishy chowder\n[[Chilli flakes]] and chopped [[Pickled|pickled]] jalape\u00f1os as a garnish make a nice spicy chowder \n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bacon #cornchowder #potatoes #fry #fat #doublecream #boil #clams #crayfish #crab #rosemary </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The Panasonic SD 253 and similar models have a 45 minute pizza dough setting that is perfect for tortilla dough.\n| Rest for at least 1 hour then shape into 10 equal sized balls.\n| Using a [[tortilla press]] or [[rolling pin]], place a ball of dough between two non-stick sheets ([[Bake-O-Glide]]or similar) and press into shape\n| Heat a frying pan to a medium high temperature (but with no oil).\n| Cook each tortilla on one side for 15 seconds.\n| Turn and cook for 45 seconds.\n| Turn again and cook for a further 15 seconds.\n| They should have brown speckles.\n}}\n===Serving suggestion===\n\nCan be eaten as they are, fried, wrapped around [[beans]], [[salad]], [[chicken]], [[cheese]] etc.\n\nUse as suggested in your recipe\n*Make [[Cheese pupusas]] or [[Dobladas]] with your homemade [[maize tortillas]]\n===Variations===\n\nAdd 1-2 teaspoons [[chilli powder]] and/or 2-3 teaspoons [[garlic powder]] to the mixture.\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute. title": "Courgette 'spaghetti'",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Courgette 'spaghetti' recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#courgette #courgettes #spaghetti #onions #oliveoil #onion #tomatoes #pasta #tomatosauce #stirfry #sieve \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is based upon Courgette and garlic 'pasta'. Both recipes are an ideal way to use up courgettes. \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 552\n|PortionCalories = 276\n|DatePublished=29th August 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  20 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Courgette spaghetti recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Simples!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Super simples, even!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Sue_spins|Susie]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Zucchini spaghetti in garlic.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Stir-frying the 'pasta' with leeks and garlic]]\n===[[TL;DR]]===\nA recipe for making [[Pasta|pasta]] from a couple of [[Courgettes|courgettes]]!\n\nThis recipe is based upon [[Courgette]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] '[[Pasta|pasta]]'.  Both recipes are an ideal way to use up [[Courgettes|courgettes]].  They are best when about 15 cm (6 in). At this size they still have a lovely shine - once the surface turns matt they should really be treated as [[Marrows|marrows]].\n\nTo shred the [[Courgette|courgette]] ([[Zucchini|zucchini]]) into '[[Spaghetti|spaghetti]]' I found the [[Oxo Good Grips Julienne peeler]] to be the quickest and simplest way.  With the strips of courgette this thin, they can be cooked in a few minutes.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 3 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| big pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 3 or 4 small [[Courgettes|courgettes]], trimmed (topped and tailed)\n| 1 tablespoon fine [[Salt|salt]]\n| 100g [[Jarlsberg]] cheese or your strong cheese of choice\n| 6 tablespoon of good [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] (I've used some of my [[Tomato sauce for pizza]])\n| [[Salt]] to taste\n| Freshly picked [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] to garnish ([[Sungold|sungold]])\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Shred the [[Courgettes|courgettes]] into [[Spaghetti|spaghetti]] with the [[Oxo Good Grips Julienne peeler]]\n| To reduce the water content of the [[Courgette|courgette]], add the strips to a [[Sieve|sieve]] with 1 tablespoon fine [[Salt|salt]] and leave to drain while the [[Onions|onions]] cook. \n| Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to a pan or a [[Wok|wok]] together with a big pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Stir fry|stir fry]] the leeds for 3 or 4 minutes\n| Add the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] and [[Saute|saute]] for no more than a minute, stirring often.\n| Rinse the [[Salted|salted]] [[Courgette|courgette]] [[Spaghetti|spaghetti]] under cold running water and dry in a [[Salad spinner|salad spinner]]\n| Toss the [[Courgette|courgette]] strips into the [[Onions|onions]] and mix well\n| [[Stir fry]] for 3 or 4 minutes - if you like your [[Courgettes|courgettes]] really well cooked, pop a lid on the pan as that helps to [[Steam|steam]] them\n| Heat the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] and spread on the base of the serving plates -  a few seconds in the [[Microwave|microwave]] is an ideal way to do this\n| MIx the [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]] into the cooked '[[Spaghetti|spaghetti]]' toss really well and serve immediately so the cheese melts on the place\n| Garnish with [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] and serve\n}}\n===Variations===\nI used a small [[Leek|leek]] instead of an [[Onion|onion]] as we have plenty at this time of year so it's nice to use as much of our garden produce as we can!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Squash recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#courgette #courgettes #spaghetti #onions #oliveoil #onion #tomatoes #pasta #tomatosauce #stirfry #sieve </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Crab quesadillas recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#crabmeat #tortillas #onions #oliveoil #peppers #culinaryoilspray #mascarponecheese #chillipowder #sweetpepper #cheddarcheese #crabquesadillas \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A quesadilla is a dish in Mexican cuisine where cheese is placed on a cooking wheat or corn flour tortilla and then folded over and cooked until the\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2760\n|PortionCalories = 690\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = Quartered quesadillas\n|Servings = 4 as a main, 6 to 8 as a [[starter]]\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cheese and ham quesadillas recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">This is my Street Food</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Can't find this anywhere, so I have to make it myself - this works well for me.</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nA quesadilla is a dish in Mexican cuisine where [[cheese]] is placed on a cooking [[wheat]] or [[corn flour]] [[tortilla]] and then folded over and cooked until the cheese melts. These would go really well with our  [[Mango salsa]]\n\nQuesadillas are similar to the dish from San Salvador; [[Cheese pupusas|pupusas]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) fresh [[crabmeat]]\n| 1 packet of [[flour]] [[tortillas]] \n| 1 red [[sweet pepper]], cut into thin strips \n| 1 green [[sweet pepper]], cut into thin strips \n| &#189; a [[red onion]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 1 tablespoon [[olive oil]] \n| 225 g (8 oz) [[mascarpone cheese]] \n| A good pinch of [[chilli powder]] \n| Good handful of [[coriander leaves]], finely chopped\n| 1 cup [[grated]] [[cheddar cheese]]\n| [[Culinary oil spray|Cooking oil spray]], I prefer [[olive oil]] for health reasons\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 230 \u00b0C (450 \u00b0F - Gas 8)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[olive oil]] in a [[frying pan]]\n| Add the [[onions]] and [[peppers]] and [[fry]] until the [[onions]] are translucent \n| Meanwhile, into a large bowl, sift the [[crabmeat]] and remove any shell fragments\n| Stir the [[mascarpone cheese]] into the [[crabmeat]], add the [[coriander]] and [[chilli powder]] and mix well \n| Spray half of the [[tortillas]] with [[Culinary oil spray|cooking spray]]. Lay them [[oil]] side down on [[baking]] sheets \n| Add equal portions of the [[crabmeat]] and then [[onions]] and [[peppers]]\n| Sprinkle with the [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| Place the remaining [[tortillas]] on top and spray with cooking spray \n| [[Bake]] for about 10 minutes or until golden [[brown]]\n| Rest for 3 minutes then cut into quarters and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Mango salsa]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#crabmeat #tortillas #onions #oliveoil #peppers #culinaryoilspray #mascarponecheese #chillipowder #sweetpepper #cheddarcheese #crabquesadillas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Gas 6)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Crayfish tails|crayfish tails]], [[Prawns|prawns]], chopped [[Chillies|chillies]] and a splash of [[Black rice vinegar]] to a bowl, mix well to distribute the [[Chillies|chillies]] evenly and leave to marinate for 20 minutes whilst the oven warms.\n| Follow the recipe for the [[Basic flan case]]\n| Add the [[Eggs|eggs]], [[Milk|milk]], [[Flour|flour]], [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]], [[Tabasco sauce]] and seasoning to a bowl\n| With an electric whisk, combine the ingredients so they are well mixed.\n| Blind [[Bake|bake]] the case.\n| Arrange the [[Crayfish tails|crayfish tails]], [[Prawns|prawns]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] in the base of the flan\n| Pour over the [[Egg|egg]] mixture\n| Arrange the sliced [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] on the top and [[Bake|bake]] for a further 30 minutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe warm or cold\n==See also==\n{{Quiche - Add the soft [[Cheese|cheese]] and the [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan]] and cook, stirring, until the cheese has melted.\n| Season to taste and serve with shavings or [[Parmesan I've cheated a little with the filling as I didnt have too much\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1811\n|PortionCalories = 905\n|DatePublished=8th November 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  3 hours, 10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  3 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Creamy tarragon chicken in pumpkin cups recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Best thing is...</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">...no washing up! \ud83e\udd2d</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is an excuse to use up our collection of home-grown [[Pumpkins|pumpkins]] and [[Squashes|squashes]].\n\nI've cheated a little with the 'filling' as I didn't have too much spare time and I've also used the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] to cook the filling for the same reason. It would be fine by just heating the [[Soup|soup]], and mixing in the [[Chicken|chicken]], providing it is properly cooked.  [[Slow cooking]] for a few hours just allows the flavours to properly mingle, providing you have the time. \n\nYou could possibly cook the [[Chicken|chicken]] filling in the [[Squash|squash]] or [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]], but there is always the risk of the body of the squash collapsing and dumping the filling all over your [[Oven|oven]] - this way is far safer!  It's also easier to check that the pumpkin is properly cooked.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 100g [[Bacon lardons|bacon lardons]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 1 small [[Onion|onion]], peeled, halved and chopped\n| 4 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| A pinch of [[Tex-Mex seasoning]] (optional)\n| 2 small [[Chicken breasts|chicken breasts]], chopped into bite-sized pieces\n| 1 can of [[Cream of mushroom soup|cream of mushroom soup]]\n| Splash of [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]] (optional)\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried tarragon|dried tarragon]]\n| 1 medium sized [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] or [[Squash|squash]] (think how it would make 2 small bowls if it were cut in two)\n| 2 tablespoons of Dzuigas [[Cheese|cheese]], finely [[Grated|grated]] (optional)\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pumpkins scooped out and ready to bake.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Pumpkins scooped out and ready to bake\nImage:Tarragon chicken filling.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Sauteed chicken filling\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Add the [[Olive oil|olive oil]], [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and [[Lardons|lardons]] to a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] and [[Saute|saute]] gently for 5 minutes\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and chopped [[Chicken|chicken]] and [[Saute|saute]] for a further 5 minutes, add the [[Garlic|garlic]] for the last few minutes, mixing well\n| Open the [[Soup|soup]] and pour into your [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]], rinse the tin out with a splash of [[Sherry|sherry]] if you have some\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] mix to the [[Soup|soup]] and slow cook for a few hours\n| Meanwhile, carefully cut the [[Squash|squash]] or [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] in half, through the stem.  [[Scoop]] out and discard the [[Seeds|seeds]]\n| [[Bake]] in the [[Oven|oven]] at  , [[Scoop|scoop]] the [[Seeds|seeds]] and bak in the oven at 180\u00b0 C for about an hour - the timing will vary depending upon the type of [[Squash|squash]]\n| If it looks as if the 'soup' might need thickening, stir in a tablespoon of [[yellow cornmeal]] and mix well during the last 15 minutes of cooking.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe the [[Tarragon|tarragon]] [[Chicken|chicken]] directly in the [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]] bowls, each sprinkled with a tablespoon of [[D\u017eiugas cheese]]. \n===Variations===\nUse any form of [[Squash|squash]] or [[Pumpkin|pumpkin]]; [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] would be great, but you would need a large one to serve as a bowl.\n\nA good [[Parmesan cheese]] would be a fair substitute for [[D\u017eiugas cheese]].\n===Chef's notes===\nThis was absolutely delicious and will be made again and again!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:D\u017eiugas cheese recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pumpkin #chicken #squash #soup #blackpepper #seeds #saute #oliveoil #creamytarragonchickeninpumpkincups #scoop #slowcooker </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Crispy baked potatoes stuffed with corn beef hash",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Crispy baked potatoes stuffed with corn beef hash Beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#oliveoil #cornedbeef #potato #crispybakedpotatoesstuffedwithcornbeefhash #cornedbeefhash #tomatoes #bakedpotatoes #onions #potatoes #fry #worcestershiresauce \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is not the Jamie Oliver 30 minutes version. This takes a lot longer, however, if you have the time it is well worth the wait\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1658\n|PortionCalories = 829\n|DatePublished=14th December 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2 pigs!\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  4 hours, 20 minutes\n|PrepTime =  3 hours\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Crispy baked potatoes stuffed with corn beef hash recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Food of the eighties</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Corned beef is food of a time, and for me it's the eighties.  Nice idea though.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nThis is not the Jamie Oliver 30 minutes version.  This takes a lot longer, however, if you have the time it is well worth the wait.  Most of the time is spent waiting, not doing so it's still an easy meal.\n\nYou don't have to [[Baked potatoes|salt the potatoes]] first, its just that this step removed moisture from the skins to make them extra crispy. The [[Salt|salt]] is washed off so does not make them the least bit salty.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 large [[Baking|baking]] [[Potatoes|potatoes]]\n| 1 x 340 g tin of [[Corned beef|corned beef]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Red onion|red onion]], peeled and thinly sliced\n| 2 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]], optional\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n}}\n''' to serve'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 6 medium [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2 large [[Free range eggs|free range eggs]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Salt the Jacket potatoes [[Baked potatoes|as show here]]\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\n[[Image:Skins dehydrated after 3 hours.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Salt the potatoes for 2 or 3 hours then rinse the salt off with cold water. Now the skins are slightly dehydrated - note the water drained from them during this time]]\n[[Image:Tomaotes ready to roast.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Tomatoes, coated with season oil, ready to roast]]\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| ''Ideally for really crispy potatoes, cook them for 1 hour 20 minutes - the 3 hours preparation time includes [[Baked potatoes|salting the potatoes]]''\n| Splash a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a [[Baking tray|baking tray]] and season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Prick the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] a few times to stop them splitting. Add them to the tray and toss them in the seasoned [[Oil|oil]].  We will add these to the [[Oven|oven]] for the final 20 minutes of cooking.\n| If you have [[Baked potatoes|salted the potatoes first]], wash the salt off and pat them dry.\n| Place them on a [[Grill tray|grill tray]] at the top part of a preheated [[Oven|oven]].\n| [[Bake]] for 1 hour.\n| Heat a few tablespoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or a [[Wok|wok]], season with [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] for 7 minutes adding the [[Garlic|garlic]] during the final few minutes.\n| Roughly chop the [[Corned beef|corned beef]] and add to the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a few minutes.\n| Meanwhile, carefully remove the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] from the [[Oven|oven]] and cut into halves. [[Scoop]] out the cooked [[Potato|potato]] and add to the [[Corned beef|corned beef]] with a good splash of [[Worcestershire sauce]].\n| If the hash is not ready, return the [[Potato|potato]] skins to the top of the [[Oven|oven]] to keep them crispy. At the same time, add the tray of [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] to the bottom of the oven.\n| Turn the heat up under the [[Corned beef|corned beef]] and let it crisp for a few minutes, scraping the bottom of the pan to prevent it  sticking.\n| Fill the [[Potato|potato]] skins with the [[Corned beef hash|corned beef hash]] and return to the top of the [[Oven|oven]] for 15 minutes.\n| When the 15 minutes is up, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Eggs|eggs]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe the [[Egg|egg]] on top of the [[Crispy jacket potatoes|crispy jacket potatoes]] filled with [[Corned beef hash|corned beef hash]] with a side order of [[Roasted tomatoes|roasted tomatoes]] and a dollop of [[HP sauce]] - what could be better?.\n===Variations===\nI like quite a 'runny' hash so I added a little [[Stock|stock]], during the last few minutes of the [[Corned beef hash|corned beef hash]] [[Frying|frying]] stage.\n==See also==\n* [[Corned beef hash with eggs]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Australian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oliveoil #cornedbeef #potato #crispybakedpotatoesstuffedwithcornbeefhash #cornedbeefhash #tomatoes #bakedpotatoes #onions #potatoes #fry #worcestershiresauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Curried lamb shanks (slow cooker recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Curried lamb shanks: A slow cooker recipe from Cookipedia\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#onions #lambshanks #slowcooker #currypowder #gravy #beefstock #muscovadosugar #guinness #manhattan #oliveoil #chili \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I was thumbing through some old cookbooks, this recipe jumped out at me from my 1986 \"The Manhattan Chili Co. Southwest American Cookbook\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1095\n|PortionCalories = 547\n|DatePublished=6th April 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = The rescued version of this dish, served as a normal roast dinner!\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 hours, 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Chilied lamb shanks recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Superb</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I wish I could have tried the New York version too.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nOnly this morning we mentioned that we hadn't had [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]] for a while, then this afternoon as I was thumbing through some old cookbooks, this recipe jumped out at me from my 1986 \"The [[Manhattan]] [[Chili]] Co. Southwest American Cookbook.  I have amended it to use a [[slow cooker]] and for once, used commercial [[curry powder]] rather than a homemade blend.\n\n===Update===\nThe ingredients shown below have been much reduced from the original recipe because, to my taste, it was almost bitter.  To rescue the meal, I discarded all of the original gravy and served it with potatoes, carrots, peas and a normal [[onion gravy]].  It still had a little of the curry bite so was not a complete disaster. The lamb shanks were perfectly cooked and delicious.\n\nIf you do make this, taste the gravy and adjust the seasoning before the extended cooking period.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 100 ml [[olive oil]]\n| 2 [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] & [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], peeled and sliced\n| 1 bulb of [[Garlic, peeled and crushed|garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 2 teaspoons of [[curry powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], lightly [[Toasted|toasted]] and finely [[Ground|ground]]\n| 1 teaspoon of [[Dried|dried]] [[Mexican oregano]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[muscovado sugar]]\n| 1 tin peeled [[Plum tomatoes|plum tomatoes]]\n| 330 ml [[Guinness]] (1 bottle)\n| 100 ml [[Beef Stock|beef stock]]\n| ''optional'' - 2 teaspoons [[Exotic chilli powders|mild chilli powder]] (''guajillo'')\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Curried lamb shanks.jpg|300px|thumb|right|After 4 hours slow cooking\nImage:Manhattan Chili Co - Goodbye.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The Manhattan Chili Co is now closed.\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| In a large flameproof [[Casserole|casserole]] or [[Dutch Oven|dutch oven]], heat 100 ml of [[olive oil]], when hot add a good pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and  [[Brown|brown]] the [[Lamb shank|lamb shank]] really well on all sides, this should take around 15 minutes.\n| Sprinkle the [[Lamb shanks|lamb shanks]] with a pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and pop them in the [[slow cooker]].  Discard the used [[Oil|oil]].\n| Return the pan to a low heat, add the remaining [[Oil|oil]] and the [[Garlic|garlic]] and the [[Onions|onions]], cover and saut\u00e9 for 15 minutes stirring now and then.\n| Add the [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]], [[Oregano|oregano]] and [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] uncovered for 5 minutes.\n| Chop the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] with a sharp knife while they are still in the can.\n| Add them to the [[Onions|onions]] together with the [[Guinness]], [[Beef Stock|beef stock]], 1/2 a teaspoon of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]],[[muscovado sugar]] and stir well.\n| Add everything to the slow cooker, set to medium and cook for 5 hours, covered.\n| After 5 hours, remove the lamb shanks and keep warm\n| Test the gravy for seasoning, if you need it hotter, spice it up with your favourite [[chili sauce]].\n| Pour the cooking [[Liquor|liquor]] through a [[Sieve|sieve]] and press out all of the juices, discard the solids.\n| Add the [[Strained|strained]] [[Gravy|gravy]] to the [[Casserole|casserole]] over a high heat and to bring it to the [[Boil|boil]].  For the next 15 minutes, reduce this by one third by stirring, [[Boiling|boiling]] and skimming.\n| Serve the lamb shanks with the hot [[Gravy|gravy]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Rice|rice]] and freshly [[Grilled|grilled]] [[Sweetcorn|sweet corn]].\n===Recipe source===\n* The [[Manhattan]] [[Chili]] Co. Southwest American Cookbook\n* The Manhattan Chili Co. has now closed, see image above. Feb 2016. The url was www.manhattanchili.com.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with beer]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#onions #lambshanks #slowcooker #currypowder #gravy #beefstock #muscovadosugar #guinness #manhattan #oliveoil #chili </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Quite a good recipe to try if you want to impress.  With a side-salad it will easily serve 4 people.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 200 g [[pepperoni]]-style sausage, peel off the skin and thinly slice the sausage. [[Chorizo]] works equally well in this recipe\n| 1 portion of [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]]\n| [[Fine yellow cornmeal|Fine yellow cornmeal]] or [[plain flour]] for dusting .''Students, you can get by without this!''\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[Cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 1 large can of chopped peeled [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], left to drain over a coarse sieve for 20 minutes\n| 1 teaspoon [[dried oregano]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[dried oregano]] or [[mixed herbs]]\n| Pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 1 ball of [[Buffalo|buffalo]] [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]], torn\n}}\n\n===How to ensure a crispy base===\nHaving made these deep pan pizzas many, many times, I've found that sometimes it's hard to get the base well cooked without burning the rest of the [[pizza dough]].  I've found the best way is to use a meta-based pan, similar to a baking tray.  The metal base gets hot enough to crisp the base properly.  I have a really heavy rectangular Le Creuset baking tray that is absolutely ideal.  It seems a shame as it will mean I'll never use my earthenware deep pan pizza dish again!\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Deep pan pepperoni pizza pie.jpg|Ready to eat\nImage:Deep pan pepperoni pizza pie topped.jpg|Topped with mozzarella and tomatoes\nImage:Deep pan pepperoni pizza pie filled.jpg|Pepperoni & cheddar\nImage:Easy tomato topping for pizza recipe.jpg|[[Drained tomato topping]]\n</gallery>\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5), [fan oven 170\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n* Make the [[Dough|dough]] as instructed\n* [[Easy tomato topping for pizza|Drain the canned tomatoes]]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Easy tomato topping for pizza|Drain the canned tomatoes]], add the herbs and season with salt and pepper\n| [[Spray]] or oil a deep pan pizza dish or a small oven tray\n| Roll out 2/3rds of the [[Dough|dough]] to about 3mm and line a pan so the [[Dough|dough]] just  overlaps the edges and trim any excess.\n| ''Students: a wine bottle, beer bottle or even beer-can makes a good substitute for a [[rolling pin]]!''\n| Sprinkle the base with the [[Cheddar cheese]] and the sliced [[pepperoni]]\n| Roll out the remaining [[Dough|dough]] to make a lid\n| Wet the edge of the dough so you can make a good seal\n| Pinch the lid on and roll the edge over so it joins the base\n| This time I'm not making any holes in the lid so it should puff up - might be fun!\n| Top with the torn [[mozzarella]] and then dab on the tomato topping\n| If you have enough spare time leave in a [[warm place]] for an hour or so to let it rise first. \n| [[Bake]] for 45 minutes, resting a sheet of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] on top of the [[Pizza|pizza]] towards the end if it looks as though it might start to burn.\n| Allow to cool for 5 minutes before slicing and serving\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Variations===\nAdd whatever you fancy, just don't add too much topping or let it get too wet of it could end up rather soggy.\n\nFinely grated [[parmesan cheese]] sprinkled on the top gives a nice toasty crust.\n==See also==\n* [[Chicago deep pan pizza]]\n* www.ibelieveicanfry.com/2012/01/chicago-stuffed-pizza.html Julia's Chicago pizza recipe\n* [[:Category:I believe I can fry recipes|Julia's recipes on Cookipedia]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Student recipes|Pizza]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes|Pizza]]\n[[Category:I believe I can fry recipes|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites|Pizza]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted|Pizza]]\n\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#deeppanpepperonipizzapie #dough #pepperoni #driedoregano #mozzarella #cheddarcheese #pizzadough #parmesancheese #tomatoes #grated #warmplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

One of my favourite recipes.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nJulia, the author of the [[Category:I believe I can fry recipes|I believe I can fry]] recipe blog always publishes interesting and original recipes and this is no exception.  The salmon is livened up by using a spicy rub and then sealed in [[mayonnaise]] before is is oven baked, so all the moisture is retained.  It's then grilled to get a nice finish.\n\nWe regularly have [[Salmon|salmon]] and this may possibly be our recipe of choice.\n\nThanks to Julia for giving us permission to publish this recipe.  www.ibelieveicanfry.com/ Do take a look at her blog, it is a must for foodies.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Salmon steaks|salmon steaks]] - ( 1 per person )\n}}\n'''spicy rub'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &#189; teaspoon fine [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| &#188; teaspoon of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| &#188; teaspoon of [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]] \n| &#188; teaspoon of unsmoked [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &#188; teaspoon of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| &#188; teaspoon of [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n}}\n'''coating'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4 tablespoons of Hellmann's [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour] while you prepare the [[Salmon|salmon]]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place the [[Salmon fillets|salmon fillets]] skin-side down on a sheet of [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]]\n| Add the rub ingredients to a small bowl and mix well\n| Sprinkle the rub over the top surface of the [[Salmon|salmon]], reserving a little to finish\n| Cover the [[Salmon|salmon]] [[Steak|steak]] with a thin layer of [[Mayonnaise|mayonnaise]]\n| Finish off with a sprinkle of the rub\n| Leaving the [[Salmon|salmon]] on the [[Greaseproof paper|greaseproof paper]], cover with a tent of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]], being careful not to let the [[Foil|foil]] touch the [[Salmon|salmon]]\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes in the middle of the [[Oven|oven]].\n| When there is 5 minutes left, preheat the [[Grill|grill]]\n| After 20 minutes, finish under the [[Grill|grill]] for a few minutes\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Salmon after grilling on Bake-O-Glide.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Salmon after grilling on [[Bake-O-Glide]]\nImage:Salmon covered with a thin layer of mayo.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Topped with a thin layer of mayonnaise\n</gallery>\n===Recipe source===\n* Julia's recipe\n** www.ibelieveicanfry.com/2014/06/easy-oven-baked-salmon.html\n* and the recipe that inspired hers\n**http://natashaskitchen.com/2013/10/02/baked-salmon-with-a-tangy-glaze/\n===Variations===\nYou can add a squeeze of [[Lemon|lemon]] and a pinch of [[Lemon zest|lemon zest]] to the top of the [[Salmon|salmon]] fillet, before you sprinkle the rub.\n===Chef's note===\nUse [[Bake-O-Glide]] instead of [[greaseproof paper]], if you have it.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish Posner Belgian Waffle Maker]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 250 g (1 cup) of cooked [[Potato|potato]] ([[Boiled|boiled]])\n| Spray of [[Olive oil]]\n| Pinch of [[salt]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Using a [[Spray|spray]] or an [[Oil|oil]]ed kitchen paper, coat both surfaces of the [[Waffle iron|waffle iron]] with a very thin film of [[Oil|oil]] before switching on the [[Iron|iron]].\n* Turn on the [[Waffle iron|waffle iron]] and allow to get to temperature (normally the green light comes on)\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| If the [[Potatoes|potatoes]] are very wet, press them into a [[Sieve|sieve]] to release any excess water.  This is especially necessary if using  [[Defrosted|defrosted]] [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Boiled potatoes|boiled potatoes]].\n| Add a pinch of salt to the potato mix\n| Place the cooked [[Boiled|boiled]] [[Potato|potato]] in the centre of the [[Iron|iron]] and close firmly to squish the [[Potato|potato]] evenly over the [[Iron|iron]].\n| Cook for 15 to 18 minutes or until golden and crispy.\n}}\n===Variations===\nDrop a knob of [[Butter|butter]] onto the top of the waffle for the last few minutes of cooking.\n\n===Chef's notes===\nFrom the experiments I have carried out, mashing the potatoes beforehand is not necessary and actually makes more of a mess, especially if the mix is rather liquid.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#waffleiron #iron #potato #boiledpotatoes #griddled #homemadehummus #barbecued #sieve #potatoes #defrosted #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The McDonalds 'Egg\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1712\n|PortionCalories = 428\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 1\n |TotalTime = 10 minutes\n |PrepTime = 5 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Eggs Benedict recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nuffingk, muffingk</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.9</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I would rather have this than an Egg Mc Muffin!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Eggs Benedict''' is a dish that consists of a half of an [[English muffin]], topped with [[Ham|ham]] or [[Bacon|bacon]], [[Poached eggs|poached eggs]], and [[Hollandaise sauce|hollandaise sauce]].\n\nThe McDonalds '[[Egg]] McMuffin' was developed as the ''poor man's'' eggs Benedict by Herb Peterson in 197\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 [[English muffins]], halved, [[Toasted|toasted]] and buttered\n| 4 slices of [[Pancetta|pancetta]] or cooked [[Home smoked bacon|home smoked bacon]], warmed.\n| 4 [[Poached eggs|poached eggs]]\n| &frac12; title": "Eight hour smoky pulled pork in Guinness",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
