                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Eight hour smoky pulled pork in Guinness an Irish recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#eighthoursmokypulledporkinguinness #roastingtray #pittabread #porkshoulder #marinade #coleslaw #muscovadosugar #marinading #bayleaves #juice #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This version of pulled pork is loosely based on the 'Eight hour smokey pulled pork shoulder' recipe from The Fabulous Baker Brothers\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 6128\n|PortionCalories = 1021\n|DatePublished=28th July 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6 \n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  20 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  12 hours 15 minutes\n|CookTime =  8 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Eight hour smoky Guinness pulled pork recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Worthy of the wait</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fabulous, if you have the time and the patience.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nThis version of [[Pulled pork|pulled pork]] is loosely based on the 'Eight hour smokey pulled pork shoulder' recipe from The Fabulous Baker Brothers. #<small>see [[Talk:Eight hour smoky pulled pork in Guinness|talk page]]</small>\n\n[[Marinading]] the [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]] overnight makes a huge difference so you need to plan ahead when making this.\n\nServe with [[Coleslaw]], pickles and [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]].  It's also great in sandwiches\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2.2kg [[Pork shoulder]] joint\n| 100 ml [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 100 ml [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n| 30g [[Smoked paprika|smoked paprika]] or a mixture of normal and [[Smoked|smoked]] [[Paprika|paprika]]\n| 1 bunch of [[Thyme|thyme]]\n| A few [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]]\n| 300 ml of Guinness original (small bottle)\n| 1 bulb of [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| [[Juice]] and [[Zest|zest]] from 1 [[Lemon|lemon]]\n| A tablespoon of [[Muscovado sugar|muscovado sugar]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n*Cut a criss-cross of slashes in the skin with a very sharp knife such as a Stanley knife.  The skin won't go crispy but it helps to keep the [[Meat|meat]] moist and the slashes let the [[Marinade|marinade]] through. I normally leave the lemon skins in while it marinades and also whilst it cooks.\n*Place the joint in a large tray, pour the [[Marinade|marinade]] over and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] overnight, '[[Basting|basting]]' now and then.\n*Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to maximum heat\n*Mix all of the ingredients together and\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Cover the [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]] with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]], sealing the edges.  Ensure that the roasting tray is very well sealed or the joint is likely to dry out after 8 hours cooking. #<small>see [[Talk:Eight hour smoky pulled pork in Guinness|talk page]]</small>\n| Place in the [[Oven|oven]] and immediately turn the heat down to 140\u00b0 C (257\u00b0 F - gas 1)\n| Cook for 8 hours\n| Decant the joint to another [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]], shred whatever [[Meat|meat]] you are going to consume immediately, store the remaining [[Meat|meat]] in a [[Lock and Lock]] style box and refrigerate for later use. This way it will stays moist and fresh.\n| Using a [[Fat strainer|fat strainer]] separate most of the excess fat from the cooking juices and discard. Add the cooking juices back to the roasting tray and heat up over the hob. Mix in the [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Meat|meat]], stir well to mix then transfer to a serving dish.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Eight hour smoky Guinness pulled pork_overnight.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to refrigerate overnight\nImage:Eight hour smoky Guinness pulled pork_ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Eight hour smoky Guinness pulled pork, the ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]], [[Pickles|pickles]] and [[Cole slaw|cole slaw]].\n===Chef's notes===\nA can of drained [[kidney beans]] or virtually any pulses added at the start of the cooking process make this recipe stretch even firther.\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Irish recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#eighthoursmokypulledporkinguinness #roastingtray #pittabread #porkshoulder #marinade #coleslaw #muscovadosugar #marinading #bayleaves #juice #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Enfrijoladas recipe",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Enfrijoladas recipe Cheese, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#enfrijoladasrecipe #chorizo #garlicoliveoil #tortilla #grapefruitsalsa #corntortillas #tortillas #refriedbeans #sourcream #montereyjack #cheddarcheese \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Enfrijoladas is a Tex-Mex dish that is similar to enchiladas\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3828\n|PortionCalories = 957\n|DatePublished=2nd April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|ImageComment = Covered with melted [[Emmental]]\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 5 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 50 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Enfrijoladas recipe 2.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tex Max at home</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was easy to make and tasted fabulous - thank you!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nEnfrijoladas is a [[Tex-Mex]] dish that is similar to [[enchiladas]].  The [[tortillas]] are slightly [[fried]] and filled with [[frijoles refritos]] ([[refried beans]]) and [[pork]], or in this recipe spicy [[chorizo]].  I cheated with the refried beans as I didn't have time to soak them so I used canned, which are ok if but a little too salty.  I used [[Emmental cheese]], which is not authentic but I though it would work well. It did. This dish was a huge success.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 8 [[corn tortillas]]\n| 2 cans refried beans (or [[Refried beans recipe|homemade refried beans]])\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[grated]] [[Emmenthal cheese]], [[Monterey Jack]] or [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| 1/2 a small jar of [[Jalape\u00f1os|pickled jalape\u00f1os chillies]] or to taste\n| 150 ml to 200 ml (1/4 pint +) of [[beef stock|beef]] or [[vegetable stock]] \n| 120 g (4 oz) or a packet of spicy [[chorizo]], sliced\n| A handful of fresh [[coriander]], chopped\n| 8 tablespoons [[sour cream]]\n| [[Garlic olive oil]] for frying the [[corn tortillas]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4)\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a frying pan heat a few drops of [[garlic olive oil]] and fry each [[tortilla]] for a minute or so a side.\n| So you don't use too much oil, turn the first one over after a minute, put the next uncooked one on top of this to soak a little of the oil, flip them both. Remove the cooked one and repeat until they are all done. Add a few more drops of olive oil if the pan is too dry.\n| Divide the [[chorizo]] the cold contents of one cans of [[refried beans]] and layer each [[tortilla]] with an equal share as in the photo.\n| Lay them in an ovenproof dish\n| Heat the remaining tin of beans and add enough [[stock]] to make them ''pourable''. This way the bean ''sauce'' can get between the tortillas. Stir in the [[pickled jalape\u00f1os]]\n| Pour the bean mixture between the [[tortillas]], add a drizzle of [[garlic olive oil]] over the top and cover with the grated cheese\n| Bake in the over for 30 minutes and finish under the grill if you like your cheese toasty\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Enfrijoladas recipe 1.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Fill each tortilla with chorizo and refried beans\nImage:Grapefruit salsa.jpg|thumb|300px|right|[[Grapefruit salsa]]\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nGarnish with a dollop of [[sour cream]] on top and a sprinkle of coriander.\n\nDon your big hat and serve with a [[grapefruit salsa]] or [[curtido]] and a glass of ice-cold San Miguel!\n\n''The Mexican way: A tip from one of our Mexican visitors'' - You can also fill your enfrijoladas with shredded chicken and sprinkle some chopped or thinly sliced onion on top.  \n\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#enfrijoladasrecipe #chorizo #garlicoliveoil #tortilla #grapefruitsalsa #corntortillas #tortillas #refriedbeans #sourcream #montereyjack #cheddarcheese </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

Its name comes from the common use of \"Marshmallow Fluff\" brand marshmallow creme. Rather good I thought!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Remember the greaseproof.jpg|thumb|right|300px|Twice now, I've forgotten to put [[greaseproof paper]] under the baking beans.  Perhaps this picture will remind me next time!]]\nThis in now becoming an obsession - I'm now up to two a day (making quiches, not eating them!)\n\nI love Frankfurters and quiches, so I thought I would combine the two.\n\nThe quantity used makes two quiches, but you could obviously halve the amounts if you only wanted to make one.\n\nI guess the obvious thing to include would be [[Mustard|mustard]], but I wasn't too sure about that so used my favourite instead - [[Louisiana Hot Pepper Sauce|Louisiana hot pepper sauce]] - use [[Tabasco sauce]] if you wish.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb 2 oz) pack of [[ready made shortcrust pastry]]\n| 350 g [[Frankfurters]] 1 pack, 10 in my packet\n| 6 [[Free range eggs|free range eggs]]\n| 6 tablespoons of [[Greek-style yogurt]]\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Mascarpone cheese|mascarpone cheese]]\n| Splash of [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon of freshly chopped [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| Grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| Splash of [[Milk|milk]]\n| 2 large [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], sliced\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - Gas 6) \n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Roll the pastry out into two circles to fit your flan trays. [[Push-out flan dishes]] are the best for this I find (as long as your pastry doesn't leak)\n| Blind [[Bake|bake]] the pastry for 10 minutes\n| Add the [[Eggs|eggs]], [[Cheese|cheese]], [[Yogurt|yogurt]] and a splash of [[Milk|milk]] to a bowl, season with [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and your hot [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| Whisk up the mixture so the [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Yogurt|yogurt]] is well combined\n| Cut the [[Frankfurters]] in half and arrange in the dishes\n| Sprinkle the [[Parsley|parsley]] into the mixture\n| Divide the [[Egg|egg]] mixture between the two trays and top with sliced tomatoes\n| Reduce the heat of the oven to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - Gas 4)\n| [[Bake]] for a further 40 minutes, leaving a little head-room as they tend to rise a bit - like a souffle\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot or cold\n\n{{Quiche - See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#frankfurterquiche #cheese #parsley #yogurt #frankfurters #bake #miseenplace #tabascosauce #mascarponecheese #freerangeeggs #sauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Frito pie a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fritopie #cheese #onion #beef #sourcream #chili #tacoseasoning #tomatoes #grated #orange #cheesenachos \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A Frito pie typically consists of a small single-serving bag of Fritos (plain corn chips / tortilla chips), with a cup of chili poured over the top\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4148\n|PortionCalories = 1037\n|DatePublished=20th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 30 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Frito pie recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Sometimes, the simple things are the best.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This is one of those times!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nA Frito pie typically consists of a small single-serving bag of Fritos (plain [[corn]] [[chips]] / [[tortilla chips]]), with a cup of [[chili]] poured over the top, usually finished up with [[grated]] [[cheese]] or [[onions]] and jalape\u00f1os and [[sour cream]]. Frito pies are popular in the Southwestern United States. \n\nThis dish is similar to [[Cheese nachos]] and the original [[Easy frito pie]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 150 g Fritos or other [[Tortilla chips|corn (maize) chips]]\n| &frac34; cup (175 ml) chopped [[onion]]\n| 2 [[tomatoes]], chopped\n| 1 cup (240 ml) [[grated]] [[cheddar cheese]]\n| 1 pound of ground [[beef]]\n| [[taco seasoning]]\n| 2&frac12; cups (590 ml) chili (homemade or canned)\n| 125 ml carton of [[sour cream]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Brown]] the ground [[beef]] and season according to [[taco seasoning]] mix.\n| Preheat oven to 350\u00b0 F (175\u00b0 C).\n| Spread 2 cups of Fritos in a [[baking]] dish.\n| Sprinkle half the [[onion]] , half the [[cheese]] and the chopped [[tomatoes]] over the Fritos.\n| Combine ground [[beef]] with the [[chili]] and pour over the [[onion]] and [[cheese]].\n| Sprinkle the remaining Fritos, [[onion]] and [[cheese]] over the [[chili]].\n| [[Bake]] for 15 or 20 minutes and [[cheese]] is bubbly.\n| Serve hot, garnish with [[sour cream]].\n}}\n===Variations===\n\nSee [[Easy frito pie|Quick and easy frito pie]]\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nScatter a handful of [[Jalape\u00f1os|pickled jalape\u00f1os]] over the top of the [[tortillas|tortilla chips]] before baking.\n\nAn [[orange]] cut into thin segments (skin on) and baked separately makes an nice refreshing accompaniment to this dish.\n\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pies tarts and flans]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fritopie #cheese #onion #beef #sourcream #chili #tacoseasoning #tomatoes #grated #orange #cheesenachos </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Best made with home-made dough too.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Garlic and crayfish pizza_ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Garlic and crayfish pizza, ready to bake]]\nA delicious excuse for pizza gluttony, again.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 portion of [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]]\n| 5 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 5 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 180g prepared [[Crayfish tails|crayfish tails]] [crawfish tails]\n| 2 x 150 g balls of [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]]\n| 30 g [[Pecorino cheese|pecorino cheese]] or [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Make the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] as instructed\n* If using a [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]], preheat the [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] under a very hot [[Grill|grill]] for about 20 minutes. Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Make 1 [[Pizza|pizza]] per person\n| Crush the [[Garlic|garlic]] and add it to the [[Crayfish tails|crayfish tails]] together with 4 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]].  Mix well and let the flavours mingle while the [[Dough|dough]] is pepared.\n| Dust the work surface with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| Stretch or roll the [[Dough|dough]] into two thin rounds\n| Sprinkle the stone with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| Pre-cook the empty [[Pizza|pizza]] base on one side only for about 3 minutes or until it is lightly [[Browned|browned]]\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]], flip and add the topping.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] one side of the [[Pizza|pizza]] and [[Grill|grill]], oiled side down, flip and repeat, about 2 minutes per side\n| Tear the [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]] into pieces and scatter over the [[Pizza|pizza]].\n| Add the [[Crayfish tails|crayfish tails]], garlic and [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and a grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n| Top with the [[Grated|grated]] [[Pecorino|pecorino]] or [[Parmesan|parmesan]] and top with a drizzle of [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| [[Bake]] for 3 or 4 minutes or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] browns a little - watch it carefully as it can burn easily.\n| Keep the fist [[Pizza|pizza]] warm at the bottom of the [[Oven|oven]] whilst you make the second.\n| Serve hot\n}}\n===Variations===\nI chopped up a small [[Roasted red pepper|roasted red pepper]] and added to this as I had one spare.\n\nSplit a [[green Indian chilli]] down the middle and saut\u00e9 it with the onions and garlic and leave it with the prawns while they marinade.  Remove and discard before making the pizza.\n\nLeave the prawn , onions and garlic to [[marinade]] for a few hours if you have the time.\n==See also==\n{{Template:Crayfish recipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Freshwater fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#garlicandcrayfishpizza #pizza #oliveoil #crayfishtails #pizzastone #pizzadough #dough #grill #fineyellowcornmeal #pecorinocheese #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

They are [[Baked|baked]] rather than [[Fried|fried]] so are possibly slightly healthy!\n\nThe recipe idea and the pictures come by courtesy of '[[I believe I can fry]]' and this was the first recipe I chose from her collection after she gave us permission to share her ideas.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 Russet [[Potatoes|potatoes]], peeled and cut into thin fries\n| A good splash of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Rosemary leaves|rosemary leaves]], finely chopped.\n| The original recipe specified [[Dried|dried]] [[Rosemary|rosemary]], I tend to use fresh rosemary as I have so much of it.  In a recipe like this it probably doesn't hurt to throw a few [[Rosemary#Sprigs of rosemary|sprigs]] onto the [[Baking tray|baking tray]] just for the aroma, Jamie Oliver style.\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| [[Black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8), [fan oven 210\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n* Soak the thin cut fries in cold water for 10 minutes\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rinse and drain the chipped fries and pat dry on paper towels.\n| Add the [[Rosemary leaves|rosemary leaves]] and [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]] to the [[Oil|oil]] and mix well, a [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] will bring out the flavour of fresh [[Rosemary|rosemary]] leaves.\n| Add the [[Oil|oil]] and [[Potatoes|potatoes]] to a large [[Lock & Lock|lock & lock]]-style box, close the lid and shake well to coat the fries.\n| Spread the fries evenly on a [[Foil|foil]]-lined [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]].\n| [[Bake]] for 30 minutes turning a few times.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe immediately, seasoned with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Potato recipes]]\n[[Category:I believe I can fry recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#rosemary #garlicandrosemarythinbakedfries #blackpepper #garlicpowder #rosemaryleaves #potatoes #garlic #snack #unusualrecipes #dried #foil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Reading one of Ken Homs early cookbooks gave me the impetus to try\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1765\n|PortionCalories = 882\n|DatePublished=8th March 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = An unusual accompaniment of garlic mushrooms and grilled tomatoes\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  3 hours, 18 minutes\n|PrepTime =  3 hours, 10 minutes\n|CookTime =  8 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Garlic fried chicken with a masa harina crust.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Air frying is nicer</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A few years ago this would have been great, but now I can get the same results using an air-fryer and a spray of olive oil.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n\nIt is years since I [[deep-fried]] anything so this is almost new territory for me.  Reading one of Ken Hom's early cookbooks gave me the impetus to try it again.  I'm glad I did, it was really good and not at all greasy.\n\nThis is really an aide-memoir for me; next time I would add a tablespoon of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]] for a bit more [[Spice|spice]], and I would also hammer the [[Chicken|chicken]] flat before slicing up.  This would enable less [[Oil|oil]] to be used (not so wasteful), and it would also give a shorter, more uniform cooking time. As it was, we had to cook all of the chicken pieces a little longer to be sure the largest pieces were properly cooked.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 400g small [[Chicken|chicken]] fillets\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Shaoxing rice wine|shaoxing rice wine]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]] - [[Balsamic vinegar|balsamic vinegar]] will be fine \n| 3 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| A pinch of [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 2 [[Egg whites|egg whites]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 1 [[Cup|cup]] [[Masa Harina|masa harina]]\n| 1 to 2 cups [[Sunflower oil|sunflower oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Cut the [[Chicken|chicken]] fillets into bite-sized pieces\n* Add to a [[Lock & Lock box]] together with the [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]], [[Rice|rice]] [[Wine vinegar|wine vinegar]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Black pepper|black pepper]].\n* Shake well to mix and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for an hour or more to allow the [[Marinade|marinade]] to penetrate the [[Meat|meat]].\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Garlic fried chicken with a masa harina crust frying.jpg|Frying in a wok\nImage:Chicken coated with masa.jpg|Coated with masa harina after the egg-white and cornflour stage\nImage:Garlic fried chicken marinading.jpg|Marinade for an hour or more\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in a [[Colander|colander]] and discard the [[Marinade|marinade]] juices.\n| Whisk the [[Egg whites|egg whites]] and [[Cornflour|cornflour]] in a bowl.\n| Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces to the bowl and mix well. [[Refrigerate]] for 30 minutes.\n| Add the [[Cup|cup]] of [[Masa Harina|masa harina]] to a dry [[Lock and Lock box]], close the lid and shake hard to coat the [[Chicken|chicken]].\n| Heat a [[Wok|wok]] or [[Frying pan|frying pan]] with enough [[Oil|oil]] to just cover the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces.\n| Heat to 176\u00b0 C [350\u00b0 F] (a 2.5cm [1\"] cube of [[Bread|bread]] should [[Brown|brown]] in 60 seconds.\n| [[Fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces in 2 batches for about 4 minutes each batch.  Cut one of the largest pieces open to check that it is properly cooked.\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n[[Chips]] and [[Salad|salad]] is probably the most usual [[Accompaniment|accompaniment]] for this.  We had this with an unusual, but fantastic combination; [[Stuffed mushrooms with garlic and Parmesan|garlic mushrooms]] and [[Grilled|grilled]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #garlicfriedchickenwithamasaharinacrust #eggwhites #blackpepper #marinade #cornflour #refrigerate #cup #lemonjuice #masaharina #accompaniment </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "General Tso's chicken",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=General Tso's chicken Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#generaltsoschicken #chicken #wok #springonions #cornflour #sauce #deepfrying #egg #darksoysauce #chilipeppers #kungpochicken \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=General Tso's chicken is a sweet and spicy deep-fried chicken dish that is popularly served in American and Canadian Chinese restaurants where it is\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1201\n|PortionCalories = 300\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:General Tso's chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Complex</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">but was probably worth the effort in the long run.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n'''General Tso's chicken''' is a sweet and spicy [[Deep-fried|deep-fried]] chicken dish that is popularly served in American and Canadian Chinese restaurants where it is erroneously considered Hunan cuisine. The origins of the dish are unclear. The dish was previously largely unknown in China and other lands home to the Chinese. Thus, General Tso's [[Chicken]] is most likely an American invention in the history of American-Chinese food.\n\nThe association with General Tso, or Zuo Zongtang, a Qing dynasty general and statesman, is unclear. The dish is atypical of Hunanese cuisine, which is traditionally very spicy and rarely sweet. Instead, the dish is believed to have been introduced to New York City in the early 1970s as an example of Hunan and Szechuan-style cooking.\n\nThe dish was first mentioned in The New York Times in 1977. It has many similarities to [[Kung Po chicken]].\n\nPeng Chang-kuei, the 98 year old chef who created the much-loved Chinese dish General Tso's Chicken died on 4th December 2016 in Taipei, the capital of Taiwan.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g (1 lb) boneless [[Chicken|chicken]] thighs cut into 2.5 cm (1\") cubes\n| 1 tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 beaten [[Egg|egg]]\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]], to taste\n| 3 tablespoons of [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n}}\n'''>[[Sauce]]:'''\n* 2 tablespoons [[Dark soy sauce|dark soy sauce]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Black rice vinegar|black rice vinegar]]\n* 2 teaspoons Chinese [[Rice wine|rice wine]] or [[Dry sherry|dry sherry]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n* 3 tablespoons [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] or water\n* 1 tablespoon minced [[Garlic|garlic]]\n* 1 tablespoon [[Minced|minced]] [[Ginger|ginger]]\n* 1 teaspoon [[Cornflour|cornflour]] for thickening\n'''>[[Stir-fry]]'''\n* 3 [[Spring onions|spring onions]], [[Chopped on the diagonal|chopped on the diagonal]]\n* 6 [[Dried|dried]] red birds' eye [[Chili peppers|chili peppers]] or to taste\n**[[Peanut]] or [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] for [[Stir-frying|stir-frying]] and [[Deep frying|deep frying]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Egg|egg]], [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Cornflour|cornflour]] to make a thin [[Batter|batter]] and coat the [[Chicken|chicken]] cubes. Set aside.\n| Add the [[Sauce|sauce]] ingredients to a bowl and mix well.  Leave for 10 minutes so the [[Sugar|sugar]] dissolves and re-mix.  Set aside.\n| In a [[Wok|wok]], heat the [[Oil|oil]] for [[Deep frying|deep frying]] [180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F)]\n| A few pieces at a time so the [[Oil|oil]] stays hot, [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces for 3 or 4 minutes until crispy.\n| In a separate [[Wok|wok]], heat 2 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]], add the chilles and [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for 40 seconds so the oil is flavoured.  Don't burn or [[Brown|brown]] the [[Onions|onions]].\n| Add all of the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces to the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] and [[Chillies|chillies]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]], shimmying the [[Wok|wok]], for a few minutes to the chicken takes some colour.\n| Stir the [[Sauce|sauce]] well, slide the [[Chicken|chicken]] to one side of the [[Wok|wok]], add the  sauce to the  middle of the wok and mix well to thicken.  Shimmy the wok to coat the chicken pieces with the sauce and serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Egg noodles|egg noodles]] and [[Steamed|steamed]] [[Broccoli|broccoli]].  A nice, healthy alternative to egg noodles might be brown rice as I've found it to be a lovely pairing with the other ingredients.\n===Variations===\nSprinkle with [[Dry-fried|dry-fried]] [[Cashew nuts|cashew nuts]].\n===See also ===\n*[http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-38181144 General Tso's Chicken creator dies in Taiwan aged 98 ''BBC'']\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Deep fried]]\n[[Category:Stir fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#generaltsoschicken #chicken #wok #springonions #cornflour #sauce #deepfrying #egg #darksoysauce #chilipeppers #kungpochicken </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Gluten free cheese sauce.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Space a velvety, creamy sauce without the use of flour.\n\nI've used [[Black bomber cheese|black bomber cheese]] but any mature (sharp) [[cheese]] would be equally good.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 160g [[Milk]]\n| [[Sodium citrate]] 6.5g\n| 170g [[Black bomber cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Combine the [[Milk|milk]] and [[Sodium citrate|sodium citrate]] in a an immersion [[Blender|blender]] every time until you have a silky smooth [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| Simmer for a few minutes, stirring all the while, until the sauce thickens a little.\n}}\n===Recipe title": "Griddle pan waffles",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Griddle pan waffles, Egg recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#butter #griddlepanwaffles #buttermilk #banana #freerangeeggs #hand #fetacheese #avocado #wafflemaker #chocolatesauce #pancake \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Sam Hardacre one of The Marketing Lab's array of Geek Brains, brought this rather clever idea to my attention\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1894\n|PortionCalories = 473\n|DatePublished=3rd January 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Sam has cleverly used a small pan to neatly constrain the waffle\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  35 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Griddle pan waffles recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Thanks Sam!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Hi Sam (& Louisa).  You are now, but a very distant memory, but your griddle-pan waffles will live on in perpetuity. --JP</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n[https://www.facebook.com/samhardacre Sam Hardacre] one of [http://themarketinglab.co.uk/ The Marketing Lab's] array of Geek Brains, brought this rather clever idea to my attention and also provided the picture, thanks Sam.\n\nIt does not require a [[Waffle maker]] and can made with a normal stove-top griddle pan.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 [[Free range eggs|free range eggs]]\n| 300 ml [[Buttermilk|buttermilk]] or [[Semi-skimmed milk|semi-skimmed milk]]\n| See this [[buttermilk]] link for how to make your own buttermilk from regular [[milk]]\n| 225 g (8 oz) [[Self-raising flour|self-raising flour]]\n| &#188; teaspoons [[Table salt|table salt]]\n| 100g [[Butter|butter]] , softened in the [[Microwave|microwave]] for a few seconds\n| 1tsp extra [[Butter|butter]] for cooking\n| Optional for sweet waffles: \n| &#189; tsp. [[Vanilla extract|vanilla extract]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sugar|sugar]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Pre heat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3) if you are making lots so they can be kept warm\n* Get the [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]] nice and hot before [[Hand|hand]] as some cast [[Iron|iron]] pans can take a while to get hot.\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Whisk the [[Milk|milk]] and [[Eggs|eggs]] in a large bowl\n| Using a fine [[Sieve|sieve]], sift the [[Flour|flour]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Baking powder|baking powder]] into the [[Egg|egg]]-mix.\n| Fold the softened [[Butter|butter]] into the mixture. Mix this just enough to combine the ingredients.  Jamie Oliver advises not to over-mix at this stage or the waffles will not puff up.\n| Add the extra teaspoons of [[Butter|butter]] to the pan and [[Brush|brush]] or swill to coat evenly.\n| Immediately pour the mixture into the pan over a medium heat  and carefully tip it to spread and cover the whole of the pan as you would with a [[Pancake|pancake]]\n| Cook for 8 to 10 minutes on this side, or until golden, then  then flip the waffle and cook for another 8 to 10 minutes on this side\n| If you are making lots then keep them warm in the [[Oven|oven]], but don't stack them of they will [[Sweat|sweat]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nCrispy [[Bacon|bacon]], sliced [[Avocado|avocado]] and [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]]\n\n[[Red onion]], [[Black olives|black olives]], and [[Feta cheese]]\n\n[[Butter]], [[Banana|banana]], [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]], and [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]]\n\n[[Maple syrup]]\n\n[[Honey]]\n\n[[Chocolate sauce]] and squirty [[Cream|cream]]\n===Recipe source===\n\n* http://www.jamieoliver.com/recipes/eggs-recipes/griddle-pan-waffles\n==See also==\n{{SeeAlso-Waffles}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Australian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:French recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #griddlepanwaffles #buttermilk #banana #freerangeeggs #hand #fetacheese #avocado #wafflemaker #chocolatesauce #pancake </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Hawaiian pizza",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Hawaiian pizza a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pineapple #pizza #ham #hawaiianpizza #oliveoil #pizzastone #cheese #grill #fineyellowcornmeal #bacon #pizzas \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Hawaiian pizza is a pizza that usually consists of a cheese and tomato base with pieces of ham and pineapple\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2225\n|PortionCalories = 556\n|DatePublished=7th November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 - Makes 2 large pizzas\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour, 25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 15 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Hawaiian pizza recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Ya can't beat this for a pizza \ud83c\udf55\ud83c\udf55\ud83c\udf55</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Some people (huh?) don't think this is a proper pizza = it is! \ud83d\ude0e</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nHawaiian [[Pizza|pizza]] is a pizza that usually consists of a [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Tomato|tomato]] base with pieces of [[Ham|ham]] and [[Pineapple|pineapple]]. Often versions will have mixed [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] and [[Bacon|bacon]]. Another variety consists of [[Pineapple|pineapple]] and Canadian [[Bacon|bacon]]. It is the most popular pizza in Australia, accounting for 15% of pizza sales. ''Wikipedia''.\n\nThis version is the [[Ham|ham]], [[mozzarella]] and [[Pineapple|pineapple]] version - and very good it is too.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 portion [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Tomato sauce for pizza]]\n| 250 g pack of sliced cooked [[Ham|ham]]\n| 2 balls of [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]], torn into small pieces\n| 280g can of [[Pineapple|pineapple]] slices or chunks (about 280g)\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1/2 an [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced, optional\n| [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]] for dusting\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* If using a [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]], preheat the [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] under a very hot [[Grill|grill]] for about 20 minutes. Place it about 8 cm (3\") from the heat source.\n* Leave the [[Pineapple|pineapple]] pieces draining in a [[Sieve|sieve]] while you prepare the [[Pizzas|pizzas]] - too much [[Juice|juice]] can make a soggy [[Pizza|pizza]].\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]] to high as you can get it\n| Set the [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] about 8 cm (3\") below the heat source or the [[Pizza|pizza]] may burn\n| Dust the work surface with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]] and then stretch or roll the [[Dough|dough]] into two thin rounds\n| Prick the pizzas all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking.\n| [[Grill]] the [[Pizza|pizza]] for about 2 minutes on one side only or until [[Browned|browned]].\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]], flip over and add the topping.\n| First give a little drizzle of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] then layer the [[Ham|ham]] [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Pineapple|pineapple]] over the [[Pizza|pizza]].\n| Add a drizzle of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for for 3 to 5 minutes (depending on how hot your [[Oven|oven]] is) or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] browns a little. Watch it carefully as it's easy to burn at such a high heat.\n| Serve!\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Australian recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pineapple #pizza #ham #hawaiianpizza #oliveoil #pizzastone #cheese #grill #fineyellowcornmeal #bacon #pizzas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

The concept is simple, the ingredients simpler.I have enhanced the 'bar food' version, as I learned they could be more complete and more satisfying. Serve for snacks or a [[Light lunch|light lunch]]. Think of [[Quesadillas|quesadillas]] as [[Tex-Mex]] [[Pizza|pizza]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] (10\"-12\")\n| 6 oz. [[Grated|grated]] [[Monterey Jack cheese]]\n| 1/3 cup fresh green or red [[Jalapeno|jalapeno]] [[Peppers|peppers]],  seeded and membraned, then [[Diced|diced]] fine\n| &frac12; cup [[Diced|diced]] [[Spanish]] (Yellow) [[Onion|onion]], fine diced\n| 3 tablespoons [[Tomato salsa|tomato salsa]] ( or more) you choose the [[Salsa|salsa]]-I make my own)\n| Chopped [[Cilantro]] (opt.)\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]] (opt.)\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Have everything at or close to room temperature and a large [[Fry|fry]] pan!\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Spread all ingredients ( except [[Cheese|cheese]])with the back of a large spoon on [[Tortilla|tortilla]] one. Set [[Grill|grill]].hob to medium low..\n| Sprinkle [[Cheese|cheese]] over [[Tomato|tomato]] [[Pepper|pepper]] [[Salsa|salsa]]. Place second [[Tortilla|tortilla]] over top. slide this into the pan, and [[Steam|steam]] by using pan cover, or not if you want a more brittle version of [[Quesadillas|quesadillas]]. After about 5 minutes, flip the [[Quesadilla|quesadilla]] to [[Brown|brown]] tortilla 2. When it is all sizzling (3 minutes), transfer to cutting board and slice in [[Wedges|wedges]], as you would a [[Pizza|pizza]] or [[Cheesecake|cheesecake]], 3  or 4 to a plate.\n| This recipe can be multiplied for extra appetisers. Remember: you can put in refritos, [[Steamed|steamed]] [[Corn|corn]], chopped [[Olives|olives]]...but this is the core recipe.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a good light 'cervesa' ([[Beer|beer]]) and lots of paper towels\n===Variations===\nChange [[Cheeses|cheeses]]. Medium Cheddars, Canadian Brick [[Cheese]] or Colby  also work well. You can also use chopped jarred [[Jalapenos|jalapenos]] or others, but it isn't fresh anymore. Canned jalapenos are milder, usually, then their fresh ancestors.\n===Chef's notes===\nOnly the [[Tortillas|tortillas]], [[Peppers|peppers]] and [[Cheese|cheese]] are constants.\n\nI found these difficult to flip, without emptying the contents all over the hob.  If you feel doubtful, use two plates to flip the quesadillas: Lay one over the pan, flip both over, place a second plate over the first, invert those, remove the top plate, replace with the pan, invert those, remove the plate.  ''If you can do a better job of explaining this, please do.''\n\nRecipe contributed by [[User:Tetramariner|Tetramariner]] 15:28, 30 January 2010 (GMT)\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #hollywoodquesadillas #diced #tortilla #salsa #pizza #quesadillas #peppers #jalapenos #tortillas #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

You need to be quick as they can burn easily.\n| Lift the cooked [[Chips|chips]] out of the pan and let the [[Oil|oil]] drain and then stack on paper towels to remove excess oil.\n| Sprinkle with a pinch of [[Salt|salt]].\n| Allow to cool and crisp-up a little before serving.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nTry one of our [[Salsa|salsa recipes]] or this [[Tex-Mex bean dip for tacos]].\n===Chef's notes===\nFor health reasons, I have used [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n\nYou could possibly fry the whole tortilla first and then cut into triangles as they remain soft for a ref minutes after frying.                         "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Hoppin' John recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#hoppinjohn #peas #rice #bacon #hamhock #onion #boil #sausages #collardgreens #beans #simmer \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Hoppin' John is the Southern United States' version of the rice and beans dish traditional throughout the Caribbean\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4733\n|PortionCalories = 591\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 8\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Hoppin' John recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">No thanks</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I'd be hoppin' mad if someone served me this \ud83d\ude42</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Hoppin' John boil.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The rice is tender and the liquid is absorbed]]\n'''Hoppin' John''' is the Southern United States' version of the [[Rice|rice]] and [[Beans|beans]] dish traditional throughout the Caribbean. It consists of field [[Peas|peas]] or crowder peas ([[Black-eyed peas|black-eyed peas]]) and rice, with chopped [[Onion|onion]] and sliced [[Bacon|bacon]] or [[Sausages|sausages]], [[ham hock]] or fatback bacon.\n\nThroughout the coastal South, eating Hoppin' John on New Year's Day is thought to bring a year filled with luck, and it's eaten by everyone. The peas, or beans with little black \"eyes,\" signify coins. Fill your plate with them and your cup will run over, as in the 23rd Psalm, perhaps. [[Collard greens]] along with this dish are supposed to also add to the wealth since they are the colour of money. On the day after New Year's Day, leftover \"Hoppin' John\" is called '''\"Skippin' Jenny\"''', and further demonstrates one's frugality, bringing an even better chance of prosperity in the New Year, it is hoped.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 cups [[Dried|dried]] [[Black-eyed peas|black-eyed peas]] (about 340 g)\n| 2 cans of [[Black-eyed peas|black-eyed peas]], drained\n| 450 g (1 lb) lean slab [[Bacon|bacon]] \n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 1 small [[red bell pepper]], de-seeded and sliced\n| &#189; teaspoon crushed [[Chili flakes|chili flakes]]\n| &#189; teaspoon freshly ground [[cumin]] seeds\n| &#189; teaspoon dried [[oregano]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[sea salt]] or [[celery salt]]\n| 1 [[bay leaf]]\n| 4 cups water or [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| 2 cups uncooked long-[[Grain|grain]] white [[Rice|rice]]. [[Basmati rice]] is fine for this, though probably not authentic!\n| [[Salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using canned black eyed [[Peas|peas]], start at step 5\n| Sort the [[Peas|peas]] and remove grit etc.\n| Soak in cold water, rinse and drain, repeat a few times\n| In a large pot, cover with cold water, bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10 minutes, remove from heat and allow to stand for 2 hours.  Drain and rinse again.\n| To a large pot, add the soaked [[Black-eyed peas|black-eyed peas]], the [[ham hock]], the chopped [[Onion|onion]] and all of the herbs and spices.  If using spicy sausages I would wait for 1 hour before adding them\n| Add water or [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] and bring to the [[Boil|boil]]\n| Reduce the heat and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 2 hours or until the [[Peas|peas]] are tender. (do not [[Boil|boil]] as the [[Beans|beans]] will burst)\n| Remove [[Bacon|bacon]], [[ham hock]] or [[Sausages|sausages]] and cut into bite-sized pieces\n| As with all [[rice]], rinse for a minute, in a sieve under cold running water to remove any excess starch\n| Return [[Meat|meat]] to pot. Stir in [[Rice|rice]], cover, and cook for 20 to 25 minutes or until rice is tender and liquid is absorbed\n| Season to taste with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nTry 450 g (1 lb) meaty [[Ham hocks|ham hocks]] or 450 g (1 lb) thick spicy [[Sausage|sausage]] instead of the bacon.\n===Serving suggestion===\nServe with [[collard greens]], [[cornbread]] or fresh crusty bread.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you like a bit more gravy then reduce the amount of rice.  You could of course increase the amount of stock but you would need to adjust the seasoning as well.\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#hoppinjohn #peas #rice #bacon #hamhock #onion #boil #sausages #collardgreens #beans #simmer </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

From its home in Mexico, the dish has spread throughout the Americas.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 3 tablespoons (45ml) [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], peeled and finely chopped\n| 1 [[Clove|clove]] [[Garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| A pinch [[Chili powder|chili powder]]\n| 4 [[Plum|plum]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], peeled, seeded and chopped\n| 2 [[Corn tortillas|corn tortillas]]\n| 2 [[free range eggs]]\n| Chopped [[Chilli peppers|chilli peppers]], to taste\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]], to taste\n| 1 tablespoon freshly chopped [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| To prepare the ranchero sauce, in a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], heat 1 tablespoon [[Oil|oil]] over medium heat\n| Add the [[Onion|onion]] and [[Garlic|garlic]], and saut\u00e9 until softened, 4 or 5 minutes\n| Add the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Chili powder|chili powder]], [[Salt|salt]] and a few grinds of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] and reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]]\n| [[Simmer]] for about 10 minutes, until the [[Sauce|sauce]] begins to thicken\n| Add the [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley|parsley]], turn off the heat and cover the pan to keep the [[Sauce|sauce]] warm\n| In another [[Frying pan|frying pan]], lightly [[Fry|fry]] the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] in 1 tablespoon of [[Oil|oil]]. Remove and drain\n| If necessary, add additional [[Oil|oil]] to the second [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and [[Fry|fry]] the [[Eggs|eggs]] until they are \"[[How to fry an egg|sunny-side up]]\". \n| Transfer the [[Eggs|eggs]] to the [[Tortillas|tortillas]], and cover with the ranchero sauce\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#huevosrancheros #eggs #tomatoes #tortillas #fry #simmer #chilipowder #onion #sauce #parsley #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Jamies 30 minutes cauliflower and macaroni cheese recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pancetta #cauliflower #pasta #oliveoil #bacon #macaroni #foodprocessor #grated #cremefraiche #breadcrumbs #jamies30minutescauliflowerandmacaronicheese \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I saw Jamie Oliver make this recently on Jamie's 30 minute meals, though it seems te program was first shown on Channel 4 way back in 2010\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3594\n|PortionCalories = 898\n|DatePublished=8th March 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  50 minutes\n|PrepTime =  25 minutes\n|CookTime =  25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Cauliflower and macaroni cheese recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Jamie wins again</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Love him of loath him, Jamie's ideas always seem to work well, especially the time saving ideas.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Cauliflower and macaroni cheese_ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Cauliflower and macaroni cheese, the ingredients]] \nI saw Jamie Oliver make this recently on Jamie's 30 minute meals, though it seems te program was first shown on Channel 4 way back in 2010.  We regularly have variations of a similar recipe but using [[Broccoli|broccoli]] instead of [[cauliflower]]. I thought it would be fun to try it 'Jamies way'.  I really liked the idea of the topping he used with the slices of [[Pancetta|pancetta]] and [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]. \n\nI won't be attempting to do the whole meal in 30 minutes - just preheating the [[Oven|oven]] breaks that one!\n\nYou will need a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a [[Grating|grating]] attachment and a metal blade for this recipe.\n\nI must say, the great tip taken from this recipe was to cook the [[cauliflower]] in quarters (leaves 'n all) with the [[pasta]] and just mash it when you assemble the dish. Genius, thanks Jamie!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 medium [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]]\n| 500g [[Dried pasta|dried pasta]] (small [[Macaroni|macaroni]] is good for this)\n| 250 g freshly [[Grated|grated]] mature [[Cheddar|cheddar]] or similar strong 'melting [[Cheese|cheese]]'\n| 2 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 250 g [[Creme fraiche|creme fraiche]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''[[Bacon|bacon]] [[Crumble topping|crumble topping]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 8 slices of [[Pancetta|pancetta]] or similar thin cut, high quality [[Cured|cured]] [[Ham|ham]]\n| 3 [[Brown|brown]] [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]] or 6 slices of good [[Brown bread|brown bread]]\n| 2 [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| Leaves picked and chopped from a bunch of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] of your choice\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n* Fill and [[Boil|boil]] a [[Kettle|kettle]] of water\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Using no [[Oil|oil]], lay the [[Pancetta|pancetta]] or [[Bacon|bacon]] out in the base of an [[Oven|oven]]-proof [[Baking tray|baking tray]]\n| Place in the middle of the preheated [[Oven|oven]] for about 6 minutes or until the [[Pancetta|pancetta]] is nice and crispy.\n| Quarter the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] together with the surrounding leaves and pop in a large pan.\n| Add the [[Pasta|pasta]] to the same pan and fill with [[Boiling|boiling]] water, ensuring  the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] is covered.  Stir the pan to ensure the [[Macaroni|macaroni]] does not start to stick. ''It's heartening to see that even Jamie manages to get [[Macaroni|macaroni]] stuck to the base of the pan''! \n| Add 1.5 teaspoons of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]], cover with a lid and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| If you saw the TV program, Jamie lets it boil over (you know it's boiling then!) and then turns it down to a simmer and rests a wooden spoon under the lid to lift it up and prevent it boiling over again.\n| Put a metal blade in the [[Food processor|food processor]] and add the crispy [[Pancetta|pancetta]] and any of the [[Oil|oil]] left after the cooking.\n| Tear the rolls into a few pieces and add those to the [[Pancetta|pancetta]].\n| Pick the leaves from your chosen [[Herbs|herbs]] and add those.\n| Season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], add 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] and 2 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| Blitzt into [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]].\n| Once the [[Pasta|pasta]] and [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] is cooked to your liking, drain, reserving 400 ml of the water it was cooked in.\n| Put the tray that the bacon was cooked in n the hob and heat it up.\n| Using the fat remaining from the bacon, or a little extra [[olive oil]] if needed, saut\u00e9 the crushed [[garlic]] with a little black pepper until it is slightly coloured. \n| Tip the [[Cauliflower|cauliflower]] and [[Pasta|pasta]] into the [[Baking tray|baking tray]] the [[Pancetta|pancetta]] was cooked in and roughly [[Mash|mash]] with a [[Potato masher|potato masher]].\n| Add the [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheddar|cheddar]] and mix with 420 ml of the cooking liquid.\n| Stir in the [[Creme fraiche|creme fraiche]] and mix everything really well to make a gorgeous [[Sauce|sauce]].\n| Tip the [[Breadcrumb|breadcrumb]] mixture over the top of the [[Pasta|pasta]] and top with a sprinkling of [[Parmesan cheese|parmesan cheese]].\n| Place in the top of the [[Oven|oven]], lay a sheet of [[tin-foil]] over the top to prevent it burning and [[Bake|bake]] for about 15 minutes or until nice and golden.\n}}\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Cauliflower and macaroni cheese_ingredients.jpg|The basic ingredients\nImage:Roughly trim the cauliflower.jpg|Roughly trim the cauliflower\nImage:Lay the pancetta in an oven tray.jpg|Lay the pancetta in an oven tray\nImage:Hold the lid open.jpg|Hold the lid open with a wooden spoon\nImage:Blitzing bacon.jpg|Blitz the bacon with the breadcrumbs\nImage:Mashing genius.jpg|Mashing genius!\nImage:Not wet dont worry.jpg|Don't worry about too much water - even with this much liquid, this turned out too dry\nImage:Bacon breadcrumbs.jpg|Bacon, herb and breadcrumb topping\nImage:Cauliflower and macaroni cheese recipe.jpg|Cauliflower mac'n'cheese in 30 minutes (almost)\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Variations===\nUse [[Bacon|bacon]] instead of [[Pancetta|pancetta]], though you will probably need to increase the cooking time because it's quite a bit thicker than [[Pancetta|pancetta]] and we want it to be crispy for this dish.\n===Chef's notes===\nI've increased the original 400 ml of liquid to 420 ml as I found it a little on the dry side.  I would also lay a sheet of tin-foil over the  breadcrumbs on the final bake as ours burnt a little.\n\nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n\n* http://bit.ly/rspcathinkpig\n\n==See also==\n\n* [http://www.channel4.com/programmes/jamies-30-minute-meals/4od#3213866 A video of Jamie Oliver cooking this recipe] (registration required)\n* [http://www.strandsofmylife.com/jamie-olivers-30-minute-cauliflower-macaroni-cheese/ A similar recipe] on a nice New Zealand cookery blog I've discovered.\n\n{{Template:YoutubePastaDough}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pancetta #cauliflower #pasta #oliveoil #bacon #macaroni #foodprocessor #grated #cremefraiche #breadcrumbs #jamies30minutescauliflowerandmacaronicheese </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Jerky recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Jerky recipe Beef, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#jerky #pork #marinated #freeze #beef #jerkyrecipe #refrigerate #fat #venison #soysauce #marinade \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Jerky is meat that has been cut into strips trimmed of fat, marinated in a spicy, salty or sweet liquid and then dried with low heat (usually under 70\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1910\n|PortionCalories = 191\n|DatePublished=6th April 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 10 \n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  6 hours, 20 minutes + marinating time\n|PrepTime =  20 minutes + marinating time\n|CookTime =  6 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Beef jerky.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Chewy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">An acquired taste, and one that I've not yet acquired!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n===What is Jerky?===\nJerky is [[meat]] that has been cut into strips trimmed of [[fat]], marinated in a spicy, salty or sweet liquid and then dried with low heat (usually under 70\u00b0C/160\u00b0F) or occasionally [[salted]] and sun-dried. The result is a salty, stripped, semi-sweet snack that can be stored without [[refrigeration]]. Jerky is an early application of food preservation techniques.\n===Preparation===\nAny single preparation, or recipe for jerky typically uses only one type of meat. Of the many types of meat that may be used, [[beef]] is the most common. Meat from other animals\u2014such as wild game, [[venison]], elk, caribou and moose\u2014is also used. Recently, other meats have come to market, such as [[turkey]], [[ostrich]], [[salmon]], alligator, and [[tuna]]. The meat must be dried quickly, to limit bacterial growth during the critical period where the meat is not yet dry. To do this, the meat is thinly sliced, or pressed thinly, in the case of ground meat. Drying is performed at low temperatures, to avoid cooking or over drying the meat and making it brittle.\n===Space jerky===\nSince 1996, jerky has been selected by astronauts several times for space flight due to its light weight and high level of nutrition.\n[[Image:Space jerky.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Jerky on International Space Station with Earth visible through the window. Carried to ISS aboard STS-118, Endevour Space Shuttle flight]]\n[[Jerky]] can be made from almost any lean [[Meat|meat]], with [[Beef|beef]] or [[Venison|venison]] being the best. If made from [[Pork|pork]] the [[Meat|meat]] must be treated to kill the trichinella parasite before it is sliced and [[Marinated|marinated]]. This parasite could cause trichinosis. To treat the [[Pork|pork]], [[Freeze|freeze]] a portion that is 15cm or less thick at -15\u00b0C or lower for 20 days. [[Poultry]] is not recommended for [[Jerky|jerky]], because of its texture when raw.\n===Recipe preparation===\nThe [[Meat|meat]] is [[Marinated|marinated]] for both flavour and tenderness. Ingredients for [[Marinades|marinades]] include [[Oil|oil]], [[Salt|salt]] and an acid product such as [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Lemon juice|lemon juice]], [[Teriyaki|teriyaki]], [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]] or [[Wine|wine]].\nThe first step in preparing the [[Meat|meat]] is to slice it into long, thin strips. Trim and discard all the [[Fat|fat]] from the [[Meat|meat]], because it becomes rancid rapidly Partially [[Freezing|freezing]] the [[Meat|meat]] before cutting makes it easier to slice evenly Slice with the [[Grain|grain]] into thin strips approximately 6mm thick if a chewy [[Jerky|jerky]] is desired. Slice across the grain for a more tender, brittle [[Jerky|jerky]] A tenderiser can also be used on the meat. \n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 750g of lean [[Meat|meat]], prepared as above\n| &frac14; teaspoon each of [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Onion|onion]] powder\n| 1 teaspoon hickory smoke-flavoured [[Salt|salt]]\n| 60ml [[Soy sauce|soy sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Combine all ingredients. \n| Place strips of [[Meat|meat]] in a bowl and cover with the [[Marinade|marinade]]. \n| Cover and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] 1-2 hours or overnight.\n| Remove [[Meat|meat]] strips from the [[Marinade|marinade]], drain on absorbent towelling and arrange on dehydrator trays. Place the slices close together but do not overlap. \n| Place the trays in the dehydrator preheated at 70\u00b0C.\n| Dry until a test piece cracks but does not break when it is bent (6-10 hours). \n| Pat off any [[Oil|oil]] with absorbent towelling and cool. Remove strips from the racks. \n| Allow to cool and package in [[Glass|glass]] jars or heavy plastic bags.\n}}\n\n===Servings===\n300g to 450g of Jerky\n===Chef's notes===\nProperly [[Dried|dried]] [[Jerky|jerky]] will keep at room temperature 1 to 2 months in a sealed container. However, to increase the shelf life and maintain the flavour, [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] or [[Freeze|freeze]].\n\nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n\n* http://bit.ly/rspcathinkpig\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Game recipes]]\n[[Category:Lamb recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Veal recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Dehydrated]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#jerky #pork #marinated #freeze #beef #jerkyrecipe #refrigerate #fat #venison #soysauce #marinade </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }
}

                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Lady Bird Johnson's Pedernales River Chili a beef recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#fat #garlic #grated #choppedspringonions #ladybirdjohnsonspedernalesriverchili #beans #frying #cheddarcheese #dutchoven #unusualrecipes #mincedbeef \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Lyndon Baines Johnson liked his chili very hot and with no beans\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 7152\n|PortionCalories = 715\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment =\n |Servings = 10 to 14\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 2 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Lady Bird Johnson's PedernalesRiver Chili recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Meh!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">3</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Nothing special, just hot, not tasty</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nLyndon Baines Johnson liked his [[Chili|chili]] very hot and with no [[Beans|beans]].  Lady Bird Johnson's original recipe also contained [[Suet|suet]] but this was later omitted after LBJ's heart attack.\n\nThis is the healthier version of the famous chili con carne.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 kg (4 lb) chuck [[Steak|steak]], cubed and trimmed of [[Fat|fat]] or lean [[Minced beef|minced beef]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and chopped\n| 3 tablespoons [[Oil|oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cumin seeds|cumin seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]]\n| 6 teaspoons red [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 2 x 340 g cans of [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| 2 cups of hot water\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n}}\n'''to garnish'''\n* 20g [[Grated]] [[Cheddar cheese]]\n* 20g [[Chopped spring onions]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a [[Dutch Oven|Dutch oven]]\n| Add the [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a minute or so\n| Add the [[Onions|onions]] and the [[Meat|meat]] and saut\u00e9 until the [[Meat|meat]] and the onions are cooked\n| Add the remaining ingredients, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 1 hour\n| Skim any [[Fat|fat]] from the surface\n| Sprinkle with [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]] and garnish with [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]]\n}}\n===Variations===\nServe it as he liked it, with [[Saltine|saltine]] [[Crackers|crackers]] and a glass of [[Milk|milk]].  Bath Olivers dry water biscuits are a good equivalent for those on this side of the pond.\n===Chef's notes===\nYou can skim the [[Fat|fat]] LBJ's way.  Allow to cool naturally, [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] and remove the fat when cold.\n\nReheat to serve.\n==See also==\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#fat #garlic #grated #choppedspringonions #ladybirdjohnsonspedernalesriverchili #beans #frying #cheddarcheese #dutchoven #unusualrecipes #mincedbeef </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=London broil recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#londonbroil #barbecue #grain #flanksteak #grill #northamerican #marination #thricecookedchips #juice #images #restfor \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=London broil is a North American beef dish made by grilling marinated flank steak, then cutting it against the grain into thin strips\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1808\n|PortionCalories = 452\n|DatePublished=18th August 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  12 hours, 10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  12 hours\n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:London_broilII.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Looks fab.</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Tastes fab too.  I marinate mine for 24 hours or more though.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\nLondon [[Broil|broil]] is a [[North American]] [[Beef|beef]] dish made by [[Grilling|grilling]] [[Marinated|marinated]] [[Flank steak|flank steak]], then cutting it against the [[Grain|grain]] into thin strips.\n\nThe name generally refers to the [[Marination|marination]] method rather than the [[Cut of beef|cut of beef]].\n\nThis recipe can also be cooked on a [[Barbecue|barbecue]].\n\nPlease ensure that you [[Rest|rest]] the [[Meat|meat]] for at least 10 minutes before serving.  It won't go cold and this method ensures a tender [[Steak|steak]] that is not too bloody.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 900g (2 lb) [[Flank steak]]\n| [[Juice]] and [[Zest|zest]] from 1 [[Lemon|lemon]] (or [[Lime|lime]])\n| 5 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 4 [[Fat|fat]] [[Cloves of Garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves of garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Balsamic vinegar|balsamic vinegar]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Dijon Mustard|dijon mustard]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Light soy sauce|light soy sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried thyme|dried thyme]]\n| Splash of good [[Chilli sauce|chilli sauce]] (to taste)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Place all of the ingredients in a shallow [[Lock & Lock]] style box.\n| Shake vigorously for a minute.\n| [[Refrigerate]] for 12 hours, shaking and turning now and then.\n| Prepare a very hot [[Grill|grill]], [[Barbecue|barbecue]] or [[Griddle pan|griddle pan]]\n| [[Grill]] for 3 to 4 minutes per side (or to your liking)\n| Allow the cooked [[Meat|meat]] joint to [[Rest for|rest for]] 10 minutes in a [[Warm place|warm place]].\n| Slicing the [[Meat|meat]] against (across) the [[Grain|grain]] will give you the most tender cuts of [[Meat|meat]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Horseradish cream|horseradish cream]], [[Thrice cooked chips|thrice cooked chips]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli
