title": "Macaroni cheese (TM)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Macaroni cheese a Thermomix recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheese #pasta #sodiumcitrate #bakingsheet #panko #cheddar #fat #tapiocaflour #bake #crumble #refrigerate \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This recipe is for a delicious macaroni cheese made in a Thermomix. It is more time consuming than most, but is well worth the effort\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4385\n|PortionCalories = 1461\n|DatePublished=23rd June 2015\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 3-4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  2 hours (plus cooling time)\n|PrepTime =  30 minutes (plus cooling time)\n|CookTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Macaroni cheese TM recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Looks lovely Julia</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Very fancy-pants!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is for a delicious [[Macaroni cheese|macaroni cheese]] made in a [[Thermomix]].  It is more time consuming than most, but is well worth the effort and the first two stages can be made in advance.\n{{RecipeIngredientsTM\n}}\n====For the cheese topping====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 120g [[Cheddar]] and / or mature [[Swiss cheese]], cut into chunks\n| 30g water\n| 1.25g [[Sodium citrate|sodium citrate]]\n| 50g [[Tapioca flour|tapioca flour]] ([[Starch|starch]])\n| 50g [[Panko|panko]]\n}}\n====For the macaroni====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1.5kg water\n| \u00bd teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| 200g [[Macaroni|macaroni]] or other short [[Pasta|pasta]] tubes\n| A little flavourless [[Oil|oil]]\n}}\n====For the cheese sauce====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 270g mixed extra mature [[Cheddar]] and [[Parmesan]], cut into chunks\n| 185g full [[Fat|fat]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 13g [[Sodium citrate|sodium citrate]]\n| 80g full [[Fat|fat]] [[Cream cheese|cream cheese]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Pre-heat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Put the [[Cheese|cheese]] into the bowl 5 seconds / Speed 5\n| Remove from the bowl and divide into 100g and 20g.  Reserve.\n| Add the water to the bowl with the [[Sodium citrate|sodium citrate]] '''2 minutes 30 seconds / 98\u00b0 C / Speed 2'''\n| Add the [[Cheese|cheese]], a little at a time '''3-4 minutes / 98\u00b0 C / Speed 2'''.  Make sure that each addition of cheese is melted and smooth before adding the next.\n| Add the [[Tapioca flour|tapioca flour]], a third at a time '''5 minutes / 98\u00b0 C / Speed 2'''.\n| Empty onto a sheet of [[Bake-O-Glide]] or silicone mat whilst still warm.\n| Soread out the mixture until thin and even.\n| Place the sheet onto a [[Baking tray|baking tray]] and [[Bake|bake]] until completely dry and golden [[Brown|brown]] for about 25-40 minutes.\n| Allow to cool and break into pieces.\n| Place in the bowl and blitz '''10 Seconds / Speed 10''' (or use a [[Spice|spice]] grinder)\n| Add the remaining [[Cheese|cheese]] and the [[Panko|panko]] and mix '''6 Seconds / Speed 3'''\n| Refigerate in an [[Airtight container|airtight container]] until needed.\n| The [[Cheese|cheese]] topping will keep for 2-3 days.\n}}\n====For the macaroni====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Chill a metal [[Baking sheet|baking sheet]] in the [[Freezer|freezer]] for a minimum of 30 minutes.\n| [[Boil]] the water in the TM jug and add [[Salt|salt]] '''11 minutes / 98\u00b0C / Speed 2''' then add [[Pasta|pasta]]. \n| Cook '''3 minutes / 98\u00b0C / Speed Spoon / Reverse Blade''', turning down to 90\u00b0C if it bubbles up onto TM lid.\n| Drain (do not rinse) and spread on the [[Baking sheet|baking sheet]] in a single layer.\n| Leave the [[Pasta|pasta]] to cool for 5 minutes, then transfer to a bowl.\n| Lightly dress in the [[Oil|oil]], cover and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] until ready for use.\n}}\n====For the cheese sauce====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a dry bowl, grate the hard [[Cheese|cheese]] '''7 seconds / Speed 5'''.\n| Remove and reserve. \n| Put the [[Milk|milk]] and [[Sodium citrate|sodium citrate]] into the bowl '''3 minutes 30 seconds / 98\u00b0 C / Speed 2'''.\n| Keeping the '''same speed and temperature''', gradually add the hard and [[Cream cheeses|cream cheeses]] and mix until they have melted and the mixture is smooth - about 4 minutes.\n| Leave to cool very slighty.\n}}\n====To assemble and bake====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Pre-heat the [[Oven|oven]] to 220\u00b0 C (425\u00b0 F - gas 7), [fan oven 200\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n| Mix the [[Cheese sauce|cheese sauce]] with the [[Pasta|pasta]] and tip into a [[Casserole dish|casserole dish]].\n| Sprinkle the [[Cheese|cheese]] [[Crumble|crumble]] mixture over the top.\n| [[Bake]] for about 15 minutes covered then remove the lid and bake for a further 10 minutes or until the top is golden [[Brown|brown]].\n| Serve whilst still hot.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis is very filling, so best served with just [[Salad|salad]].\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Adapted and converted for Thermomix from a recipe in ''' ''[http://www.amazon.co.uk/Modernist-Cuisine-Home-Nathan-Myhrvold/dp/0982761015/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&ie=UTF8&qid=1435037010&sr=1-1&keywords=Modernist Modernist Cuisine at Home]'' '''\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Molecular gastronomy recipes]]\n[[Category:Thermomix recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#cheese #pasta #sodiumcitrate #bakingsheet #panko #cheddar #fat #tapiocaflour #bake #crumble #refrigerate </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Meatball pizza",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Meatball pizza a cheese recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pizza #meatballpizza #meatballs #sauce #pizzastone #grill #pizzas #oliveoil #mozzarellacheese #chili #redwine \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=To my mind this is about the pizza and the sauce, not the actual meatballs, hence using shop-made meatballs\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1893\n|PortionCalories = 473\n|DatePublished=22nd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 - Makes two large [[Pizzas|pizzas]]\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour 25 minutes<br />Includes making the dough\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes  \n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Meatball pizza recipe baked.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Pizza perfection</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A complete meal that tastes even better than it looks</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nTo my mind this is about the [[Pizza|pizza]] and the [[Sauce|sauce]], not the actual [[Meatballs|meatballs]], hence using shop-made meatballs.  By all means '''[[Meatballs|make your own]]''' if you feel so inclined.\n\nUse a [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]]!  It makes such a difference.  Your [[Pizzas|pizzas]] will go from those soggy-based shop bought shockers, to [[Pizza]] Express perfection in one simple step!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 portion [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]]\n| 300 g pack of cooked [[Meatballs|meatballs]] of your choice\n| 150 g pack of [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]]\n| large can [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], chopped.\n| A good glug of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and sliced\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, crushed|cloves garlic, crushed]]\n| 1 [[Dried|dried]] [[Chile de Arbole|chile de arbole]], [[Ground|ground]] to powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]] or [[Pestle and mortar|pestle and mortar]] (or &frac12; teaspoon [[Chili powder|chili powder]])\n| 125 ml [[Red wine|red wine]]\n| A pinch of [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| [[Fine yellow cornmeal]] for dusting\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Make the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] as instructed\n* If using a [[pizza stone]], preheat the [[pizza stone]] under a very hot [[grill]] for about 20 minutes.  Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Meatball pizza ready for the oven.jpg|Ready for the oven\nImage:Meatball pizza stone baked.jpg|One done, one waiting\nImage:Meatball pizza tomato sauce.jpg|Tomato sauce reduced\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n'''Meatball [[Sauce|sauce]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| [[Fry]] the [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] in a few glugs of [[Olive oil|olive oil]] seasoned with [[Black pepper|black pepper]] until soft, about 10 minutes.\n| Add the [[Meatballs|meatballs]], [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Red wine|red wine]], [[Chili|chili]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] until reduced and very thick - you don't want a wet [[Pizza|pizza]].\n| As I have plenty of time on [[Pizza|pizza]] day (Friday!) I make the [[Sauce|sauce]] early in the afternoon and put it on the heat for 5 minute batches every hour or so, leaving it uncovered to 'dry-out' in between. You can of course just [[Simmer|simmer]] to reduce, but you need to watch it and keep stirring all the time.\n| Season to taste\n}}\n'''Putting it together'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Preheat the [[Grill|grill]] to high as you can get it\n| Set the [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] about 8 cm (3\") below the heat source or the [[Pizza|pizza]] may burn\n| Dust the work surface with [[yellow cornmeal]] and then stretch or roll the [[Dough|dough]] into two thin rounds\n| Prick the pizza all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking\n| [[Grill]] the [[Pizza|pizza]] for about 2 minutes on one side only or until browned.\n| Remove from the oven, flip over and ad the topping.\n| Divide the [[Meatballs|meatballs]] and [[Sauce|sauce]] between the two [[Pizzas|pizzas]], cut the meatballs in half and spread over the [[Pizza|pizza]]\n| Cover with sliced [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]], drizzle with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and [[Bake|bake]] for for 3 to 5 minutes (depending on how hot your [[Oven|oven]] is) or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] browns a little.  Watch it carefully as it's easy to burn at such a high heat.\n| Serve!\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nLots of supermarkets do chopped tomatoes, flavoured with [[Chili|chili]]/[[Basil|basil]]/[[Oregano|oregano]] etc, and though it's as easy to do this yourself, they are quite handy for [[Pizza|pizza]] toppings.\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]][[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pizza #meatballpizza #meatballs #sauce #pizzastone #grill #pizzas #oliveoil #mozzarellacheese #chili #redwine </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Memphis BBQ pulled duck tacos",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Memphis BBQ pulled duck tacos recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#duck #memphisbbqpulledducktacos #barbecuesauce #tacotrays #tacos #tacoshells #springonions #sourcream #sauce #fat #cherries \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Crispy tacos filled with Gressingham pulled duck and salad, serve with sour cream and black cherries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1008\n|PortionCalories = 504\n|DatePublished=30th November 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  45 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Memphis BBQ pulled duck tacos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice, but...</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">What an expensive way to buy duck! \ud83e\udd2d</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is more an assembly list than a recipe.  I spotted the [[Gressingham Memphis Barbecue Pulled Duck]] in Morrisons and thought it would make a good [[Taco|taco]] filling. \n\nThe [[Duck|duck]] was very good and I'll be getting more today.  Do note though that the duck is notreally pulled duck, it's duck legs with a sauce that need to be ''pulled'' once they've been cooked.  \n\nThe Old El Paso [[Tacos|tacos]] however, ''really'' let this recipe down.  They are so thin now that they break apart as you touch them. Any because they are so miserably thin, they don't even have the crunch purported on the packet.  Another cynical attempt at increasing profits I guess.\n\nIf you don't want to use the flimsy El Paso [[Tacos]], try to hunt down the cheaper and far nice Discovery [[Taco trays|taco trays]], or forget tacos altogether and use [[Corn|corn]] or [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] instead.\n\nThe [[Duck|duck]] feels like it might serve 4 but is actually contains 2 duck legs, a [[Foil|foil]] tray and a sachet of [[Sauce|sauce]], plenty for 2 people, not enough for four.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 pack [[Gressingham Memphis BBQ Pulled Duck]] (2 duck legs in with [[Barbecue sauce|barbecue sauce]])\n| 1 Pack Discovery [[Taco trays|taco trays]] or if you must ,1 Pack El Paso [[Taco shells]] (see notes above)\n| 6 [[Spring onions|spring onions]]\n| 12 [[Baby tomatoes|baby tomatoes]]\n| Half a green [[Sweet Pepper|sweet pepper]]\n| 10 [[Black cherries|black cherries]]\n| 150 ml pot of [[Sour cream|sour cream]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat your [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Memphis BBQ pulled duck tacos ingredients.jpg|thumb|right|300px|The basic ingredients\nImage:Gressingham Memphis Barbecue Pulled Duck.jpg|thumb|right|300px|[[Gressingham Memphis Barbecue Pulled Duck]] (whole duck legs with sauce)\n</gallery>\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Remove the [[Duck|duck]] legs from the plastic wrapping and place in the tray provided, make sure you include all the lovely [[Fat|fat]] too!\n| Leave the [[Sauce|sauce]] sachet to one side for now\n| [[Roast]] the [[Duck|duck]] legs at 180\u00b0 C for 25 minutes, uncovered, in the tray provided\n| After 25 minutes, drain and discard some of the cooking juices (see [[Chef's notes]] below).\n| Add the contents of the Memphis [[Barbecue sauce|barbecue sauce]] to the duck's legs and mix well\n| [[Bake]] for a further 10 minutes\n| When there is 5 minutes remaining pop the [[Taco trays|taco trays]] or fragile El Paso [[Taco shells|taco shells]] into the [[Oven|oven]] to warm up\n| Meanwhile: chop the [[Spring onions|spring onions]] ([[Scallions|scallions]])\n| Halve the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| Halve the [[Cherries|cherries]] and remove the stones\n| Chop the [[Green pepper|green pepper]]\n| Using two forks, shred the [[Duck|duck]] legs with two forks\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe the pulled [[Duck|duck]], [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[Tacos|tacos]] and [[Sour cream|sour cream]] in separate dishes so diners can assemble the tacos at the table\n===Variations===\nUse whatever filling ingredients that take your fancy, some other suggestions, sliced red onions, avocado, pickled chillies, crispy lettuce, pineapple chunks.\n===Chef's notes===\nThe [[Gressingham BBQ Pulled Duck]] (legs) are already pre-cooked. If you are using [[Fresh duck|fresh duck]] legs, they will will probably take about the same time, but the [[Oven|oven]] could do with being 1 little warmed (190\u00b0 C - 200\u00b0 C) and they will benefit from resting for 15 minutes once removed from the oven.\n\nThe cooking instructions on the [[Gressingham Pulled Duck]] suggests discarding all of the cooking juices after 25 minutes of [[Roasting|roasting]]. I would definitely suggest otherwise.  Next time I will mix them in with the [[Barbecue sauce|barbecue sauce]], and not waste them.\n\nI allowed the juices to solidify overnight and it was almost all lovely tasty jelly, hardly any [[Fat|fat]] - made a great [[Sandwich|sandwich]] filling and reminded me of jelly and [[Dripping|dripping]] of old.\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#duck #memphisbbqpulledducktacos #barbecuesauce #tacotrays #tacos #tacoshells #springonions #sourcream #sauce #fat #cherries </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Minced beef for tacos",
                "revisions": [
                    {

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Minced beef for tacos a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#spices #mincedbeeffortacos #beef #chicken #tacotrays #orange #tomatopuree #ghee #guacamole #springonions #tacoshells \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I decided to perfect this because I was fed up with buying a famous brand packet of spices every time I wanted to make tacos\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1004\n|PortionCalories = 502\n|DatePublished=31st October 2012\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 hour 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 5 minutes plus 1 hour marinading\n|CookTime = 10 minutes \n|Image = [[Image:Shredded minced beef for tacos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Favetastic!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Just about my favourite meal!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Taco trays.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Discover Taco Trays]]\nI decided to perfect this because I was fed up with buying a ''famous brand'' packet of [[spices]] every time I wanted to make tacos. I think that this is pretty close.  It works with [[chicken]] as well as [[beef]].\n\nI deliberately wanted a dry mix to put into taco shells, as the ''[[sauce]]'' would be provided by [[guacamole]], [[sour cream]] or [[yogurt]]\n\n\n'''Main ingredients'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 packet of [[taco shells]] or [[taco trays]]\n| 225 g (1/2 lb) lean minced [[beef]]\n| 1 [[red pepper]], chopped finely\n| Juice from &#189; an [[orange]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[ghee]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[tomato puree]]\n}}\n'''For the dry spice mix'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon dried smoked chillies such as [[chipotle]]:\n| 1/4 of a teaspoon of [[black peppercorns]]\n| 5 cm (1/2\") [[cinnamon stick]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[white cumin]] seeds\n| 1 teaspoon [[black cumin]] seeds\n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[dried minced garlic]]\n| [[Sea salt]] to taste\n| &#189; teaspoon of [[dried]] [[oregano]]\n| Good pinch of [[salt]] or 1 tablespoon of juice from [[preserved lemons]] - if using the latter, add in step 3 \n}}\n'''For garnishing'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| Four [[spring onions]], [[chopped on the diagonal]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind all of the dry [[spices]] in a [[coffee grinder]]\n| Tip the mince and the [[chopped red peppers]] into a bowl\n| Add the dry [[spices]] and [[tomato puree]] and mix them together by kneading the mince\n| If you have the time, leave for an hour in a cool place for the flavours to mingle\n| Heat the [[ghee]] in a [[frying]] pan or [[wok]]\n| Add the mince and [[fry]]  until done to your liking\n| Pour off any excess [[fat]]\n| Add the juice from &#189; an [[orange]]\n| [[Stir fry]] for a few more minutes and pour away any excess liquid\n| If desired, put in half the of the spring onions during the last minute of cooking (as in the photo), kill the heat and serve immediately.\n| Arrange on a hot plate and sprinkle with all of/the rest of the chopped [[spring onions]] over the filled taco shells\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[taco shells]] (or the really neat [[taco trays]]), [[sour cream]], [[guacamole]], [[pickled jalape\u00f1os]] and a salsa such as [[sweet potato salsa]]\n===Variations===\n\nTry [[chicken]] fillets or [[shredded]] [[beef]] steak instead\n\nSprinkle with grated [[Monterey Jack]] or [[Cheddar cheese]]\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Beef]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes|Beef]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spices #mincedbeeffortacos #beef #chicken #tacotrays #orange #tomatopuree #ghee #guacamole #springonions #tacoshells </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Don't not rinse the [[Pasta|pasta]]\n| Mix [[Pasta|pasta]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]] together and serve, topped with the [[Cheese sauce|cheese sauce]] and a garnished with sliced tomatoes and a sprinkling of chopped [[Chives|chives]] and [[Parsley|parsley]]\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Based on Mac and [[Cheese|cheese]]: ''Modernist Cuisine'' ISBN 978-0982761007\n===Variations===\nUse any hard [[Cheese|cheese]] of your choice\n\n===Chef's notes===\nFor the quantities I used recipe scaling to calculate the portion sizes for 2 people from a 5 portion original. (scaling factor 0.4 [2/5]), however I think we could have done with a little more so have adjusted the ingredients on this recipe to a scaling factor of 0.6 [3/5].\n\nTry variation of [[Pasta|pasta]] and [[Vegetables|vegetables]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Molecular gastronomy recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pasta #cheese #vegetables #cauliflower #grated #broccoli #blackbombercheese #sodiumcitrate #parsley #chives #modernistmacandcheeserecipe </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Serves 8 - Makes 8 [[Tamales|tamales]]\n |Difficulty = 3\n |ImageComment = An assembled nacatamal\n |TotalTime = 4 hours 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 25 minutes plus overnight marinade\n |CookTime = 4 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Nacatamal (Nicaraguan tamales) recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span filling:'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g boneless [[pork]], [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces or [[Turkey|turkey]] breast, cut into 8 pieces\n| 70 ml [[Seville orange]] [[Juice|juice]] or 35 ml each of [[Orange|orange]] and [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Achiote|achiote]]\n| [[Garlic]], to taste, crushed\n}}\n'''For the [[Masa|masa]]:'''\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 450 g [[Tamale|tamale]] [[Flour|flour]] or [[Masa harina|masa harina]]\n| 280 ml [[Milk|milk]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Lard|lard]] or Trex\n| 15 ml [[Seville orange]] [[Juice|juice]] or a mixture of [[Orange|orange]] and [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| 115 g [[Mashed potato|mashed potato]]\n}}\n\n'''Garnishes:'''\n\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 [[Potato]], raw, sliced thinly into 5 cm squares\n| 2 [[Tomatoes]], thinly sliced\n| 2 [[Onions]], thinly sliced\n| 2 [[Sweet peppers]], thinly sliced\n| [[Mint leaves]]\n| 8 teaspoons of raw [[Rice|rice]]\n| [[Chillies]], thinly sliced\n}}\n'''For wrapping:'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 8 sheets of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]], cut into 38-40 cm squares \n}}\n'''OR'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Corn husks]]\n}}\n'''OR'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Banana leaves]]\n}}\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the filling ingredients and leave to [[Marinate|marinate]] overnight.\n| Mix the [[Masa|masa]] ingredients in a saucepan and cook over medium heat until the mixture is firm, but remains moist - about 30 minutes.\n| Take one-eighth of the [[Masa|masa]] and place in the centre of one piece [[Foil|foil]] or a husk.\n| Push 2 slices of [[Potato|potato]] into the [[Masa|masa]] near the bottom, then one piece of [[Meat|meat]] in the centre.\n| Cover the [[Masa|masa]] with 2 slices each of the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Peppers|peppers]].\n| Place 3 [[Mint leaves|mint leaves]] and a teaspoon of [[Rice|rice]] on the top.\n| Push [[Chilli|chilli]] slices into the edges of the [[Masa|masa]] and pour a teaspoon of the [[Marinade|marinade]] over the top.\n| To wrap, fold both ends of the [[Foil|foil]] or husks to the centre, allowing an overlap of 1 cm.\n| Fold one end tightly, stand the parcel on its end and shake down.\n| Tighten the wrapping and fold over the sides and seal.\n| The [[Tamale|tamale]] should be about 13 cm by 9.5 cm.\n| Repeat the process to make the remaining 7 [[Tamales|tamales]].\n| Place the [[Tamales|tamales]] in a large pan so that they are all in one layer.\n| Add cold water to cover.\n| Cover the pan and on a high heat, bring to the [[Boil|boil]], reduce heat, and [[Simmer|simmer]] for about 4 hours.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe as a snack, [[Light lunch|light lunch]] or even for breakfast.\n===Chef's notes===\nTamale flour, which is slightly more granular than masa harina can be obtained from [[Cool Chile Co]].                         "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=New England clam chowder, Fish recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#newenglandclamchowder #clams #boiling #flour #onion #bacon #frozen #butter #potato #saltpork #hardtack \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=New England clam chowder is a milk or cream-based chowder, traditionally made with potatoes, onion, bacon or salt pork, flour or hardtack, and clams\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2008\n|PortionCalories = 334\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 50 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 35 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:New England clam chowder recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Moorish with mussels</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.6</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I make the English version using good old mussels - lovely!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}}\nNew England clam chowder is a milk or cream-based chowder, traditionally made with [[potatoes]], [[onion]], [[bacon]] or [[salt pork]], [[flour]] or [[hardtack]], and clams.  It is occasionally referred to as Boston Clam Chowder in the Midwest.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 450 g canned [[Clams|clams]], [[Minced|minced]], or 350 g [[Frozen|frozen]] clams, thawed\n| 2 tablespoons plain white [[Flour|flour]]\n| 1 medium [[Potato|potato]], [[Dice|diced]]\n| 1 medium [[Onion|onion]], chopped finely\n| 250 ml [[Boiling|boiling]] water\n| 3 ounces [[salt pork]], diced\n| 1.7 [[Litres|litres]] [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Butter|butter]]\n| [[Salt|Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| If using [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Clams|clams]], drain and reserve liquid.\n| Cut hard parts away and keep them separate.\n| [[Saut\u00e9ing|Saut\u00e9]] salt pork in a heavy iron pot until brown and crisp.\n| Remove [[Pork|pork]] and saut\u00e9 hard part of [[Clam|clam]] and [[Onions|onions]] in hot [[Fat|fat]] until [[Onion|onion]] is light [[Brown|brown]].\n| Stir in [[Flour|flour]], then slowly add [[Boiling|boiling]] water, [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], and [[Diced|diced]] [[Potato|potato]].\n| Cover and [[Simmering|simmer]] gently 10 minutes or until potato is tender.\n| Add soft parts of [[Clams|clams]] and liquid.\n| Just before serving, stir in scalded [[Milk|milk]] and [[Butter|butter]].\n| Heat thoroughly, but not to [[Boiling|boiling]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe piping hot with [[oyster crackers]], [[soda crackers]] or crusty [[Bread|bread]].\n===Variations===\nUse [[bacon]] or [[home smoked bacon]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Soup and stock recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#newenglandclamchowder #clams #boiling #flour #onion #bacon #frozen #butter #potato #saltpork #hardtack </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Make 1 pizza per person\n| Dust the work surface with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| Stretch or roll the [[Dough|dough]] into two thin rounds\n| Sprinkle the stone with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| Prick the pizza all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking\n| Pre-cook the empty pizza base on one side only for about 3 minutes or until it is lightly browned\n| Remove from the oven, flip and add the topping.\n| Lightly [[Oil|oil]] one side of the [[Pizza|pizza]] and [[Grill|grill]], oiled side down, flip an repeat, about 2 minutes per side\n| Drizzle the [[Pizza|pizza]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and spread the pizza with &frac12; of the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]]\n| Top with torn [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]], Crushed [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Sausage|sausage]] and [[Meatballs|meatballs]]\n| [[Bake]] for 3 or 4  minutes or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] browns a little - watch it carefully as it can burn easily.\n| Remove and sprinkle with torn [[Basil|basil]] and [[Capers|capers]]\n| Keep the fist pizza warm at the bottom of the oven whilst you make the second.\n| Serve hot\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:New York-style stone baked pizza ready.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to go back in the oven\nImage:New York-style stone baked pizza base.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Stone baked base resting while the other base is cooking\n</gallery>\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[pizza peel]] use an upturned plate, dusted with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]] and some deft handwork to slide the dough onto the stone.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#newyorkstylestonebakedpizza #fineyellowcornmeal #pizzastone #grill #meatballs #pizzas #pizza #pizzadough #sausage #capers #pizzapeel </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "New York style calzone pizza",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=New York style calzone pizza a cheese recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#provolonecheese #pizzas #parmesancheese #meats #pizzadough #pizzastone #newyorkstylecalzonepizza #unusualrecipes #bake #dip #homesmokedbacon \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=You can fill this spicy calzone with just about anything\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1866\n|PortionCalories = 933\n|DatePublished=1st November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 2 plus some breakfast pizza!\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour 25 minutes<br />Includes making the dough\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes  \n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Goat's cheese and asparagus calzone pizza recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n}}\n\nYou can fill this spicy calzone with just about anything. For this version, I have used a packet of sliced speciality cold [[Meats|meats]], pepperoni, [[Salami|salami]], [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]] and [[Home smoked bacon|Home smoked bacon]].  Use what you have available but don't try to over-fill the [[Pizzas|pizzas]]!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 portion [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]]\n| 1 portion [[Spicy tomato pizza topping|spicy tomato pizza topping]] (use a jar of shop-bought [[Pizza|pizza]] [[Sauce|sauce]] if you're pushed for time)\n| 150 g selection of quality sliced meats from the [[deli counter]]\n| 250g [[Provolone cheese|provolone cheese]], sliced\n| 20 g (&frac14; cup) [[Parmesan cheese]], freshly [[Grated|grated]]\n| [[Basil leaves]] to garnish\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8) using a [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] if possible\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Divide your [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] into two balls and roll out into two 20 cm (8\") rounds\n| Spread one half of the base with the [[Spicy tomato sauce|spicy tomato sauce]]\n| Layer the [[Provolone cheese|provolone cheese]] and the sliced [[Meats|meats]], sprinkling with [[Parmesan cheese]]\n| Fold the pizza over so it creates a semi-circle and seal the edge by crimping rolling over, starting from one corner. A short [[Calzone folding|how-to guide is here]].\n| [[Brush]] the seal and the surface with [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| Cut 3 small slits in the top to allow [[Steam|steam]] to escape\n| Dust the [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]] with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| [[Bake]] for 10 minutes\n| Remove and let the [[Pizzas|pizzas]] rest for 5 miutes\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Salad|salad]].  If there is any [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] left over after making the [[Pizzas|pizzas]], warm it up and serve with the pizzas as a [[Dip|dip]]\n===Variations===\nUse [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]] if you can't get [[Provolone cheese|provolone cheese]]\n\nI love en egg inside a [[calzone]] pizza, but often find that it often does not cook properly, so a neat cheat is to [[Poached eggs|poach the egg]] in water beforehand.  I'm sure no self-respecting pizza chef would do that but it works for me!\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Like a Cornish pastie..</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..but much, much nicer!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#provolonecheese #pizzas #parmesancheese #meats #pizzadough #pizzastone #newyorkstylecalzonepizza #unusualrecipes #bake #dip #homesmokedbacon </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Try and keep the quantities about the same though\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1177\n|PortionCalories = 294\n|DatePublished=6th November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4 - Makes two large [[Pizzas|pizzas]]\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  1 hour 25 minutes<br />Includes making the dough\n|PrepTime = 1 hour 15 minutes  \n|CookTime =  10 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Pizza stone-used.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Almost as good!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not quite New York, but almost!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nAs with any pizza, you can make it with almost any ingredients. Try and keep the quantities about the same though.  You can end up with a damp soggy pizza if you overdo the [[cheese]].\n[[Image:New York style deli pizza ready to cook.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Ready to cook]]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 portion [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] - makes 2 pizzas\n| 1/2 portion [[Spicy tomato pizza topping|spicy tomato pizza topping]] (use a jar of shop-bought [[Pizza|pizza]] [[Sauce|sauce]] if you're pushed for time)\n| 150g [[Mozzarella cheese]], torn into pieces\n| 100g from a selection of good quality sliced meats from the [[deli counter]]\n| 25g of [[Parmesan cheese]], freshly [[Grated|grated]]\n| Olive oil\n| [[Basil leaves]] to garnish\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Make the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] as instructed\n* If using a [[pizza stone]], preheat the [[pizza stone]] under a very hot [[grill]] for about 20 minutes.  Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Make 1 pizza per person\n| Preheat the oven to 230\u00b0 C (450\u00b0 F - gas 8) or about 9 cm (3\") from a very hot grill if using a [[Pizza stone|pizza stone]]\n| Dust the work surface with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]] and divide your [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] into two balls and roll out into two 20 cm (8\") rounds\n| Prick the pizza all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking.\n| Pre-cook the pizza base for about 3 minutes on one side only if using a [[pizza stone]], then remove from the oven, flip and add the topping\n| Spread the [[Spicy tomato sauce|spicy tomato sauce]] on the surface of the pizza\n| Layer the sliced [[Meats|meats]] and [[Mozzarella cheese]] onto the pizza and sprinkle with [[Parmesan cheese]]\n| Drizzle with [[olive oil]]\n| [[Bake]] for about 9 to 10 minutes or until the base is crispy and the cheese has melted\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nGarnish with the [[basil leaves]] and serve with a [[Salad|salad]].  If there is any [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] left over after making the [[Pizzas|pizzas]], warm it up and serve with the pizzas as a [[Dip|dip]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pizzastone #pizzadough #newyorkstyledelipizza #basilleaves #pizzas #mozzarellacheese #parmesancheese #dip #meats #cheese #sauce </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Pick out and discard (or chop finely) any very large pieces that the food processor may have missed. [[Refrigerate]] overnight to allow the flavours to mingle\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n===Variations===\nUse a red cabbage instead of a [[white cabbage]] for a lovely pink [[coleslaw]].\n\nFor a really rich and luxurious slaw, use half the carrots, cabbage and apple but leave the quantities of the other ingredients as stated above.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you make the recipe using the quantities above, you will need a bucket to mix them in and a big fridge to store it in afterwards - great for barbecue quantities though.\n\nThe Manhattan Chili Co. has now closed, see image above. This recipe is a completely stripped down, wholesome paleo version of a [[Sausage|sausage]] [[Muffin|muffin]]! It has all the flavour, but without any processed nasties!\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 2 [[Debbie and Andrew's Harrogate 97% Gluten Free Pork Sausages]], de-skinned\n| 2 large [[Eggs|eggs]]\n| [[Salt]]\n| [[Black pepper]]\n| 1 [[Avocado|avocado]], [[Mashed|mashed]] with the [[Juice|juice]] of 1 [[Lime|lime]]\n| 100ml of water\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Take two stainless steel 8cm cutters, and grease using [[Olive oil|olive oil]].\n| In a mixing bowl, de-skin the [[Sausages|sausages]], season and mix.\n| On a plate, take the cutter and fill with the [[Sausage meat|sausage meat]].\n| Take a [[Frying pan|frying pan]], add [[Olive oil|olive oil]], and cook the [[Sausage|sausage]] patty on a medium heat for around 4 minutes.\n| Flip over, cook on the other side for 4 mins - place the cutter around the [[Meat|meat]] again to retain the shape.\n| Wash and clean the cutter.\n| Take the [[Eggs|eggs]] and crack into a bowl. Pierce the [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] with a fork.\n| In a non stick [[Frying pan|frying pan]], heat some [[Olive oil|olive oil]]. Add the cutter to the pan. Once the [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]] is hot, pour in the [[Egg|egg]].\n| Repeat this with the second [[Egg|egg]]. Season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Once the [[Eggs|eggs]] are cooking add the water to the pan, reduce the heat and cover. Allow the eggs to [[Steam|steam]] for a couple of minutes.\n| Remove from the pan. Assemble the [[Muffin|muffin]] by layering the [[Sausage meat|sausage meat]] on top of the [[Egg|egg]]. Top with [[Avocado|avocado]], and add the eggy lid.\n| You can add [http://paleopolly.com/2014/12/15/paleo-bacon-sandwich-with-ketchup/ Paleo Polly\u0092s paleo ketchup] for tomato sauce fans!\n}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Gluten free recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Debbie&andrew's sausage recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Paleolithic diet recipes]]\n{{Template:DebbieAndAndrew attribution}}\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#oliveoil #eggs #egg #sausagemeat #sausages #muffin #sausage #avocado #recipesfromothersites #cookipedia #lime </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[http://www.foodnetwork.com/diners-drive-ins-and-dives/index.html Diners, Drive-ins and Dives], my favourite cooking program.\n[[Image:Pecorino stuffed chorizo burgers_ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|That's all she wrote...]]\n\nIts basically a [[Burger|burger]] made from a mix of [[Beef mince|beef mince]] and [[Minced|minced]] [[Chorizo sausage|chorizo sausage]] stuffed with nice [[Italian cheese]].\n\nThis was a fantastic and will be made again and again!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 200g [[Chorizo sausage|chorizo sausage]]\n| 500 g [[Beef mince|beef mince]] ([[Ground beef|ground beef]])\n| 100 g [[Pecorino Romano|pecorino romano]], freshly [[Grated|grated]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Mexican oregano]]\n| [[Fresh herbs]]\n| 2 large slices of [[Bread|bread]] or a cup of [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1 large [[Egg|egg]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Blitz the [[Bread|bread]] slices to crumbs in a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade.\n| Soak the [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]] in the [[Milk|milk]] for about 15 minutes and then squeeze out any excess [[Milk|milk]].\n| Skin the [[Chorizo|chorizo]] and blitz to a [[Mince|mince]] in a [[Food processor|food processor]] with a metal blade.\n| To the [[Chorizo|chorizo]] [[Mince|mince]] in the [[Mixer|mixer]], add the [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]], [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]], the [[Egg|egg]] and the mince.\n| Blitz until combined but be careful not ro turn it into [[Pate|pate]]!\n| Divide the [[Burgers|burgers]] and the [[Cheese|cheese]] into four.\n| Using you hands, press out into large [[Burgers|burgers]] and fill with the [[Cheese|cheese]] and fold up to seal.  [[Mould]] into flat burgers.\n| Refrigerate for 30 minutes if you have the time, this seems to help firm them up and bind them together.\n| [[Grill]] for 15 minutes on a tray, not a rack, turning once. ''I think it's nice to let them cook in their own chorizo flavoured oil.''\n| [[Rest for]] a 5 minutes before serving to allow the [[Meat|meat]] to relax and the [[Cheese|cheese]] to melt properly.\n}}\n<gallery widths=270px heights=270px perrow=5>\nImage:Pecorino stuffed chorizo burgers ingredients.jpg|A few simple ingredients\nImage:Chorizo, herbs, beef mince.jpg.jpg|Minced chorizo and herbs with ground beef\nImage:Chorizo, herbs, beef mince, breadcrumbs, egg.jpg.jpg|Breadcrumbs and egg agged\nImage:Chorizo burger mince, pecorino cheese.jpg|Chorizo mince with 100g of [[pecorino cheese]]\nImage:Moulding the pattie,stage one.jpg|Filling the burger with cheese\nImage:Moulding the patttie, stage two.jpg|Folding\nImage:Mouilding the pattie, stage three.jpg|Closing the gaps\nImage:Four half-pound burgers.jpg|Four half-pounders\nImage:Pecorino stuffed chorizo burgers recipe.jpg|The best burger I've ever tasted!\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Chips|chips]], in a bun with [[Salad|salad]] leaves and sliced [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]].\n===Variations===\nI've used [[Oregano|oregano]] as the base flavour but use a little of what you fancy; [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Horseradish|horseradish]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Sage|sage]], [[Thyme|thyme]] would all make good alternatives.\n===Chef's notes===\nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n\n* http://bit.ly/rspcathinkpig\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pecorinostuffedchorizoburgers #breadcrumbs #cheese #chorizosausage #foodprocessor #egg #bread #burgers #chorizo #beefmince #mince </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

You can make these superior [[Breakfast muffins|breakfast muffins]] yourself, at home!\n\nJust the thing for an after-party [[Breakfast|breakfast]] - communal cooking at its best - we want your pictures!\n\n{{PhiladelphiaPermission}}\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4 rashers back [[Bacon|bacon]], rind removed\n| 4 [[English muffins|english muffins]] or [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]], cut in half horizontally\n| 100 g [[Philadelphia Original]]\n| 2 medium [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], sliced\n| 4 large [[Eggs|eggs]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Grill|grill]] and cook the [[Bacon|bacon]] until golden and crisp, keep warm. Fill a medium-large pan \u00be\u0092s full with water. Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and then reduce to a [[Simmer|simmer]].\n| Toast the [[Muffins|muffins]] on both sides (If using rolls and they are fresh, you may prefer not to toast them) under a preheated [[Grill|grill]] and [[Grill|grill]] the [[Tomato|tomato]] slices at the same time to warm through.\n| Spread one half of the [[Muffins|muffins]] or rolls with Philly and top the other halves with [[Tomato|tomato]] slices.\n| [[Poach]] the [[Eggs|eggs]] in the [[Simmering|simmering]] water for 2-3 minutes or until just cooked. Place two [[Muffin|muffin]] or roll halves onto each plate, serving the [[Poached eggs|poached eggs]] on the Philly half. Lay the [[Bacon|bacon]] over the top and serve.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* [http://www.philadelphia.co.uk/philadelphia3/page?siteid=philadelphia3-prd&locale=uken1&PagecRef=609&rid=9127 The Philadelphia recipe website]\n===Chef's notes===\nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n* http://bit.ly/rspcathinkpig\n==See also==\n{{OtherRecipesPhiladelphia Original}}\n\n\n* [[Eggs Benedict]]\n* [[Breakfast muffins]]\n* [[Molletes antequeranos (Antequera muffins)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Philadelphia recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Poached]]\n[[Category:Toasted]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bacon #grill #philadelphiabreakfastmuffins #breakfast #tomato #breakfastmuffins #muffins #eggs #breadrolls #simmer #boil </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Picadillo",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Picadillo a beef recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#picadillo #beef #bellpepper #tomatoes #garlic #potato #vegetables #spanishrice #unusualrecipes #browning #diced \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Picadillo is a dish mainly consisting of ground beef typically found in Puerto Rico, Cuba, Mexico, and other Latin American countries\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2856\n|PortionCalories = 476\n|DatePublished=8th December 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 10 minutes\n|CookTime = 40 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Picadillo recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Home cooking!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">We love this</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Carla_Cancio-Bello,_J.D.,_on_behalf_of_Cuban_Cuisine_UK|Carla]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nPicadillo is a dish mainly consisting of ground [[Beef|beef]] typically found in Puerto Rico, Cuba, Mexico, and other Latin American countries. In Mexico and Puerto Rico it is sometimes used as a filling, such as for [[Tacos|tacos]], and can be mixed with [[Vegetables|vegetables]]. It can also be prepared as a type of stew. In most other Latin American countries it consists of a common table from where people pick small beef pieces or other food such as [[French fries|french fries]]. The name comes from the Spanish word, \"picar\" which means \"to mince\" or \"to chop\".\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb 2 oz) of lean [[minced]] [[Beef|beef]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped\n| 4 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], chopped\n| 284 ml (&frac12; pint) [[Beef stock|beef stock]] \n| 1 large [[Green bell pepper|green bell pepper]],deseeded and chopped\n| 3 large russet [[Potato|potato]], cubed, bite size\n| 1 400 g (14.5 oz) tin [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]] together with the juice\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Oil|oil]]\n| 1/8 teaspoon [[Sea salt|sea salt]] \n| 2 tablespoons of [[Tex-Mex seasoning]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a large, heavy pan, heat the [[Oil|oil]] to medium-high heat. Add the [[Onions|onions]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] and seasoning to the pan.\n| When the [[Bell pepper|bell pepper]] starts to discolour, add to it ground [[Beef|beef]], stirring to break up large pieces and [[Brown|brown]] evenly, about 7 minutes. \n| As [[Meat|meat]] is [[Browning|browning]], add [[Potato|potato]], [[Beef|beef]] broth and [[Diced|diced]] [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]. \n| [[Simmer]] until the potato is cooked and the picadillo has thickened, stirring occasionally.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Spanish rice]] and tortilla.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Cuban recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#picadillo #beef #bellpepper #tomatoes #garlic #potato #vegetables #spanishrice #unusualrecipes #browning #diced </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

If [[Batter|batter]] looks too thick (must be thin, like a [[Crepe|crepe]] to cook the way we're accustomed) add a little bit of water.\n| Pour [[Batter|batter]] on a hot cast [[Iron|iron]] [[Griddle|griddle]] (note: with no [[Lard|lard]] of any sort, this demands a 'well-seasoned' cast-iron)\n| Let the ploye cook; you will see little holes open up, and the edges will start to curl-up. the more holes, the better your ploye\n| When you see the mixture is not liquid any more, your ploye is done; you only cook it on one side\n| To have really good ployes, you need to re-mix the [[Batter|batter]] between pours\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* Recipe from the Madawaska (Maine) based St John Valley Times kindly sent to us by Roger Ouellette\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Dry fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#batter #ployes #griddle #crepe #boiling #buckwheatpancakes #flour #dryfried #bakingpowder #iron #lard </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Jamie Oliver's Popcorn baked beans with sun dried tomatoes recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beans #sundriedtomatopaste #bakedbeans #tomatopuree #peppers #popcorn #popped #redpepper #unusualrecipes #frying #steam \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=These beans are not baked, they're popped like popcorn. Better than any tinned baked beans and only take 10 minutes from start to finish\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1557\n|PortionCalories = 778\n|DatePublished=9th November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  3 minutes\n|CookTime =  7 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Popcorn baked beans with sundried tomatoes recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Well I never!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">The oddest thing, but really good.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]]</span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Morrisons mixed bean salad.jpg|300px|thumb|right|Morrisons' mixed bean minutes from start to finish.\n\nI got the idea of [[Frying|frying]] the [[Beans|beans]] from one of Jamie Oliver's 15 minute meal TV programs but instead of making a [[Salad|salad]] I wanted to make luxury [[Baked beans|baked beans]].\n\nThis is a brilliant recipe to mess about with and is ideal for using up odd leftovers.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 400g can of [[Mixed bean salad|mixed bean salad]]\n| 1 whole bottled [[Red pepper|red pepper]], chopped and 2 tablespoons of the [[Oil|oil]] from the jar\n| [[Freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Sundried tomato paste|sundried tomato paste]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| Pinch of [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Drain the [[Beans|beans]] and rinse them a few times and allow them to drain well\n| Heat the [[Red pepper|red pepper]] [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] over a high heat\n| Add a pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] to the [[Oil|oil]] and swill it around the pan\n| Get a cover for the pan as it will spit violently when you add the [[Beans|beans]]\n| Very carefully tip the [[Beans|beans]] into the [[Frying pan|frying pan]] and cover quickly\n| Jiggle the pan to keep the [[Beans|beans]] turning over, ideally while holding the cover an inch away from the pan so they don't start to [[Steam|steam]] yet\n| After a minute or so, the [[Beans|beans]] will pop like [[Popcorn|popcorn]], crisping the skins and revealing a fluffy core\n| Once most of the [[Beans|beans]] have [[Popped|popped]] and the pan has calmed down a little, stir in the  chopped [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Sundried tomato paste|sundried tomato paste]] and [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| Mix well, reduce the heat and cover and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 3 or 4 minutes\n| If they look too dry, add a splash of liquid.  You could use water, [[Stock|stock]] , [[Wine|wine]] or [[Beer|beer]].  I used a splash of Stella [[Lager|lager]] to loosen them\n| Serve immediately\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse any variety of canned [[Beans|beans]] and practically anything you can think of.  Bottled [[Peppers|peppers]] are good because they don't require any cooking, however you could add fresh peppers for a little crunch, finely [[Chopped spring onions|chopped spring onions]], chillies, oh the list is endless!\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #sundriedtomatopaste #bakedbeans #tomatopuree #peppers #popcorn #popped #redpepper #unusualrecipes #frying #steam </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Popover",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Popover, Egg recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#popover #yorkshirepudding #muffin #flour #eggs #bake #custard #baked #batter #baking #plainflour \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A popover is a recipe of American origin. A light, hollow roll made from an egg batter similar to that used in making Yorkshire pudding\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1271\n|PortionCalories = 211\n|DatePublished=4th October 2012\n|Author = JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 - Makes 6 popovers\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Popover recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Tall Yorkies</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Doesn't really matter what you call them - theses are just tall Yorkshire puddings.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA popover is a recipe of American origin. A light, hollow roll  made from an [[Egg|egg]] [[Batter|batter]] similar to that used in making [[Yorkshire pudding]]. The name \"popover\" comes from the fact that the batter swells or \"pops\" over the top of the [[Muffin|muffin]] tin while [[Baking|baking]]. They can also be [[Baked|baked]] in individual [[Custard|custard]] cups.\n[[Image:Popover.jpg|thumb|300px|right|'''Nordic Ware popover tin''']]\n\nThese are best server directly from the [[Oven|oven]].  For authentic popovers, use a large [[Muffin|muffin]] tray rather than a [[Yorkshire pudding]] tray.\n\nRecently whilst reading John Steinbeck's ''Sweet Thursday'', I noticed a reference to '''popovers''' and wondered what they were: \n\n''Joe Elegant was a pale young man with bangs. He smoked foreign cigarettes in a long ebony holder and he cooked for the Bear Flag. The girls said he made the best '''popovers''' in the world, and he could give a massage that would shake the kinks out of a Saturday night when the fleet was in.''\n\n..hence this page.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 cup [[Milk|milk]]\n| 3 whole [[Eggs|eggs]], lightly beaten\n| 1 cup [[Plain flour|plain flour]], sifted\n| Large pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n* Allow the [[Milk|milk]] to get to room temperature\n* Sift the [[Flour|flour]]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the ingredients to a [[Food-processor|food-processor]] with a metal blade, in the following order:\n| [[Milk]]\n| [[Eggs]]\n| [[Flour]]\n| [[Salt]]\n| Pulse blend for about 35 seconds\n| Pour in to a well buttered [[Popover tray|popover]] or [[Muffin tray]]\n| [[Bake]] for 20 minutes at 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6)\n| Reduce the heat to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4) and [[Bake|bake]] for a further 10 minutes\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]] and serve immediately\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Egg recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#popover #yorkshirepudding #muffin #flour #eggs #bake #custard #baked #batter #baking #plainflour </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

title": "Pork London broil with a creamy mushroom and cucumber sauce",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pork London broil with a creamy mushroom and cucumber sauce recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#porklondonbroilwithacreamymushroomandcucumbersauce #butter #mushrooms #cucumber #blackpepper #rice #dried #dill #londonbroil #doublecream #peas \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I've added this odd sounding recipe as an aide-memoir for myself, so it can be easily repeated.  It sounds very strange but the combination worked brilliantly\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2137\n|PortionCalories = 534\n|DatePublished=28th August 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  25 minutes\n|PrepTime =  5 minutes\n|CookTime =  20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Pork London broil with a creamy mushroom and cucumber sauce recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">The Best Sauce!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Unusual, and unforgettable.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI've added this odd sounding recipe as an aide-memoir for myself, so it can be easily repeated.  It sounds very strange but the combination worked brilliantly.  The sauce is based on [[Mushrooms in a cucumber sauce|mushrooms in a cucumber sauce]], with added [[double cream]].  The [[London broil]] marinade was just a rather successful experiment. Although [[London broil]] is usually associated with beef, this worked really well with a pork fillet - even better because it was barbecued, creating a smoky, crisp finish, but remaining tender inside.\n\n\n'''Mushroom and cucumber sauce'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| A good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 50g [2 oz] [[Butter|butter]]\n| 110 g [4 oz] of oyster [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]], wiped clean and chopped\n| 1 tablespoon [15 ml] [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| Half a [[Cucumber|cucumber]], de-seeded, peeled and cubed\n| 150 ml [1/4 pint] hot [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Dill|dill]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to taste\n| 150 ml [[double cream]]\n}}\n'''London broil pork fillet'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 300g [[Pork tenderloin fillet]], sliced into 2 pieces lengthways\n| 4 tablespoons of orange juice\n| 2 tablespoons of [[dark soy sauce]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[light soy sauce]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[sherry vinegar]]\n| Pinch of [[black pepper]]\n| Pinch of [[chilli powder]]\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\nAdd the pork fillet and the marinade ingredients to a [[Lock and Lock]] box, close the lid and shake well to coat evenly. Refrigerate for up to 12 hours, turning and shaking now and then if you are able.\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add a good grind of [[Black pepper|black pepper]] to a small saucepan and melt the [[Butter|butter]]\n| [[Saut\u00e9]] the [[Mushrooms|mushrooms]] in the [[Butter|butter]] for 4 minutes, turning often\n| Add the cubed [[Cucumber|cucumber]] cubes and cook until they visibly 'wilt', about 5 minutes, stirring now and then\n| Make a [[Roux|roux]] by sprinkling  the [[Flour|flour]] over the buttery [[Cucumber|cucumber]] and [[mushrooms]] and mix well so all the [[Fat|fat]] is absorbed\n| Add the [[Dried|dried]] [[Dill|dill]] and hot [[Stock|stock]] and [[Blend|blend]] into a [[Sauce|sauce]]\n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and then reduce and [[Simmer|simmer]] for 10 minutes\n| Stir in the double cream and heat gently - don't allow it to boil or the cream will 'split'\n}}\n'''London broil pork fillet'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Drain the pork fillets and discard the marinade\n| Barbecue or grill over a fairly high heat for about 5 minutes per side\n| Check the [[meat is properly cooked]]\n| Serve\n}}\n\n===Serving suggestion===\nWe had this with [[rice]], it might be nice to add a few [[peas]] or [[beans]] to the [[rice]], just for a little colour.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#porklondonbroilwithacreamymushroomandcucumbersauce #butter #mushrooms #cucumber #blackpepper #rice #dried #dill #londonbroil #doublecream #peas </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Prawns 'n' Pepsi recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#prawnsnpepsi #sauce #garlic #prawns #fry #lime #chillies #tomatoes #pepsi #butter #onions \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The idea for this recipe came from the delightful cookbook ''Two cooks and a suitcase'' by Doug Bell & Rhoda Robertson\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1105\n|PortionCalories = 276\n|DatePublished=17th January 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Prawns 'n' Pepsi, served with [[boiled rice]]\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 50 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 35 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Prawns 'n' Pepsi dish.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Strange, but true!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.8</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">It really does work - about the only time I would bother to buy Pepsi though \ud83d\ude1b</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThe idea for this recipe came from the delightful cookbook '''''Two cooks and a suitcase''''' by Doug Bell & Rhoda Robertson, who also run the Scottish Mexican deli chain: '''Lupe Pintos Deli''' and the companion website: [http://www.lupepintos.com/ http://www.lupepintos.com/]. Both are a must for all things Mexican and much more.  The book is available from their website.\n\nThis dish is very similar in taste to the Indian dish, Garlic chilli prawns, I trust you will enjoy it\n\n'''..for the [[prawns]]..'''\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500 g (1 lb) of fresh [[peeled prawns]]\n| 25 g (1 oz) [[butter]] for [[frying]]\n| 4 cloves of [[Garlic]]\n| [[Sea salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''..for the [[sauce]]..'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Olive oil]]\n| 2 medium [[onions]], peeled and chopped\n| 2 cloves of [[Garlic]]\n| 1 large (400g) can of peeled plum [[tomatoes]], blitzed in a [[food processor]].\n| 2 tablespoons [[tomato puree]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[lime]] [[zest]]\n| 1 can or small bottle of [[Pepsi]] Original. Not lo-cal, diet or odd-flavoured versions)\n| 2 [[chipotle chillies]], finely chopped\n| 2 [[chile de Arbole]], finely chopped\n| [[Sea salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n}}\n'''..to garnish..'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| [[Wedges]] of fresh [[lime]]\n| A handful of chopped [[parsley]], finely chopped\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Prawns 'n' Pepsi reduced.jpg|the sauce...reduced\nImage:Prawns 'n' Pepsi sauce.jpg|The sauce\nImage:Prawns 'n' Pepsi recipe.jpg|Prawns 'n' Pepsi\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| '''The [[sauce]]'''\n| [[Fry]] the [[onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] for 4 minutes in a little [[olive oil]] until they are translucent\n| Add the pressed [[tomatoes]], [[tomato puree]], chopped [[chillies]], [[lime]] zest, [[Pepsi]], [[salt]] and [[pepper]] then [[simmer]] vigorously for 25 minutes or until reduced to a thick [[sauce]].\n| '''The [[prawns]]'''\n| [[Fry]] the [[Garlic|garlic]] in the [[butter]] until it takes a little colour\n| Add the [[prawns]] and [[fry]] them until they turn pink\n| Season to taste with [[salt]] and [[pepper]]\n| Mix the [[sauce]] into the [[prawns]], combine well and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[plain boiled rice]] and [[peas and peppers]]\n===Variations===\n\nIf you can afford it, try chunks of [[monkfish]] or even [[lobster]].\n\n===Any left overs?===\n\nYes? - then make [[Prawn 'n' Pepsi flan]]! \n\n===Chef's tip===\n\nIf you are using [[dried]] [[chillies]], soak them for 30 minutes in [[boiled]] water before removing the stalks and chopping.  If you are uncertain as to how hot this dish will be for you, don't add the seeds, reserve them, taste the sauce after 15 minutes and add them if you need more heat. Wear rubber gloves when handling [[chillies]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Garlic recipes]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Shellfish recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#prawnsnpepsi #sauce #garlic #prawns #fry #lime #chillies #tomatoes #pepsi #butter #onions </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pulled pork",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pulled pork, Barbecue recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#pulledpork #pork #cider #cinnamon #ground #whitewinevinegar #smokingfood #brownsugar #lemonjuice #chillipowder #gingerpowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pulled pork (carnitas) is a classic American barbecue-style dish that can just as easily be cooked in a normal domestic oven. Lots of recipes suggest\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4358\n|PortionCalories = 726\n|DatePublished=3rd August 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Oh - how I love pulled pork!\n |TotalTime = 17 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 5 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Pulled pork recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Can't stop eating this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">So moorish.  Nice in corn tortillas with sour cream.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Pulled pork''' ('''carnitas''') is a classic American [[barbecue]]-style dish that can just as easily be cooked in a normal domestic [[oven]].\n\nLots of recipes suggest adding a tablespoon of [[liquid smoke]] over the meat at the final stage.  I prefer to leave chemicals like that in the garage!  However, if you have your own [[Smoking food|smoker]], I would smoke it for an hour or so before you start the cooking process.\n\nIf you like this, you will also love the selection of pulled pork recipes at the bottom of this page.\n\nNote: This recipe needs to be prepared 24 hours in advance.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) boneless [[pork shoulder]].\n| 2 level teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Paprika|paprika]] - [[smoked paprika]] if you have it.\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] powder, freshly ground if possible - see ''Chef's notes''\n| 2 teaspoons [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] or a bunch of your favourite [[Dried|dried]] [[Chillies|chillies]], powdered\n| 2 teaspoons [[coriander seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder\n| 2 teaspoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]] \n}}\n'''Cook it over:'''\n* 450 ml [[Cider|cider]]\n'''The reduction'''\n* 1 tablespoon [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n* [[White wine vinegar]] to taste\n\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 150\u00b0 C (300\u00b0 F - gas 2)\n*If you are lucky enough to have a [[Smoking food|smoker]], smoke the joint for an hour or so.\n*Mix all of the [[Spices|spices]] together in a large [[baking tray]].\n*Slice the skin off the joint - we're not going to use it today.\n*Make random slashes all over the [[Meat|meat]].\n*Rub the [[Spice|spice]] mix all over the [[Pork|pork]] and into the cuts you've made.\n*Cover and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours.\n* 15 minutes before you are ready to start cooking, preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 150\u00b0 C (300\u00b0 F - gas 2)\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pulled pork on cider.jpg|thumb|300px|right|24 hours later, sitting over the cider, ready for the oven\nImage:Spice mix for pulled pork.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Spice mix for pulled pork\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Place the [[Pork|pork]], 'skin-side-up' on a wire rack resting on a tray full of [[Cider|cider]].  The pork must be clear of the cooking liquor.\n| Cover and seal with two layers of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] so the joint can [[Steam|steam]] in the [[Cider|cider]].\n| Cook for 4.5 hours, and don't fiddle or mess about with it!\n| After 4.5 hours, turn the heat up to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6).\n| Reserving the original tray and its juices, place the joint on its rack over a clean, dry [[roasting tray]] and [[Roast|roast]] uncovered for a further 30 minutes.\n| When the [[Pork|pork]] is cooked, use two forks to shred the pork into tiny pieces.\n| To the juices, add the final [[Sugar|sugar]], taste, and then add a splash or so of [[white wine vinegar]] to balance the flavours. Use a wooden spatula to get all of the goodness from the pan and then whisk well.\n| Tip the [[Pork|pork]] into the [[Sauce|sauce]] and heat until it is reduced to a sticky mass.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on [[Toasted|toasted]] buns with [[cole-slaw]] and buttery [[Corn on the cob|corn on the cob]].\n\n===Chef's notes===\nThe spices in this are not an exact science. If you don't have a certain spice, use something else.  Look at the individual spice links on this page or our main [[:Category:Spices|spice category]] to find similar spices that you may have instead.  If you favour a certain flavour, add more of it. Mess around, be bold!!\n\nHaving made this five or six times now, I would be inclined to leave out the [[cinnamon]] as I find the flavour somewhat overpowering.  However, it does seems to be included in most traditional recipes.\n\nI have also started to coat the pork with a good splash of [[lime]] or [[lemon juice]] before I add the rub.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n[[Category:Smoked]]\n[[Category:Smoker recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with beer]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#pulledpork #pork #cider #cinnamon #ground #whitewinevinegar #smokingfood #brownsugar #lemonjuice #chillipowder #gingerpowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Pulled pork (slow cooker recipe)",
                "revisions": [
