                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Pulled pork, a slow cooker barbecue recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#slowcooker #cider #lockandlock #gingerpowder #ground #orange #smokingfood #garlicpowder #mustardpowder #barbecue #brownsugar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Pulled pork (carnitas) is a classic American barbecue-style dish. This recipe is basically my standard pulled pork recipe, slightly adapted for a slow\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4047\n|PortionCalories = 674\n|DatePublished=10th May 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 6\n |Difficulty = 2\n |ImageComment = Served with a salad and homemade pittas.\n |TotalTime = 18 hours 15 minutes\n |PrepTime = 12 hours 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 6 hours\n |Image = [[Image:Pulled pork slow cooker.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">You can't beat pulled pork</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..and you can't beat this version either!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n'''Pulled pork''' ('''carnitas''') is a classic American [[barbecue]]-style dish.\n\nThis recipe is basically my standard [[pulled pork]] recipe, slightly adapted for a [[slow cooker]].  I've added 150 ml of [[cider]] and the flesh of 1 [[orange]], otherwise it's the same.\n\nLots of recipes suggest adding a tablespoon of [[liquid smoke]] over the meat at the final stage.  I prefer to leave chemicals like that in the garage!  However, if you have your own [[Smoking food|smoker]], I would smoke it for an hour or so before you start the cooking process.\n\nIf you like this, you will also love [[Cochinita pibil]] and [[Beer pickled belly of pork]]!\n\nNote: This recipe needs to be prepared 24 hours in advance.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) boneless [[pork shoulder]].\n| 2 level teaspoons [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Paprika|paprika]] - [[smoked paprika]] if you have it.\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cinnamon|cinnamon]] powder, freshly ground if possible - see ''Chef's notes''\n| 2 teaspoons [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[Peppercorns|peppercorns]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder in a [[Coffee grinder|coffee grinder]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] or a bunch of your favourite [[Dried|dried]] [[Chillies|chillies]], powdered\n| 2 teaspoons [[coriander seeds]], [[Ground|ground]] to a powder\n| 2 teaspoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]] \n| 250 ml [[cider]]\n| 1 [[orange]], peeled, and roughly chopped\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pulled pork slow cooker recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Use a [[Lock and Lock]] box to mix the ingredients and marinade the pork\nImage:Spice mix for pulled pork.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Spice mix for pulled pork\n</gallery>\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n*If you are lucky enough to have a [[Smoking food|smoker]], smoke the joint for an hour or so.\n*Mix all of the [[Spices|spices]] together in a large [[baking tray]].\n*Remove and discard the rind.\n*Make random slashes in the [[Meat|meat]].\n* Add all of the remaining ingredients to a large [[Lock and Lock box]] together with the pork joint.  Replace the lid and shake like mad for a minute to mix the ingredients.\n*[[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours or so, shaking the box now and then.\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the contents of the [[Lock and Lock]] box to your [[slow cooker]].\n| Cover and slow cook on medium for 8 hours - it will be good to go after 4, but really disintegrates nicely the longer you cook it.  If you are able, you could reduce to low after 4 hours too.\n| Remove the cooked pork from the slow cooker and drain and reserve the juices and return the meat to the [[slow cooker]] to keep warm.\n| Using a frying pan over a medium heat, boil the juices and reduce by about 50%, stirring now and then.  This should take about 5 minutes.\n| Pour the reduction over the cooked pork, remove from the slow cooker and use two forks to shred the pork into tiny pieces.\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with chopped salad vegetables in [[pitta breads]].\n\n===Chef's notes===\nThe spices in this are not an exact science. If you don't have a certain spice, use something else.  Look at the individual spice links on this page or our main [[:Category:Spices|spice category]] to find similar spices that you may have instead.  If you favour a certain flavour, add more of it. Mess around, be bold!!\n\nIn this recipe we are [[marinating]] the pork in the [[cider]], rather than as a dry rub so you could just as easily add 3 or 4 peeled and crushed [[cloves of garlic]] instead of the [[garlic powder]] and a thumb-sized piece of [[ginger root]], peeled and grated, instead of the [[ginger powder]].\n\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n[[Category:Smoked]]\n[[Category:Smoker recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with beer]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Barbecue recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinaded]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#slowcooker #cider #lockandlock #gingerpowder #ground #orange #smokingfood #garlicpowder #mustardpowder #barbecue #brownsugar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

However, it does not have the keeping qualities of standard jam so it is best to make it in small quantities.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 x 500g bag of [[Frozen|frozen]] [[Fruit|fruit]] of your choice, [[Defrosted|defrosted]]\n| 150g [[Sugar|sugar]] (any sort is fine, but no need for special [[Preserving sugar|preserving sugar]])\n| 1.5g [[Agar|agar agar]] (generous 1\u00bd teaspoons in powder form)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix the [[Fruit|fruit]] with the [[Sugar|sugar]] in a [[Saucepan|saucepan]] and leave for 15 minutes\n| Stir in the [[Agar|agar agar ]] \n| Bring to the [[Boil|boil]] and cook for a minute, then remove from the heat\n| Transfer to hot or warm, clean jars, before it has a chance to set in the pan\n| Once cooled, keep [[Refrigerated|refrigerated]] even if unopened\n}}\n\n===Recipe source===\nLightly adapted from a [http://www.molecule-r.com/en/content/45-quick-and-easy-jam Molecule-R] recipe\n===Chef's notes===\nKeep in the [[Fridge|fridge]] at all times and it should last a couple of weeks at least.  I [[Sterilised|sterilised]] my jars, but I am not sure that that is necessary as the [[Jam|jam]] should be used up quickly.\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Breakfast recipes]]\n[[Category:Pickles and preserves]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Molecular gastronomy recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#agar #jam #fruit #quickfruitjam #frozen #fridge #sterilised #defrosted #boiledorsimmered #boil #preservingsugar </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Refried beans recipe Cooking with chillies\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beans #onion #bacon #butter #litres #fry #refriedbeansrecipe #pints #mash #potatoricer #refriedbeans \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Refried beans are the essential ingredient for Mexican and Tex-Mex dishes. They are ideal for freezing\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1875\n|PortionCalories = 468\n|DatePublished=17th March 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 14 hours\n|PrepTime = 12 hours\n|CookTime = 2 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Refried beans.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"><span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than El Paso</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Fresher and not at all cloying or gloopy (which the tinned stuff is!)</span> \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\">[[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\n\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\n[[Refried beans]] are the essential ingredient for [[:Category:Mexican recipes|Mexican]] and [[:Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Tex-Mex]] dishes.  They are ideal for [[freezing]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 500g (1lb 2oz) [[dried]] [[pinto beans]]\n| 1.2 [[litres]] (2 [[pints]]) water\n| 1 large [[onion]], chopped\n| 250g (9oz) [[smoked]] streaky [[bacon]], finely chopped\n| 1 small [[fresh red chili]], deseeded and finely chopped\n| 2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n| knob of [[butter]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Soak the [[beans]] overnight in plenty of water.  Drain and re-rinse.\n| [[Boil]] the [[beans]] in 1.2 [[litres]] (2 [[pints]]) of water boil until tender. Reserve the cooking water.\n| In a large [[frying]] pan or [[wok]], heat the [[oil]] and [[butter]] and [[fry]] the the [[onion]] until soft.\n| Add the [[bacon]] and [[fry]] it until cooked, but not crispy.\n| [[Mash]] the [[beans]], a [[potato ricer]] or [[Potato masher|masher]] is good for this,  then mix them with the [[fried]] [[bacon]] and [[onion]].\n| Stir in a little of the reserved cooking water so the [[beans]] are the same consistency as [[double cream]].\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot as a [[side dish]] or as an ingredient in your recipe.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beans #onion #bacon #butter #litres #fry #refriedbeansrecipe #pints #mash #potatoricer #refriedbeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker",
                "revisions": [

                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Proper roast chicken, cooked only in a slow cooker / crockpot recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #aluminiumfoil #roastingachickeninaslowcooker #slowcooker #onion #oliveoil #freshherbs #tacoseasoning #heart #smokedpaprikapowder #liver \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I didn't think that this would be possible until I read Julia's blog, she is always coming up with innovative ideas! What a great use for a slow cooker / crockpot\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1117\n|PortionCalories = 279\n|DatePublished=19th June 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = After 8 hours it looks and smells divine!\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  8 hours, 10 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  8 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Unbelievable</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Until I tried this, I did not believe it would be possible.   I wish I had been able to this when I had my first bed-sit!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nI didn't think that this would be possible until I read [[:Category:I believe I can fry recipes|Julia's blog]], she is always coming up with innovative ideas!\n\nWhat a great use for a [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]], go out to work in the morning and come back to [[Roast|roast]] [[Chicken|chicken]]!\n\nI've used my own variation of Julia's [[Marinade|marinade]] rub.  You can invent your own, all you need is a little imagination.  At the very least, you should rub the skin with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and a little [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 whole raw [[Chicken|chicken]] - if it has been [[Frozen|frozen]], ensure that it is completely [[Defrosted|defrosted]].\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], un peeled, cut into quarters\n| A few sprigs of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] of choice (if available)\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n}}\n'''rub'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon fine [[Salt|salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[chilli powder]] \n| &#189; teaspoon [[Smoked paprika powder|smoked paprika powder]] (optional)\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried mixed herbs|dried mixed herbs]]\n| Plenty of [[aluminium foil]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Random recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Unbelievable</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Until I tried this, I did not believe it would be possible.   I wish I had been able to this when I had my first bed-sit!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker - ready to cook.jpg|Ready to start cooking\nImage:Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker - tin foil, rub and stuffing.jpg|Slow cooker lined with aluminium foil, rub ingredients and onion and herbs\nImage:Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker - no tin foil.jpg|No aluminium foil? a lattice of spoons does just as well\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Scrunch up the [[aluminium foil]] into 8 loose balls, line the base of the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] with these.\n| These will keep the [[Chicken|chicken]] from sitting in the cooking juices, so we get a [[Dry roast|dry roast]].\n| Remove and discard the innards, if any ([[Heart|heart]], [[Liver|liver]], neck etc)\n| Remove the [[Parson's nose|parson's nose]].\n| Rinse inside and out with cold-running water and pat dry using [[Paper towels|paper towels]].\n| Drop the quartered [[Onion|onion]] into the cavity together with any [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] you may have to [[Hand|hand]].\n| Mix the rub ingredients together in a small bowl.\n| Using you hands, massage the [[Oil|oil]] all over the [[Chicken|chicken]]'s skin.\n| Cover the [[Chicken|chicken]] with the rub so it is really well coated.\n| Sit the [[Chicken|chicken]] (breast upwards) gently on the [[aluminium foil]], taking care not to crush it.\n| Set the [[slow cooker]] to low and leave to cook for 8 hours.  It won't hurt if it's left for a little longer.\n| Check the chicken has reached a [[safe cooking temperature]] [74 \u00b0C (165 \u00b0F)]\n}}\n===Variations===\nUse a packet of [[Taco seasoning]] as a rub for the [[Chicken|chicken]] or make your own here: [[Tex-Mex seasoning]]\n===Chef's notes===\nI would start with a medium sized chicken unless you are sure that a large chicken will fit.  We have a large Morphy Richards 6.5 litre slow cooker and a small chicken fitted easily, but I'm not so sure that a large one would fit.\n\n'''A little more environmentally friendly:''' Revisiting this recipe, the reason for the [[aluminium foil]] is just to stop the [[chicken]] overcooking should it make contact with the [[crockpot]]. It seems rather wasteful to use so much [[aluminium foil]] and then chuck it away afterwards so I looked for an alternative.  An ovenproof plate would be good but it has to be surprisingly small to fit in a slow cooker.  After a few experiments, a lattice of spoons worked the best. I still use a ball of [[aluminium foil]] on each side to hold the legs away from the edge of a cooker.\n\nYou could also rest the chicken on some [[carrots]], [[parsnips]] and [[onions]] which would serve the same purpose.\n==See also==\n* www.ibelieveicanfry.com/2013/04/slow-cooker-rotisserie-chicken.html\n* http://www.paleocupboard.com/slow-cooker-rotisserie-chicken.html\n* [[Slow cooker chicken (slow cooker recipe)]]\n* [[Roasting a turkey in a slow cooker]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:I believe I can fry recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #aluminiumfoil #roastingachickeninaslowcooker #slowcooker #onion #oliveoil #freshherbs #tacoseasoning #heart #smokedpaprikapowder #liver </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Roasting a chicken on a beer can (Modernist Cuisine)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roasting a chicken on a beer can (Modernist Cuisine) recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#chicken #beercan #bake #beercanchicken #roastingachickenonabeercanmodernistcuisine #equipment #modernistcuisine #rosemary #thighs #sage #herbs \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The technique here is basically to flay the chicken and then to cook the chicken very slowly, afterwards, baking very quickly on a high heat\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1070\n|PortionCalories = 267\n|DatePublished=29th November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = After 4 hours plus the browning stage\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  5 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Roasting a chicken on a beer can Modernist Cuisine recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Beer in the butt chicken</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.9</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Almost the perfect meal</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Roasting a chicken on a beer can Modernist Cuisine 4hours.jpg|thumb|300px|right|After baking for 4 hours]]\nI've cooked [[Beer can chicken|beer can chicken]] many, many times and even cooked [[Beer can turkey|beer can turkey]] for Christmas dinner 3 years in a row so after reading ''[[Modernist Cuisine]]. The Art and Science of Cooking, Volume 1: Volume 2 - Volume 2 - Techniques and [[Equipment]]'' ISBN 978-0982761007, I was interested to try the approach they used there.\n\nThe technique is basically to flay the [[Chicken|chicken]] (separate the skin from the flesh) , cook the chicken very slowly and then to [[Bake|bake]] quickly at an intense heat to crisp the skin.\n\nI've modified their recipe slightly by adding a rub of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], and adding a large bunch of herbs to the empty beer can and just putting 120 ml of water into the beer can so the herbs don't burn and the chicken gets a little extra moisture.\n\nAs with most of the [[Molecular gastronomy]] recipes, they are rather involved or take longer than normal though it is generally worth the extra effort.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 x 1.7 kg [3.7 lb] whole [https://www.cookipedia.co.uk/calories/chicken/bq/11#jump chicken chicken]\n| 1 tablespoon of [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Old India Taco Seasoning]]\n| A large bunch of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]], [[Thyme|thyme]], [[Sage|sage]] and [[Rosemary|rosemary]]\n| 120 ml water\n| Empty [[Beer can|beer can]]\n| [[Grillpro Stainless Steel Chicken Roaster]] (optional)\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 100\u00b0 C (225\u00b0 F - gas \u00bc) or even lower if your oven will allow\n| Remove the [[Parson's nose|parson's nose]]\n| Starting from either end, separate the skin of the [[Chicken|chicken]] from the flesh, leaving it completely intact, being careful not to tear the skin.  When you have finished, the skin should hang from the chicken like a baggy jumper.\n| I found a very large flat spoon ideal to do this.\n| Leave the skin connected to the wings and the tips of the [[Drumsticks|drumsticks]].\n| Cut a small hole in the skin at the bottom of each leg so any juices can drain. each \n| Empty the [[Beer can|beer can]] or find a volunteer to do this for you :-)\n| Pop the [[Herbs|herbs]] into the empty [[Beer can|beer can]] and add 120 ml of water.\n| If you have a [[Grillpro Stainless Steel Chicken Roaster]],  put the can on this and sit the [[Chicken|chicken]] on the roaster.  If you don't have one, put the [[Beer can|beer can]] on a [[Roasting tray|roasting tray]] and very carefully sit the chicken on the [[Beer|beer]] can.\n| Nathan Myhrvold also suggests cutting a hole in the butt, however, the way I've flayed my [[Chicken|chicken]] that is not necessary.\n| [[Bake]] the [[Chicken|chicken]] to a core temperature of 60\u00b0 C (140\u00b0 F) when measured with a [[Digital thermometer|digital thermometer]].  This will probably take around 4 hours.\n| When core temperature has been reached, remove the bird from the [[Oven|oven]] and set to one side.\n| Set the [[Oven|oven]] to its highest temperature and let it heat for 20 minutes.\n| Make a little 'hat' of [[tin-foil]] to sit over the uppermost part of the chicken to enable even [[browning]] ands return the [[Chicken|chicken]] to the [[Oven|oven]] and [[Bake|bake]] until the skin is crisp and golden.\n| This should take around 15 to 20 minutes, but watch it like a hawk or you will have a burnt, [[Smoking|smoking]] [[Chicken|chicken]].\n| Remove from the [[Oven|oven]], carve and serve immediately\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n\n* The Art and Science of Cooking, Volume 1: Volume 2 - Volume 2 - Techniques and [[Equipment]]'' ISBN 978-0982761007, Nathan Myhrvold with Chris Young and Maxime Bilet\n===Variations===\nBy adjusting the core temperature you can cook your preferred [[Meat|meat]] so it is at its best.\n\nFor juicy, tender white [[Meat|meat]] (the breast), use a core temperature of 60\u00b0 C (140\u00b0 F)\n\nFor succulent [[Brown|brown]] [[Meat|meat]] (legs and [[Thighs|thighs]]) aim for 65\u00b0 C (150\u00b0 F)\n\nMake these adjustments by leaving the door slightly ajar.\n\n===Chef's notes===\nAfter making this, I have to say that it was brilliant, really moist and juicy, however, that goes for any [[beer can chicken]], this distinct disadvantage of this method is that it is because of the variations in cooking time, it's not as easy to produce the finished dish at a very specific time.  I will still be cooking my beer can chickens the way I always done.\n{{Template:Beercan chicken -  See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Molecular gastronomy recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #beercan #bake #beercanchicken #roastingachickenonabeercanmodernistcuisine #equipment #modernistcuisine #rosemary #thighs #sage #herbs </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

title": "Roasting a turkey in a slow cooker",
                "revisions": [

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roasting a turkey in a slow cooker recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#turkey #slowcooker #foil #onion #bacon #baking #freshherbs #roastingaturkeyinaslowcooker #stock #oliveoil #garlic \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=You wouldn't believe this recipe was possible until you try it.  A brilliant way to cook poultry, no one would know it wasn't oven cooked\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 4185\n|PortionCalories = 1046\n|DatePublished=24th November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  10 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  10 hours\n|Image = [[Image:Roasting a turkey in a slow cooker recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Brilliant idea!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I didn't think this would work until I tried it.  It's great if you don't have access to an oven and it tasted as good as it looked.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nOk, I admit that it's not possible to [[Roast|roast]] a whole [[Turkey|turkey]] in a [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] unless it is ''very small''.  However it is perfectly possible to slow cook a turkey crown, turkey breast or a turkey leg.\n\nIn the UK our local supermarket (Morrisons) sell a 1600g [3.5 lb] [[Turkey|turkey]] leg, separated into two pieces for just \u00a34.50, compared to \u00a324 for a turkey crown.  The leg is ideal for prolonged cooking and it '''''will''''' [[Roast|roast]] in the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]].\n\nI've used a massive amount of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]] from our garden to give this joint masses of flavour.\n\nThe [[Roasting|roasting]] occurs because the [[Turkey|turkey]] is kept out of the [[Stock|stock]] by sitting it on 5 or 6 balls of scrunched up [[Baking|baking]] [[Foil|foil]], a large [[Onion|onion]], halved and a bed of [[Herbs|herbs]].  I've used 500 ml of stock and 6 rashers of streaky [[Bacon|bacon]] to prevent the turkey from [[Drying|drying]] out. Plus some [[Garlic|garlic]] for extra flavour.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1.6kg [1lb 8oz] [[Turkey|turkey]] leg (separated)\n| 6 rashers of streaky [[Bacon|bacon]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], unpeeled and cut into two halves\n| 5 [[Cloves of garlic|cloves of garlic]], unpeeled and smashed under the flat of a knife\n| Large pinch of [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]]\n| Large bunch of [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]]. ([[Sage|sage]], [[Rosemary|rosemary]], [[Thyme|thyme]], etc). I also added the remains of a bunch of [[Dill|dill]]\n| [[Olive oil]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* [[Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker]] - [[Tin foil|tin foil]], rub and [[Stuffing|stuffing]].jpg\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Roast turkey and trimmings.jpg|Served with [[roast potatoes]] and [[roasted vegetables]] that were cooked in a conventional oven\nImage:Cooking turkey leg in a slow cooker prepped.jpg|Prepped and ready for 10 hours of slow cooking\nImage:Cooking turkey leg in a slow cooker ingredients.jpg|The basic ingredients - all that turkey for \u00a34.50!\nImage:Roasting a turkey leg in a slow cooker - tin foil balls.jpg|Scrunch up the baking foil into small balls to give the turkey some support and keep it dry so it can roast\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Loosely scrunch up 5 or 6 balls of [[Baking|baking]] [[Foil|foil]] and place in the base of the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]]\n| Arrange the [[Onion|onion]] halves where they will provide the best support for the [[Turkey|turkey]] leg\n| Distribute the smashed [[Garlic|garlic]] in the base of the [[Cooker|cooker]] and make a bed with your [[Fresh herbs|fresh herbs]]\n| Make up 500 ml ( almost a pint) of [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]] and pour this into the base of the [[Cooker|cooker]]\n| Lay the [[Turkey|turkey]] leg on the bed of [[Herbs|herbs]] and drizzle with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and sprinkle with the [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Lay the rashers of streaky [[Bacon|bacon]] over the leg\n| Loosely cover with a sheet of [[Baking|baking]] [[Foil|foil]]\n| Pop the lid on and slow cook on low for 10 hours\n| You could prepare this the night before and set the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] on a timer if you wanted to have this in the middle of the day\n| Discard the bacon rashers as they will now be tasteless, all their flavour has gone into the turkey and the stock.\n| Use the [[Stock|stock]] as [[Gravy|gravy]], thickening it with a tablespoon of [[gravy granules]] or few teaspoons of [[Cornflour|cornflour]] if needed\n| Carve and serve!\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with [[Roast potatoes|roast potatoes]] and all the trimmings\n==See also==\n\n* [[Roasting a chicken in a slow cooker]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooked]]\n[[Category:Cookery cheats]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#turkey #slowcooker #foil #onion #bacon #baking #freshherbs #roastingaturkeyinaslowcooker #stock #oliveoil #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Roast turkey with apricot chardonnay glaze recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#turkey #foil #apricot #baste #roastturkeywithapricotchardonnayglaze #garlic #sage #preserves #pastry #stuffing #unusualrecipes \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This seasonal roast turkey recipe comes from Woodbridge Chardonnay\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 10852\n|PortionCalories = 1085\n|DatePublished=14th November 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = 10 people\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 4 hours 10 minutes \n|PrepTime = 40 minutes \n|CookTime = 3 hours 30 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Turkey with Apricot Chardonnay recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fancy-pants turkey!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Gravy is cheaper!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:NonLoggedInUser|NonLoggedInUser]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis seasonal roast turkey recipe comes from [https://www.facebook.com/WoodbridgeByRobertMondavi Woodbridge Chardonnay].  It uses Woodbrigde Chardonnay for the unique glaze.  It is ideal for Thanksgiving and Christmas.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 4kg [10 lb] Butterball [[Turkey|turkey]]\n}}\n''''External [[Turkey|turkey]] seasoning:''''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| &frac14; cup [[Canola|canola]]/[[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] to season entire bird\n| 1 large piece [[Foil|foil]]\n}}\n'''Internal [[Turkey|turkey]] seasoning:'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 bunch fresh [[Sage|sage]]\n| 2 whole [[Garlic|garlic]] bulbs,\n| 1 large piece [[Foil|foil]]\n}}\n'''[[Apricot]] Chardonnay Glaze:'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1&frac12; cups of Woodbridge Chardonnay\n| 1 cup [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Apricot|apricot]] [[Preserves|preserves]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Lemon zest|lemon zest]] (optional)\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n* Wash hands\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n}}\n'''the [[Turkey|turkey]]'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Thoroughly rinse [[Turkey|turkey]] with water.\n| Remove innards and neck; pat dry with clean paper towels.\n| Place [[Turkey|turkey]] breast up in a large, stable [[Roasting pan|roasting pan]].\n| Tuck wings back to prevent burning.\n| Neatly tie legs together with butcher\u0092s twine.\n| Massage [[Turkey|turkey]] with [[Oil|oil]], making sure to coat evenly.\n| Season entire bird, including internal cavity, with [[Sea Salt|sea salt]].\n| Place [[Sage|sage]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] bulbs inside (optional).\n| Loosely cover just the top of [[Turkey|turkey]] with [[Foil|foil]].\n| Place [[Turkey|turkey]] on bottom [[Oven|oven]] rack.\n| Set timer accordingly.\n| Remove [[Foil|foil]] and [[Baste|baste]] [[Turkey|turkey]] with pan juices approx. every 45 min.\n| When [[Turkey|turkey]] is &frac34; cooked, remove [[Foil|foil]] and [[Baste|baste]] with [[Apricot]] Chardonnay Glaze.\n| Place back inside [[Oven|oven]] and let crisp up during remaining time.\n| Safe internal temperature is 180\u00b0F (82\u00b0 C) deep in the thigh\u0097juices should run clear, not pink.\n| If stuffed, temperature should be 165\u00b0F (74\u00b0 C) in center of [[Stuffing|stuffing]].\n| When bird is done, allow it to stand for 15 min. to release juices before serving.\n}}\n'''the glaze'''\n{{RecipeMethod\n| In a medium saucepan over medium-low heat, add Chardonnay, [[Sugar|sugar]], and [[Apricot|apricot]] [[Preserves|preserves]].\n| Cook down, stirring occasionally until thick (approx. 30 min.).\n| When [[Turkey|turkey]] is &frac34; cooked, evenly [[Baste|baste]] with glaze using a [[Pastry|pastry]] [[Brush|brush]].\n| Remove [[Foil|foil]] from top of bird and finish cooking.\n}}\n===Recipe source===\n* Woodbridge chardonnay\n==See also==\n* [https://www.facebook.com/WoodbridgeByRobertMondavi Woodbridge chardonnay (Facebook page)]\n* [[Meat cooking time calculator Imperial]]\n* [[Meat cooking time calculator Metric]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Australian recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#turkey #foil #apricot #baste #roastturkeywithapricotchardonnayglaze #garlic #sage #preserves #pastry #stuffing #unusualrecipes </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Cover until needed.\n| Heat a [[Frying pan|frying pan]] with a dash of [[Oil|oil]] and add the patties, cooking for two to three minutes each side, and cook through in a hot [[Oven|oven]] for 5 minutes. Repeat with remaining [[Muffins|muffins]].\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nSeparating the [[Muffins|muffins]]: Use a fork instead of a knife (this keeps the inside fluffy) to separate the [[Muffin|muffin]]. On rare occasion, it is referred to as \"[[Vodka]] and Orange\". While the basic drink is simply the two ingredients, there are many variations, many of these with multiple names, that can be found all over the world.\n\nThe earliest written reference to the Screwdriver is from the October 24, 1949 issue of Time:\n\"In the dimly lighted bar of the sleek Park Hotel, Turkish intelligence agents mingle with American engineers and Balkan refugees, drinking the latest Yankee concoction of [[Vodka|vodka]] and [[Orange juice|orange juice]], called a 'screwdriver'.\"\n\nThe [[Drink|drink]] reportedly got its name because American petroleum engineers in Saudi Arabia secretly added [[Vodka|vodka]] to small cans of [[Orange juice|orange juice]] and stirred the mixture with their screwdrivers.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5 oz [[Vodka]]\n| 6 oz fresh [[Orange juice|orange juice]]\n\n}}\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add the [[Vodka|vodka]] to an ice filled [[Highball glass|highball glass]]\n| Top up with [[Orange juice|orange juice]]\n}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Drink and beverage recipes]]\n\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#vodka #orangejuice #drink #highballglass </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Shortcake sponge baskets with diplomat cream and fruit",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Shortcake sponge baskets with diplomat cream and fruit recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#butter #fridge #gelatine #icingsugar #boil #airtightcontainer #foil #cherries #castersugar #saucepan #cream \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I would advise making these over two days. Each component will keep well in the fridge for 3 days at least. You will need a special tin to make the..\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3554\n|PortionCalories = 592\n|DatePublished=19th April 2016\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 6\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime = 1 hour\n|PrepTime = 40 minutes \n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Shortcake baskets with diplomat cream and fruit recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nice creamy filling</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Never knew this was called 'Diplomat cream'!</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n\nI would advise making these over two days. Each component will keep well in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for 3 days at least.\n\nYou will need a special tin to make the baskets. I used Nordic Ware's Shortcake Basket Tin and not sure if anyone else makes them. They can be got from [https://www.amazon.co.uk/Nordic-Ware-Platinum-Shortcake-Basket/dp/B000Q7QI3U?ie=UTF8&psc=1&redirect=true&ref_=oh_aui_detailpage_o03_s00 Amazon]\n{{RecipeIngredients\n}}\n====For the Shortcake Sponge:====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 150g [[Plain flour|plain flour]], sieved with\n| 1.5 teaspoons [[Baking powder|baking powder]]\n| 1/4 teaspoons [[Salt|salt]]\n| 140g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]]\n| 1 [[free range egg]]\n| 1/2 a teaspoon of [[Vanilla|vanilla]] or other extract of your choice\n| 150g softened [[Butter|butter]]\n}}\n====For the Cr\u00e8me P\u00e2tissi\u00e8re ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 4g leaf [[Gelatine|gelatine]] (optional) \u2013 the 'set' version only\n| 50g [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]]\n| 60g [[Caster Sugar|caster sugar]]\n| 25g [[Cornflour|cornflour]]\n| 250g [[Milk|milk]]\n| 25g [[Butter|butter]]\n}}\n====For the Cr\u00e8me Chantilly====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 200g [[Double Cream|double cream]] (chilled)\n| 40g [[Icing Sugar|icing sugar]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Vanilla extract|vanilla extract]]\n}}\n====To finish====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 36 [[Cherries]] or other small [[Fruit|fruit]] as desired\n| 15g [[Icing Sugar|icing sugar]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n}}\n====For the Shortcake Sponge:====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Pre-heat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180C / 350F / Gas 4 (see [[Chef's notes|chef's notes]] below for fan oven instructions)\n| Mix all of the ingredients together.\n| Beat for 2 minutes using a medium speed\n| Taste and add more [[Vanilla|vanilla]] etc extract if necessary\n| Grease the tin with melted [[Butter|butter]] and lightly dust with [[Flour|flour]]. If using the Nordic Ware tin, I suggest you paint the butter on with a [[Pastry|pastry]] [[Brush|brush]] to make sure you get into all the crevices.\n| Divide the mixture into the 6 moulds. If you fill to the last basket market, that should be about right.\n| [[Bake]] for about 20 minutes.\n| Leave in the tin for 10 minutes, then turn out onto a [[Cooling rack|cooling rack]] and allow to go completely cold.\n| The sponges should have an interior texture of a cross between normal sponge [[Cake|cake]] and a nicely [[Baked|baked]] scone. Do not expect them to be like a Victoria [[Sandwich]] as that type of sponge won\u00c2\u2019t be strong enough to hold the filling.\n| When cold, reserve the sponges until ready for use. They can go into an [[Airtight container|airtight container]] in the [[Fridge|fridge]] if necessary.\n}}\n====For the Cr\u00e8me  Diplomate (This will probably make more than you need)====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| This is made in two parts \u2013 the Cr\u00e8me P\u00e2tissi\u00e8re and the Cr\u00e8me Chantilly \u2013 which are then mixed together. You can either make it a 'set' version or an 'unset' one. The 'set' one requires the use of [[Gelatine|gelatine]] to set the Cr\u00e8me P\u00e2tissi\u00e8re, but I chose to do the 'unset' one, being a [[Vegetarian|vegetarian]]. It may be possible to use [[Agar|agar]]-agar as a setting agent, but this will need some experimentation because agar behaves differently to gelatine. I would make the Cr\u00e8me P\u00e2tissi\u00e8re first as that need to cool.\n}}\n====For the Cr\u00e8me P\u00e2tissi\u00e8re ====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Hydrate the [[Gelatine|gelatine]] (if using).\n| Beat the [[Egg yolks|egg yolks]] with the [[Sugar|sugar]].\n| Whisk in the [[Cornflour|cornflour]].\n| Bring the [[Milk|milk]] to the [[Boil|boil]] in a [[Saucepan|saucepan]], the pour half of the milk over the [[Egg|egg]] mixture.\n| Whisk, return to the [[Saucepan|saucepan]] and heat, whisking thoroughly.\n| As the mixture thickens, carry on whisking.\n| When it returns to the [[Boil|boil]], cook for 45 seconds and remove from the heat.\n| Whisk in the [[Gelatine|gelatine]] (if using) and the [[Butter|butter]].\n| Cover and leave to cool.\n}}\n====For the Cr\u00e8me Chantilly====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Whisk all of the ingredients in a chilled bowl until it has thickened.\n| Do not over-whisk or you will end up with sweet [[Butter|butter]].\n| Cover the bowl and keep in the [[Fridge|fridge]] until needed.\n}}\n====To mix the two====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Whisk the cold Cr\u00e8me P\u00e2tissi\u00e8re.\n| Whisk in one-third of the Cr\u00e8me Chantilly, until smooth.\n| Fold in the remaining [[Cream|cream]] with a [[Spatula|spatula]].\n| Store in an [[Airtight container|airtight container]] the [[Fridge|fridge]] until needed, although it is easier to work with if used immediately\n}}\n====Assembly====\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Fill the sponge cases with the Diplomat Cream \u2013 if you have made the unset version, just [[Pile|pile]] it in. For set version, you can use a [[Piping bag|piping bag]].\n| Arrange [[Cherries|cherries]] or [[Fruit|fruit]] of your choice on the [[Cream|cream]].\n| Sprinkle with a little [[Icing Sugar|icing sugar]].\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\nIt is likely that you will have some of the Diplomat Cream left over.  This can be [[Frozen|frozen]] and used in other recipes.\n\nIf using a fan [[Oven|oven]] which does not allow the fan to be switched off, do the following:\n\nOnce you have put the mixture into the moulds, wrap some [[Tin foil|tin foil]] around the [[Baking|baking]] in. The sponges need to be protected from the fan, but you don\u00c2\u2019t want the [[Foil|foil]] to touch them. I made a sort of tent over the top, which helped to keep it free of the mixture and if possible, enclose the whole [[Baking tin|baking tin]] with foil, so that the fan doesn\u00c2\u2019t dry up the sponges.\n\nPlace in a COLD [[Oven|oven]], below the middle, but not at the bottom.\n\nSwitch the [[Oven|oven]] on to 160C and [[Bake|bake]] for about 35 minutes (!).\n\nRemove the [[Foil|foil]] and check that they are cooked. If not they can go back in without the foil covering.\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Sweets and desserts]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Fruit recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#butter #fridge #gelatine #icingsugar #boil #airtightcontainer #foil #cherries #castersugar #saucepan #cream </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

title": "Sincronizada recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sincronizada recipe Cheese, from Cookipedia.Co.Uk\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#cheese #ham #quesadillas #tortillas #sincronizadarecipe #flourtortillas #tortilla #sandwich #grilled #masa #cheddar \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=In Mexican cuisine, the sincronizada is a tortilla-based sandwich\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2455\n|PortionCalories = 1227\n|DatePublished=21st January 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 2\n |Difficulty = 1\n |ImageComment = A \"sincronizada\", cut into wedges\n |TotalTime = 25 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Sincronizada recipe recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Cheese tortilla sandwich</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.7</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I like mine with extra chillies!</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n\n}}\nIn [[Mexican Cuisine|Mexican cuisine]], the sincronizada is a [[Tortilla|tortilla]]-based [[Sandwich|sandwich]]. They are frequently confused with [[Quesadillas|quesadillas]], due to their resemblance to \"quesadillas\" sold in the United States. (U.S. quesadillas are usually made with [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]] rather than molded from [[Masa|masa]] in the [[Mexican]] style).\n\nSincronizadas (so called because the top and bottom [[Tortilla|tortilla]] are \"synchronized\" together) [[Sandwich|sandwich]] ingredients between two [[Tortillas|tortillas]]. The sandwich is then [[Grilled|grilled]].\n\n=== The difference between Sincronizadas & [[quesadillas]] ===\n''This is only a rough guide, there are many, many regional differences.''\n* Sincronizadas usually include [[Ham|ham]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually made with [[Wheat flour|wheat flour]] [[tortillas]]\n* Sincronizadas are usually served flat, cut into segments\n* [[Quesadillas]] are usually made with [[corn tortillas]], though can be made with [[flour tortillas]]\n* As well as [[cheese]], [[Quesadillas]] can often contain, meat, [[refried beans]] and vegetables.\n* [[Quesadillas]] are often rolled before serving.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 4 soft [[Flour tortillas|flour tortillas]]\n| 1 cup [[Grated|grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]].\n| 70g strong [[Cheddar]]. ''Original recipes suggest [[Oaxaca cheese]] or [[Monterey Jack cheese]]''.\n| 4 slices of thinly sliced [[Ham|ham]] or [[Prosciutto|prosciutto]], cut into strips\n| 2 red [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], de-seeded and thinly sliced (or to taste)\n|* You can use [[Chilli|chilli]] [[Sauce|sauce]] instead if you prefer\n| A few thinly cut slices of fresh [[Tomato|tomato]]\n| A few rings of thinly sliced [[Onions|onions]]\n| A handful of [[Coriander|coriander]] or [[Parsley leaves|parsley leaves]], chopped finely\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Lay two of the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] side-by-side on a flat surface and sprinkle with half of the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Layer the half of [[Ham|ham]] on to the [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Distribute the remaining ingredients apart from the [[Cheese|cheese]] and [[Ham|ham]]\n| Top with the remaining [[Ham|ham]] and [[Cheese|cheese]]\n| Complete the 'sandwiches' by covering with the [[Tortillas|tortillas]]\n| On a [[Griddle|griddle]] or a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]], cook the sincronizadas, one at-a-time until the [[Tortillas|tortillas]] are lightly [[Browned|browned]] and starting to become crispy, turning once\n| Cut each sincronizada into 6 quadrants\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe hot with [[Guacamole|guacamole]] and a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n===Variations===\nChange the [[Cheddar cheese]] for a Mexican type of cheese that is called [[Oaxaca cheese|\"quesillo/queso oaxaca\"]] which can be easily torn into thinner strands and melts faster. \n\nI usually put some mayonnaise on the tortillas then the ham,cheese, a bit of fried beans, and cover it with the other tortilla with mayonnaise and another slice of ham. -- [[User:Pepekike]] 04:28, 21 July 2011 \n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n* [[Talk:Sincronizada_recipe|Visitor comments]] relating to this recipe\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code I feel like a movie star eating this.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nA Sloppy Joe is an American dish of [[Ground beef|ground beef]], [[Onions|onions]], sweetened [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]] or [[Ketchup|ketchup]] and other seasonings, served on a hamburger bun. Contradictory lore suggests that the Original Sloppy Joe [[Sandwich]] was invented at Sloppy Joe's Bar in Key West, Florida, or by a cook named Joe at a cafe in Sioux City, Iowa, as a variation of the popular \"loose meat\" sandwich (which does not contain [[Tomato|tomato]] [[Sauce|sauce]]).\n\nThere are numerous variations of this recipe, this is my favourite.  I add lots more [[chilli]] so it becomes [[chilli con carne]] in a roll.\n===Other names===\nSloppy joes can also referred to as:\n* ''Yip Yips'' in Southern Illinois near St Louis. \n* ''Yum Yums'' in parts of the Midwest USA, particularly in Nebraska\n* ''Wimpies'' in parts of the Northeast USA, especially Northeastern Pennsylvania\n* ''Slushburgers'' in parts of the Upper Midwest, particularly in Eastern Montana and Western North Dakota\n* ''Barbecues'' in other areas of the Upper Midwest, and also in some parts of Southeastern Pennsylvania.\n* ''Taverns'' in parts of northwest Iowa and Minnesota.\n* ''Sloppy Janes'' in parts of central Minnesota.\n* '' Steamers'' in parts of Virginia, West Virginia, and Maryland.\n* ''Gulash'' (not to be confused with [[Goulash]]) in parts of the Upper Midwest.\n* ''Dynamites'' in northern Rhode Island.\n* ''Manwich'' in parts of Northern New Jersey, after the popular name brand sauce, as a distinction from the local variant also known as a \"sloppy joe\"\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tablespoon [[Olive oil|olive oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n| 450 g (1 lb) [[Minced beef|minced beef]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], chopped\n| 1 small [[Sweet pepper|sweet pepper]], chopped\n| 4 tablespoons of [[Tomato|tomato]] pur\u00e9e\n| 1 tablespoon [[Worcestershire sauce]]\n| 142 ml (&frac14; pint) water\n| 2 [[Cloves garlic, peeled and crushed|cloves garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried oregano|dried oregano]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Brown sugar|brown sugar]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Ground cumin|ground cumin]]\n| &#189; teaspoon [[Cider vinegar|cider vinegar]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n'''to serve:'''\n* 4 [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]], halved\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat the [[Oil|oil]] in a large [[Frying pan|frying pan]] or [[Wok|wok]] to medium/high and [[Brown|brown]] the [[Minced beef|minced beef]] for 5 minutes.\n| Lower the heat to medium, add the [[Peppers|peppers]], [[Onions|onions]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] and [[Stir-fry|stir-fry]] for a further 5 minutes.  Drain any excess [[Fat|fat]] at this stage.\n| Mix the remaining ingredients with the water and add to the pan.\n| Cook for 10 minutes or until thickened enough to just about hold together.\n| Spoon on to lightly [[Toasted|toasted]] [[Bread rolls|bread rolls]]\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe on their own or with one or two of the following:\n* [[Chips]]\n* [[Green salad]]\n* [[Tomato & onion salad]]\n* [[Red onion and orange salad]]\n* [[Fennel, red onion and orange salad]]\n* [[Cole-slaw|cole-slaw]]\n* [[Sour cream]]\n===See also===\n* {{ChiliConCarne}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#sloppyjoerecipe #mincedbeef #onions #tomato #breadrolls #oliveoil #chillipowder #groundbeef #peppers #sourcream #garlic </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Sous vide barbecue short ribs",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Sous vide barbecue short ribs recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#shortribs #marinade #sousvidebarbecueshortribs #slowcooking #chocolate #sousvidecooking #fat #peas #pasta #port #dried \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Yet another experiment at sous vide cooking using my homemade sous vide conversion kit. Short ribs are probably much better suited to slow cooking\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3950\n|PortionCalories = 1975\n|DatePublished=9th February 2015\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 2\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 1 day, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime = 1 day\n|Image = [[Image:Sous vide barbecue short ribs recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Hard to find short-ribs</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4.5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">But worth searching for.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nYet another experiment at [[Sous vide cooking|sous vide cooking]] using my homemade sous vide conversion kit.  [[Short ribs]] are probably much better suited to [[Slow cooking|slow cooking]] (''[[Beef short ribs (slow cooker recipe)]]'') than sous vide cooking as they need prolonged cooking to break down the [[Fats|fats]] and collagen to make them palatable.  10 hours in the [[Slow cooker|slow cooker]] is just about right from the experiments I've done.  Anyway, to my thinking, the benefits of sous vide cooking in a sealed pouch would be in  concentrating the [[Marinade|marinade]] flavours.\n[[Image:Vacuum large bag vertical.jpg|300px|thumb|right|An oversized bag hung vertically lessens the chance of liquid being sucked into the sealer]]\n\nIn the end the results were very good, but no better than [[Slow cooking|slow cooking]] the [[Short ribs|short ribs]].\n\nI cooked the [[Short ribs|short ribs]] in the [[Marinade|marinade]] for 24 hours at 75\u00b0C(''167\u00b0F'')\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 800g rack of halved beef [[Short ribs|short ribs]] containing 2 [[Ribs|ribs]]\n}}\n'''[[Marinade|marinade]]'''\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Sea Salt|sea salt]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| 2 tablespoons [[Tomato puree|tomato puree]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Dried|dried]] [[Parsley|parsley]]\n| 1 tablespoon Heinz [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]]\n| 1 square of Bournville [[Chocolate|chocolate]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Muscovado sugar|muscovado sugar]]\n| 50 ml ruby [[Port|port]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Mix the [[Marinade|marinade]] ingredients together (I microwaved them for a minute just to melt the [[Chocolate|chocolate]] and enable it to mix well)\n| Place the [[Marinade|marinade]] and the [[Short ribs|short ribs]] in an oversized vacuum pouch.  This helps prevent the marinade being sucked into the sealer.\n| Cook sous vide at  75\u00b0 (''167\u00b0F'') C for 24 hours.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nThis went well served with [[Peas|peas]], [[carrots]], some extravagant looking [[Pasta|pasta]] and some of the [[Sauce|sauce]] poured over.\n===Chef's notes===\nAs [[Short ribs|short ribs]] release an awful amount of [[Fat|fat]], it might be an idea, if you have the time, to allow them to cool, skim the solidified fat and reheat to serve.\n{{SousVideSeeAlso}}\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#shortribs #marinade #sousvidebarbecueshortribs #slowcooking #chocolate #sousvidecooking #fat #peas #pasta #port #dried </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Spam fritters, British recipe \n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#spamfritters #guinness #bitter #branstonpickle #chips #spam #batter #bakedbeans #fritter #frying #fry \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=I know I shouldn't, but I just love Spam, especially in the form of a fritter, served with baked beans, chips and Branston pickle - it's junk food at\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1547\n|PortionCalories = 386\n|DatePublished=23rd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|ImageComment = Spam fritters, [[home made Branston pickle]]<br />and strong coffee, the perfect breakfast!\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes\n|PrepTime = 25 minutes\n|CookTime = 15 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Spam fritters recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Naughty, but nice!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Delicious and dead easy to make. Fried in olive oil they are almost healthy! </span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Image:Spam fritters frying.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Spam fritters, fried]]\nI know I shouldn't, but I just love [[Spam]], especially in the form of a [[fritter]], served with [[Baked beans|baked beans]], [[Chips|chips]] and [[Branston pickle]] - it's junk food at its worst and its best.  Go on, indulge!\n\nIf you like these, give our [[Spam pizza]] a try as well!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 tin [[Spam]], cut into 10 mm (1/2\" slices)\n| [[Olive oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n}}\n\n'''[[Batter]] mix'''\n* 60 g [[Self-raising flour|self-raising flour]]\n* 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n* Splash of [[Guinness]], [[Bitter|bitter]] or if you must, [[Milk|milk]] and water mixed (about 35 to 40 ml of liquid is required)\n* Splash of [[Louisiana hot pepper sauce]] or [[Tabasco sauce]] (to taste)\n* Pinch of [[Salt|salt]]\n* A little plain flour\n\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add all of the dry [[batter]] ingredients to a bowl, then whisking well, add just enough fluid ([[Guinness]], [[Bitter|bitter]], or the [[Milk|milk]]/water mix) to make a thick batter. Add the egg and mix it in extremely well.\n| Rest the batter in the [[refrigerator]] for 20 minutes if you can\n| Dip each piece of spam in a saucer of plain flour and knock off any excess (this helps the batter mix to stick)\n| Dip each piece of spam in the batter \n| Heat a shallow [[Frying pan|frying pan]] with a little [[Oil|oil]]. When it has just started to smoke, reduce the heat a little and [[Fry|fry]] the fritters a few at a time for 3 minutes a side\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe hot with [[Baked beans|baked beans]], [[Chips|chips]] and [[Branston pickle]] or [[OK Sauce]]\n=== Tip ===\n\nTo make it easier to dip the pieces of spam in the batter, use a fork and spear the slice about 1cm from its end. Have the bowl of batter as close to the frying pan as possible, then dip the Spam and transfer into the hot oil immediately. Slide the fritter off the fork with a knife or other metal implement. '''Do not use your fingers at any point - severe burns can occur!!'''\n\nAlternatively, if you're handy with a pair of chopsticks, you can grip the end of the Spam with them and do the dipping and transferring that way. For me, the only disadvantage of this method is that there is always a 'naked' uncovered bit on the fritter. Forking it is the only way!!!\n==See also==\n{{FritterRecipes}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with beer]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spamfritters #guinness #bitter #branstonpickle #chips #spam #batter #bakedbeans #fritter #frying #fry </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

[[Spam]] cooks up really well when grilled at a very high heat so is ideal for a [[Stone baked pizza]].\n\nIf you really don't like the idea of using [[Spam]], use fresh [[ham]] instead.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 portion [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] - Makes 2 pizzas\n| 150 g ball of [[Mozzarella cheese|mozzarella cheese]], torn into pieces\n| 1 340 g can of [[Spam]] original (chopped pork and ham), cut into thin strips.\n| [[Extra virgin olive oil]] for drizzling\n| 1 cup [[Spicy tomato sauce|spicy tomato sauce]]\n| Handful of [[Basil leaves|basil leaves]], torn\n| 1 tablespoon [[Fine yellow cornmeal|cornmeal]]\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Make the [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]] as instructed\n* If using a [[pizza stone]], preheat the [[pizza stone]] under a very hot [[grill]] for about 20 minutes.  Place it about 8cm (3\") from the heat source.\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Make 1 pizza per person\n| Dust the work surface with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| Stretch or roll the [[Dough|dough]] into two thin rounds\n| Prick the pizza all over with a fork. This prevents it puffing up too much and burning while it is cooking\n| Place the pizza dough on a [[pizza peel]] that has been dusted with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]]\n| With a deft move, slide the pizza dough from the [[pizza peel]], on to the [[pizza stone]].\n| Cook for about 2 minutes on one side only or until lightly browned.\n| Remove from the oven, flip over and add the topping.\n| Repeat for the second pizza whilst you prepare the first.\n| Drizzle the [[Pizza|pizza]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and spread the pizza with &frac12; of the [[Tomato sauce|tomato sauce]]\n| Top with torn [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]] and sliced [[Spam]].\n| Add a final drizzle of [[olive oil]] or for a spicy touch, some [[chili oil]].\n| [[Bake]] for 3 or 4  minutes or until the [[Cheese|cheese]] browns a little - watch it carefully as it can burn easily.\n| Remove and sprinkle with torn [[Basil|basil]].\n| Keep the fist pizza warm at the bottom of the oven whilst you make the second.\n| Serve hot\n}}\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[pizza peel]] use an upturned plate or a flat baking tray, dusted with [[Fine yellow cornmeal|fine yellow cornmeal]] and some deft handwork to slide the dough onto the stone.\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes]]\n[[Category:Italian recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spam #fineyellowcornmeal #pizzapeel #spampizza #pizzastone #oliveoil #pizzadough #bake #ham #pizza #cheese </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I've found the best way is to use a meta-based pan, similar to a baking tray.  The metal base gets hot enough to crisp the base properly.  I have a really heavy rectangular Le Creuset baking tray that is absolutely ideal.  It seems a shame as it will mean I'll never use my earthenware deep pan pizza dish again!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 medium [[chicken breasts]] chopped very finely.\n| 1 small [[Onion|onion]], chopped finely\n| 3 cloves of [[garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1 teaspoon [[Chilli flakes|chilli flakes]] (Guajillo - not too hot)\n| 1 teaspoon dried [[oregano]]\n| 1 portion of [[Pizza dough|pizza dough]]\n| [[Fine yellow cornmeal]] for dusting\n| 110 g (4 oz) [[Cheddar cheese]], [[Grated|grated]]\n| 85 g (3.5 oz) freshly [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan cheese]]\n| 1 large can of chopped peeled [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]], left to drain over a coarse sieve for 5 minutes\n| Pinch of [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| 1 ball of [[Buffalo|buffalo]] [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]], torn\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 190\u00b0 C (375\u00b0 F - gas 5), [fan oven 170\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n* Make the [[Dough|dough]] as instructed\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Spicy chicken mozarella.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Just before the grated parmesan is added\nImage:Spicy chicken pizza.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken cooked, ready to add\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Add 2 tablespoons of olive oil to a hot frying paan or [[wok]] and add a good grind of [[black pepper]]\n| Add the [[onions]] and saut\u00e9 for 3 minutes.\n| Stir in the chopped [[chicken breasts]], the [[garlic]], the [[chilli flakes]] and [[oregano]] and stir-fry for 3 or 4 minutes just to colour the chicken.\n| [[Spray]] or lightly [[Oil|oil]] a deep 25cm (10\") pizza dish or pan\n| Roll out 2/3rds of the [[Dough|dough]] to about 3mm and line a pan so the [[Dough|dough]] just  overlaps the edges and trim any excess\n| Sprinkle the base with the [[Cheddar cheese]]\n| Add the chicken mixture\n| Sprinkle with one third of the [[Parmesan cheese]]\n| Roll out the remaining [[Dough|dough]] to make a lid\n| Pinch the lid so it joins the base and make a few slashed in the top for [[Steam|steam]] to escape\n| Mix another third of the [[Parmesan cheese]] with the [[Herbs|herbs]] and [[Spices|spices]] and mix into the [[Tomatoes|tomatoes]]\n| Spread the tomato mixture over the top of the [[Dough|dough]]\n| Top with crumbled [[Mozzarella|mozzarella]] and sprinkle with the remaining [[Parmesan cheese]]\n| [[Bake]] for 45 minutes, resting a sheet of [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] on top of the [[Pizza|pizza]] for the final 10 minutes\n| Allow to cool for 10 minutes before slicing and serving\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a [[Green salad|green salad]]\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Pizza recipes]]\n[[Category:I believe I can fry recipes]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer Well done you.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nI made this as a little experiment and it went down so well with everyone that I've decided to add it as a recipe.\n\nThis recipe is fairly healthy as it does not need to be [[Deep-fried|deep-fried]].  I've used [[Olive oil|olive oil]] but you could use any [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]].  If you do use [[Olive oil|olive oil]], as its smoke point is much lower that most [[Frying|frying]] [[Oils|oils]], so keep the temperature lower than you normally would, or put the smoke alarm in the garden!\n\nAlthough the preparation time is shown as 4 hours, you could sacrifice the [[Marination|marination]] period if you were short on time.\n\nI've used [[Tex-Mex mix]] for the seasoning, but in place of that you could just add a pinch of [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] and any powdered [[Spices|spices]] that you fancy.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 2 large [[Chicken breasts|chicken breasts]], chopped into thumb-sized pieces\n| 1 tablespoon [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n| &#188; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]] for the [[Marinade|marinade]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Taco-mix|taco-mix]] for the [[Marinade|marinade]]\n| 1 large [[Clove|clove]] of [[Garlic, peeled and crushed|garlic, peeled and crushed]]\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n| 2 tablespoons fine [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]]\n| 5 tablespoons [[Plain flour|plain flour]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Taco-mix|taco-mix]] for the 'batter'\n| Enough [[Olive oil|olive oil]] to fill the base of a [[Wok|wok]] by 1.3cm (1/2\")\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Add the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces, [[Salt|salt]], [[Taco-mix|taco-mix]], [[Lime juice|lime juice]] and [[Crushed garlic|crushed garlic]] to a [[Lock and Lock box]], replace the lid, shake very well and leave in the [[Fridge|fridge]] for 3 or four hours to [[Marinade|marinade]], shaking now and then if you can.\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Chicken pieces frying in the wok.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken pieces frying in the wok\nImage:Chicken pieces coated with flour, ready to fry.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Chicken pieces coated with flour, ready to fry\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Heat the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] in a [[Wok|wok]] or [[Frying pan|frying pan]].  Not too hot that it smokes.\n| Add the [[Taco-mix|taco-mix]] (or your desired [[Spices|spices]]) to a bowl containing the [[Plain flour|plain flour]] and mix well.\n| When you are ready to [[Fry|fry]] the [[Chicken|chicken]], add two tablespoons of [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] to the [[Chicken|chicken]] pieces and shake really well to coat the chicken evenly.\n| Beat the [[Egg|egg]] and add to a bowl.\n| [[Dip]] each pice of [[Chicken|chicken]] in the beaten [[Egg|egg]], then coat coat with the spicy [[Flour|flour]] mix, then carefully add to the hot [[Oil|oil]].  Do this in two batches so you don't overwhelm the [[Oil|oil]] and kill the temperature.\n| [[Fry]] for about 2 to 3 minutes, turning often.\n| Remove the cooked [[Chicken|chicken]] with a [[Slotted spoon|slotted spoon]] and allow to drain on kitchen paper.\n| Check the [[Chicken|chicken]] is properly cooked, though it should be fine as the pieces are very small and turning them ensures an even heat.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe with a mixed [[Salad|salad]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#chicken #oliveoil #spicyfriedchickenpieces #egg #marinade #wok #limejuice #plainflour #fry #cornmeal #spices </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

cup [[White wine|white wine]] or water\n| 1 [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n| Sea [[Salt|salt]] and freshly ground [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| [[Flour]] for rolling\n| [[Olive]] [[Oil|oil]] for [[Frying|frying]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| With clean hands, mix the [[Mince|mince]], [[Onion|onion]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]], [[Oregano|oregano]], [[chili flakes]] and [[Mint|mint]].\n| Moisten the [[Bread|bread]] in the [[Wine|wine]] or water.\n| Add [[Bread|bread]] and [[Egg|egg]] to [[Meat|meat]]. Knead well.\n| Shape into 2.5 cm (1\") balls, dust with [[Flour|flour]], and [[Saute|saute]] in hot [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]] until [[Browned|browned]] and cooked to your liking.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nUse them to make [[New York-style stone baked pizza]], [[Meatball pizza]] or serve them with [[spaghetti]] and one of the following [[sauces]].\n* [[Balsamic vinegar gravy]]\n* [[Sofrito (Spanish tomato sauce)]]\n* [[Spicy tomato salsa]]\n* [[Tomato sauce for pizza]]\n* [[Roast garlic and sherry vinegar sauce]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Beef recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#bread #olive #garlic #mint #dried #egg #sauces #flour #onion #spicymeatballs #oregano </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Juicy tuna flakes mixed with tomatoes and rice\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2760\n|PortionCalories = 690\n|DatePublished=24th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = The production line!\n|Servings = Serves 4 as a main course\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 40 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = 25 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Grilled spicy tuna burritos recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Texy-Mexy</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Big bold burritos, packed with taste.  Amazing.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nA great filling for a [[burrito]]. Juicy [[tuna]] flakes mixed with [[tomatoes]] and [[rice]].  Other fish varieties would work fine including [[red snapper]], [[cod]], [[bass]], [[bream]] and [[pollack]]\n[[Image:Spicy tuna burritos recipe.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Spicy tuna burritos, ready to roll!]]\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 175 g (6 oz) [[tuna steaks]] per person\n| 90 g (3.5 oz) [[basmati rice]]\n| 1 small [[onion]]\n| 1 teaspoon ground [[achiote seed]] ([[annatto powder]])\n| A few small dried [[chillies]], ground to a powder\n| 75 g (3 oz) flaked [[almonds]]\n| 1 400g tin chopped [[tomatoes]]\n| 85 g (3&frac12; oz) [[Cheddar cheese]], grated\n| 6 large wheat [[flour]] tortillas\n| 2 tablespoons [[olive oil]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Preheat the grill\n| In a small frying pan, toast the [[almonds]] until browned. Careful not to burn them!  Set aside\n| Cook the [[tuna]] for 4 minutes per side on an oiled grill tray.  When cooked, flake into a bowl and set aside\n| Rinse the [[rice]] well under cold running water\n| In a large pan, cover the [[rice]] with boiling water, return to the boil and simmer for about 8 minutes.  Drain and set aside\n| Heat the oil in a large pan and cook the [[onion]] until soft and translucent\n| Add the [[achiote powder]] and [[Chili powder|chili]] powder and cook for a few minutes\n| Add the rice and stir fry for a minute\n| Add the [[tomatoes]], stir well and then cover and simmer until most of the juice has been absorbed into the rice (about 15 minutes)\n| Warm the tortillas under a grill for a few minutes (or seconds in a microwave)\n| Stir in the cheese and serve\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nYou can roll the [[burritos]] in the kitchen so they are ready to serve or bring the mixture to the table in a bowl and let everyone make their own.\n\nServe with wedges of [[lime]] and a green salad\n\n===Variations===\n\nMake the [[burritos]] and heat under a grill for a few minutes for an interesting change.\n\nIf you can't get [[Annatto powder|annatto powder]], try other spices such as [[cumin]] and [[paprika]].\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Cheese recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Rice recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Tuna]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#spicytunaburritos #tomatoes #rice #almonds #burritos #onion #tuna #annattopowder #redsnapper #basmatirice #burrito </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
