title": "Succotash (Native American)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Succotash (Native American) Cooking with chillies recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#succotash #limabeans #corn #beans #squash #limejuice #vegetableoil #vegetables #garlic #favabeans #greenbeans \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=Succotash is standard American fare, the addition of squash probably makes the a more traditional recipe\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1284\n|PortionCalories = 321\n|DatePublished=25th October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Succotash without the squash\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 35 minutes\n |PrepTime = 15 minutes\n |CookTime = 20 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Succotash.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">It's just mixed vegetables</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">1</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I've bags of these in the freezer, from Tesco's \ud83d\ude03</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Succotash]] is standard American fare, the addition of [[Squash|squash]] probably makes the a more traditional recipe.\n[[Succotash]] (from the native American Narragansett; ms\u00edckquatash, \"[[Boiled|boiled]] [[Corn|corn]] kernels\") is a food dish consisting primarily of [[Lima beans|lima beans]], [[Carrots|carrots]] and [[Sweetcorn|sweetcorn]], possibly including pieces of [[Cured meat|cured meat]] or [[Fish|fish]]. \n\nThis method of preparing [[Vegetables|vegetables]] became very popular during the Great Depression in the United States. It was sometimes cooked in a [[Casserole|casserole]] form, often with a light pie crust on top as in a traditional pot pie. In some parts of the American south, any mixture of [[Vegetables|vegetables]] prepared with lima [[Beans|beans]] and topped with [[Lard|lard]] or [[Butter|butter]] is called succotash. Succotash is a traditional dish of many Thanksgiving celebrations in Pennsylvania and other states. In Indiana, Succotash is made with [[Green beans|green beans]] and corn instead of lima [[Beans|beans]].\n\nOther uses of the word \"[[Succotash|succotash]]\" include its use as the catch phrase of the Warner Bros. cartoon cat Sylvester; \"Sufferin' succotash\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 20 ml [[Vegetable oil]]\n| 2 cups fresh, [[Frozen|frozen]] or drained, canned [[Corn|corn]]\n| 1 large [[Onion|onion]], peeled and chopped finely\n| 2 medium [[Sweet peppers|sweet peppers]], any colour, de-seeded chopped\n| 1 or 2 fresh [[Hot chillies|hot chillies]], de-seeded and chopped into rings\n| 1 cup [[Butternut squash|butternut squash]] flesh, cut into 1 cm (1/2\") cubes\n| 2 cups canned [[Lima beans]], drained\n| 2 Cloves of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| 1 tablespoon [[White cumin|white cumin]], freshly [[Ground|ground]]\n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste.\n| &frac12; cup [[Chicken|chicken]] or [[Vegetable Stock|vegetable stock]]\n}}\n'''Garnish'''\n* Bunch of finely chopped coriander leaves, stems discarded\n* Squeeze of [[lemon juice]] or [[lime juice]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Heat 1 tablespoon of [[Vegetable oil|vegetable oil]] in a large pan or [[Wok|wok]] until [[Smoking|smoking]]\n| Add the [[Corn|corn]], [[Peppers|peppers]] and [[Onions|onions]] and saut\u00e9 until the onions start to take a little colour, about 6 to 7 minutes\n| Reduce the heat, add the [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Squash|squash]] cubes, [[Salt|salt]], [[Pepper|pepper]] and [[Cumin|cumin]] and cook for about 4 minutes, stirring often.\n| Add the [[Stock|stock]] and the [[Lima beans|lima beans]] and [[Simmer|simmer]] until the [[Squash|squash]] is tender\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nServe garnished with [[Coriander|coriander]] and [[Lime juice|lime juice]]\n===Variations===\nIf you cannot obtain [[Lima beans|lima beans]] then try [[Fava beans|fava beans]], [[Broad beans|broad beans]], [[Flageolet beans|flageolet beans]], '''Sufferin' [[Succotash|succotash]] - use any [[Beans|beans]]''' - just try the recipe!\n==See also==\n* [[Succotash (British ingredients)]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Ingredients]]\n[[Category:Beans]]\n[[Category:Prepared foods]]\n[[Category:Vegetables]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]][[Category:Pan fried]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#succotash #limabeans #corn #beans #squash #limejuice #vegetableoil #vegetables #garlic #favabeans #greenbeans </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }

title": "Tex-Mex beercan chicken",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tex-Mex beercan chicken, a chicken recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#beer #chicken #texmexbeercanchicken #tacomix #oliveoil #wine #cider #cocktailstick #roastpotatoes #steam #orange \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is an unusual way to cook chicken with beer\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2711\n|PortionCalories = 677\n|DatePublished=28th July 2013\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 1 hour 40 minutes\n |PrepTime = 10 minutes\n |CookTime = 1 hour 30 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Tex-Mex beercan chicken recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">You MUST make this</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This was one of the first 'variations' on beer can chicken that I ever made, and it's once of the best.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis is an unusual way to cook [[Chicken|chicken]] with [[beer]]. The basic idea is to carefully balance the chicken on a 3/4 full can of beer using its legs as an additional support, coat it with a flavoured rub and [[roast]] it.  The [[Steam|steam]] from the beer permeates the chicken to produce a succulent dish.  I think my [[Taco mix|taco mix]] suits this admirably, though any flavoured rub would do.\n\nOur American friends seem to barbecue chicken using this method, and though I'm sure it's worth trying, I can't believe that the upper part of the chicken would even get warm on our barbecue.  And we have a BIG barbecue.  I would welcome any feedback.\n\nThe process is made even easier and safer with one of these: [[Grillpro Stainless Steel Chicken Roaster]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.5kg free range [[Chicken|chicken]]\n| 6 tablespoons [[Taco mix|taco mix]], El Paso taco mix or a seasoning rub of your choice\n| 2 tablespoons [[Olive oil|olive oil]]\n| 440ml can of [[Beer|beer]] or [[Lager|lager]] \n| 1 [[tangerine]] or [[orange]] (optional)\n\n}}\n\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the oven to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - Gas 6)\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Wash the outside of the beer can\n| [[Parson's nose|Remove the parson's nose]], any giblets, bags, tranklements etc. from the [[Chicken|chicken]] \n| Cut off and discard the [[Parson's nose]].\n| Rinse inside and out under cold running water and pat dry with kitchen towel\n| Rub 1 tablespoon of the [[Taco mix|taco mix]] into the cavity of the bird \n| Rub the outside of the [[Chicken|chicken]] with the [[Olive oil|olive oil]] and coat with 3 tablespoons of [[Taco mix|taco mix]]\n| Seal the neck of the bird by folding over and skewering with [[skewers]] or [[cocktail sticks]] \n| Open the [[Beer|beer]] and toast the start of the proceedings with about a &#188; of the beer - you don't want a full can\n| Punch a few holes around the empty top-part of the can\n| Add the remaining rub to the [[Beer|beer]] tin\n| Sit the [[Chicken|chicken]] on the [[Beer|beer]] can in a baking tray and balance it on its legs. A small chicken sits quite happily; a large chicken might be a bit trickier\n| Cut the top off the tangerine so the juice can run down while it cooks, affix with a [[cocktail stick]] into the top cavity (see photo) and add the cut slice as a hat!\n| Place the baking tray in the bottom of the oven\n| After 30 minutes, reduce the heat to 180\u00b0 C ( 350\u00b0 F - Gas 4)\n| The [[Chicken|chicken]] should be cooked in about 1.5 hours [total cooking timw], depending upon the size of the bird. Check every 15 minutes towards the end.  It is done when the juices run clear if the deepest part of the flesh (eg the thigh) is pierced with a metal skewer or sharp knife\n| Remove the [[Chicken|chicken]] extremely carefully with [[Oven gloves|oven gloves]] and tongs if needed.\n| Allow to rest for 10 minutes before carving\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Tex-Mex beercan chicken ready.jpg|thumb|250px|right|Oven-ready!\nImage:Tex-Mex beercan chicken ingredients.jpg|thumb|300px|right|The basic ingredients\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\nUsing [[The Jamie Oliver carving method|the Jamie Oliver carving method]], serve with [[roast potatoes]] and [[garlic mayonnaise]].\n\nThe remaining beer could be used to make gravy if needed.\n===Variations===\nTry this with a cock [[pheasant]] (hens are too small) and use [[cider]] or [[wine]] instead of [[beer]].  Wash out an empty 440 ml [[beer]] can and pour 330 ml of dry white [[wine]] or dry [[cider]] into it.  For this, a [[herb]] and [[Garlic|garlic]] rub is excellent - this can be made with the ingredients (minus the [[onion]] and [[pork]]) used in the [[Slow roast herby pork belly]] recipe.\n\nWe have also tried this with a small [[duck]], but the cavity was too large for the [[beer]] can, but not big enough for two cans.  Duckling might be worth a try if you can get it.\n===Chicken falls over?===\nMy chicken has just fallen over, I may have to get one of these: [http://www.socal.co.uk/BBQ_Accessories/Beer_Can_Chicken/Grillpro_Stainless_Steel_Chicken_Roaster/332/17302 (beer can) Chicken roaster]\n\nLarge chickens seem to be ok - it's the smaller birds that have problems balancing on a beer can.  440ml is probably the biggest can you should use with all but the largest birds. The last few times I have made this, I have placed the chicken and can inside an oven proof saucepan, in the oven, so the chicken has a little more support if it tends to lean over.  It also makes far less mess if it does fall over!\n\n... or go for the real thing: '''[[Grillpro Stainless Steel Chicken Roaster]]'''!\n{{Template:Beercan chicken - See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with beer|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Chicken]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Student recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#beer #chicken #texmexbeercanchicken #tacomix #oliveoil #wine #cider #cocktailstick #roastpotatoes #steam #orange </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }

Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime = 2 hours 20 minutes\n|PrepTime = 2 hours\n|CookTime = 20 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tex-Mex pork fried.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Spicy fried pork</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Perfect with chips \ud83d\udc37\ud83c\udf5f\ud83d\udc37\ud83c\udf5f\ud83d\udc37\ud83c\udf5f. </span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\nTry this [[Pork|pork]] recipe for [[Mexican]]-style [[Fried|fried]] pork, using the best cut of pork and your favourite [[Chillies|chillies]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1 [[Pork|pork]] fillet cut into 4 steaks or 4 pork escallops, [[Pork fillet|flattened as shown here]] (don't cut them into strips though)\n| 1 tablespoon [[Cider|cider]] [[Vinegar|vinegar]]\n| 2 of your favourite [[Chillies|chillies]], rehydrated if dried and deseeded (to taste)\n| 2 [[Cloves|cloves]] of [[Garlic|garlic]], peeled and crushed\n| Sea [[Salt|salt]] and freshly ground [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n| Juice of 1 [[lemon]]\n| Dash of [[olive oil]] for the marinade\n| [[Olive]] [[Oil|oil]] for fryng (It's not authentic, but I feel so much healthier when [[Frying|frying]] with [[Olive oil|olive oil]]!)\n| 1 large [[Egg|egg]], beaten\n}}\n\n'''Seasoned [[Flour|flour]]'''\n* Sea [[Salt|salt]] and freshly ground [[Black pepper|black pepper]]\n* 75 g (3 oz ) [[masa harina]] or [[yellow cornmeal]]\n* 75 g (3 oz ) plain [[Flour|flour]]\n* 2 tablespoons of [[Taco mix]]\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix together, the [[Vinegar|vinegar]], [[Garlic|garlic]], [[Chillies|chillies]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]], [[lemon juice]] and a splash of [[olive oil]] and mix to a thin marinade.\n| Coat the [[Pork|pork]] steaks with the marinade, refrigerate and allow to infuse for at least 2 hours.\n| Add the two flours, the [[taco mix]] to a shallow dish and mix well to combine\n|# You can omit the taco mix but it would be a shame as it gives the coating a homemade 'Kentucky-fried' flavour.\n| [[Dip]] both sides of the steaks into the seasoned [[Flour|flour]]\n| Knock off any excess [[Flour|flour]] and [[Dip|dip]] into the beaten [[Egg|egg]], then back into the seasoned flour.\n| Again, knock off any excess [[Flour|flour]].\n| [[Fry]] in a little [[Olive|olive]] [[Oil|oil]] until the pork is properly cooked and golden brown on both sides.\n| Pat any excess [[Oil|oil]] off on a kitchen towel.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Pork fillet breaded.jpg|thumb|300px|right|'Breaded' fillets\nImage:Pork fillet marinade.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Marinading\n</gallery>\n===Serving suggestions===\n\nServe with [[yellow rice]] and [[tomato salsa]].\n\n===Chef's note===\n\nIf you can't get [[Masa harina]] then use [[yellow cornmeal]] instead.\n\n{{Template:ThinkPig}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Main courses|Pork]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:North American recipes|Pork]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#flour #chillies #pork #oliveoil #egg #garlic #blackpepper #olive #dip #masaharina #yellowcornmeal </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }
                ]
            }
        }
    }

It's easy, allows you to tailor it to your taste\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 35\n|PortionCalories = 35\n|DatePublished=22nd October 2012\n|Author=Chef\n|Servings = 8 teaspoons of the spice mix is the equivalent of a 35 g (1.25 oz) packet of [[taco]] seasoning\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime = 15 minutes\n|PrepTime = 15 minutes\n|CookTime = None\n|Image = [[Image:Tex-Mex seasoning recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Better than El Paso mixes</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This beats the (expensive) commercially made Tex Mex mixes, hands down.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nRather than buying packets of Mexican spice mix from that well known company, make your own.  It's easy, allows you to tailor it to your taste.  The recipe is easy to adjust to make different quantities.\n\nThe Main ingredients that give that authentic flavour are the [[oregano]], [[cumin seeds]] and [[chili powder]].  I would suggest you keep those at the levels here and adjust the other items if you have a desire to tinker.\n\nEverything is in teaspoons to make it easy to make different quantities - use tablespoons at the same rate to make more.\n===Commercially available Tex-Mex seasoning===\nI also use ready made seasoning mixes, but the one I had been using changed and was far too salty so I went in search of another supplier.  This let to my discovery of [[Taste Sensation Ltd]].  if you love your spices and seasonings, take a look at them.  They sell them directly and via [https://www.amazon.co.uk/stores/TasteSensation/node/4434351031 Amazon UK] and I can thoroughly recommend them.  Also, Nick Lumby, who has run the company for 20 years, is a really nice guy!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 2 teaspoons [[chili powder]] or chili flakes or crushed dried chillies\n| 2 teaspoons [[paprika powder]]\n| 2 teaspoons dried [[Mexican oregano]] or [[oregano]] leaves\n| 3 teaspoons [[dried garlic granules]] or [[Garlic|garlic]] powder\n| 1 teaspoon [[sea salt]]\n| 6 teaspoons [[white cumin]] seeds\n| 5 teaspoons [[onion]] powder or dried onion flakes\n}}\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Grind all the ingredients to powder in a [[coffee grinder]]\n| Mix together well if you had to do this in batches\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\n\nStore in an airtight container out of the light.\n\n35 g of this spice mix is sufficient to season; [[chicken]], [[pork]], [[beef]] for four people.  Rub the mix on the [[meat]], coat well with a tablespoon of [[vegetable oil]] and 1 tablespoon [[lemon juice]] and marinate for 2 hours.\n\nI've recently discovered [[Old India Taco Seasoning]], which saves me from makling this.  It's sold in 500g quantities, which last us about 4 months!  Wonderful stuff.  Give it a try.\n\nA good [[:Category:Indian ingredients (supplier)|Asian grocer / wholesaler]] will [[stock]] all of the ingredients for this recipe, and a whole lot more besides!\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chilli pepper recipes]]\n[[Category:Marinades dressings and butters]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Spices]]\n[[Category:Uncooked]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#texmexseasoning #chilipowder #oregano #vegetableoil #paprikapowder #whitecumin #stock #driedgarlicgranules #garlic #coffeegrinder #beef </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "The renowned Mr Brown's Pulled Pork (Slow cooker recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=The renowned Mr Brown's Pulled Pork (Slow cooker recipe)\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#slowcooker #onion #groundblackpepper #smokedpaprikapowder #vegetables #greensalad #coarseseasalt #chillipowder #sherry #cayennepepper #apple \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=We make pulled pork fairly regularly - and this is my slow cooker variation of The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3798\n|PortionCalories = 949\n|DatePublished=5th July 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Served in [[pitta pockets]] with a crispy salad\n |Servings = Serves 4\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 8 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 8 hours\n |Image = [[Image:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - (slow cooker recipe).jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Beat this!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">..you cannot.</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Klapaucius|Klapaucius]] </span></span>\n}} \nWe make [[pulled pork]] fairly regularly - and this is my [[slow cooker]] variation of [[The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental]], originally from [[:Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes|FotoosVanRobin recipes]].\n\nIdeally this should also marinade for 12 hours in the fridge to allow the flavours to penetrate.  However as there are lots of powerful spices in this, coupled with an 8 hour cook, I think it will be just as good without the extended marinating.\n\nThe [[Meat|meat]] is great as a main meal with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[potatoes]] or with a salad or even as a [[Sandwich|sandwich]] filler.  My favourite way is to have it as a [[Kebab|kebab]]-type filling in [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]] with [[Salad|salad]].\n\nI have included this in the North American recipe category as a homage to the original.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) boneless [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]].\n| &#189; tablespoon coarsely [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| &#189; tablespoon coarsely ground [[Szechuan pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Smoked paprika powder|smoked paprika powder]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 4 tablespoons cane [[Sugar|sugar]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coarse sea salt|coarse sea salt]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]])\n| 2 tablespoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 1 teaspoon [[Cayenne pepper|cayenne pepper]] or a [[Chilli powder|chilli powder]] mix of your choice\n| &#189; cup  [[Shaoxing rice wine]], [[Sherry|sherry]] or even spirit of your choice\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 1 [[Armagh_Bramley_Apples|Bramley apple]], peeled, cored and sliced\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:pulled pork in a slow cooker.jpg|Pork joint after 8 hours, shredded and ready to serve\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Spices|spices]], cut deep slashes on both sides of the joint so you have lots af places to pack the rub into.\n| Carefully slice the rind from the joint and discard it.\n| Ensure that the rub fills all of the cuts you've made and all surfaces are well covered.\n| Chop the [[Apple|apple]] and [[Onion|onion]] and place in the base of the [[slow cooker]]\n| Sit the pork on top of the onions and apples.\n| Pour the wine down the side of the cooker so as not to wash off the rub.\n| Slow cook on low for 8 hours.  It never seems to hurt if you cook a dish like this for longer, so don't worry if you have to leave it cooking for longer.\n| If you get the chance, turn the meat halfway through the cooking process\n| 30 minutes before you are ready to serve, use two forks and shred the meat while it's still in the slow cooker and then leave it to cook in the gravy for the final 30 minutes.\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nShred with two forks and serve in [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] with a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Slow cooker recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#slowcooker #onion #groundblackpepper #smokedpaprikapowder #vegetables #greensalad #coarseseasalt #chillipowder #sherry #cayennepepper #apple </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "The renowned Mr Brown's Pulled Pork (Sous-Vide recipe)",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=The renowned Mr Brown's Pulled Pork Sous-vide recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#salad #whitewine #stickblender #vacuumbag #potatoes #onions #armagh_bramley_apples #onion #therenownedmrbrownspulledporksousviderecipe #vacuumseal #garlicpowder \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=We make pulled pork regularly, and this is my sous-vide variation of The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{Template:AdvancePreparationIcon}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3851\n|PortionCalories = 481\n|DatePublished=14th May 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n |Servings = Serves 8\n |Difficulty = 2\n |TotalTime = 24 hours 20 minutes\n |PrepTime = 20 minutes\n |CookTime = 24 hours\n |Image = [[Image:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - sous-vide recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Pulled Pork Perfection</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">This recipe cannot be beaten - we make this regularly now!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry]] </span></span>\n}}\nWe make [[pulled pork]] regularly - and this is my [[sous vide]] variation of [[The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental]], originally from [[:Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes|FotoosVanRobin recipes]].\n\nThis should also marinade for 12 hours in the fridge to allow the flavours to penetrate.  However as there are lots of powerful spices in this, in the [[sous-vide bath]] for 24 hours will be just as good without the extended marinating.\n\nCooking this sous-vide makes the meat really tender, however the onions and apples don't break down as well as they do when it is cooked conventionally. I've found the solution to this to blitz the gravy with [[stick blender]].\n\nThe [[Meat|meat]] is great as a main meal with [[salad]] and [[potatoes]].  My favourite way is to have it as a [[Kebab|kebab]]-type filling in [[Pitta bread|pitta bread]] with [[Salad|salad]].\n\nI have included this in the North American recipe category as a homage to the original.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 1.3 kg (3 lb) boneless [[Pork shoulder|pork shoulder]]\n| &#189; tablespoon coarsely [[Ground black pepper|ground black pepper]]\n| &#189; tablespoon coarsely ground [[Szechuan pepper]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Smoked paprika powder|smoked paprika powder]]\n| 3 tablespoons [[Paprika powder|paprika powder]]\n| 4 tablespoons [[muscovado sugar]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Coarse sea salt|coarse sea salt]]\n| 2 teaspoons [[Mustard powder|mustard powder]])\n| 2 tablespoons [[Garlic powder|garlic powder]]\n| 1 tablespoon [[Ginger powder|ginger powder]]\n| 2 [[Bird's eye chili peppers|Bird's eye chili pepper]] ground to powder (or chilli of choice, to taste.)\n| &#190; cup [[white wine]]\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped\n| 1 [[Armagh_Bramley_Apples|Bramley apple]], peeled, cored and sliced\n}}\n\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Spices|spices]] and add to a very large [[vacuum bag]] together with the chopped [[onions]] and [[apple]]\n| Carefully slice the rind from the joint and discard it.\n| Cut the pork joint into smaller pieces or slash it up so the marinade can penetrate easily\n| Add to [[vacuum bag]] with the remaining ingredients\n| [[Vacuum seal]] the bag.  Use the cancel button and 'Seal Only' button to prevent liquid being pulled into the [[vacuum sealer]]\n| Leave in the fridge to 12 hours or more\n| Cook in a [[sous vide water bath]] for 24 hours at 80\u00b0 C [176\u00b0 F]\n| Remove the meat and shred with 2 forks\n| Blitz the gravy mixture with a [[stick blender]] and thicken and reheat before mixing the meat back in. \n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - shredding.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Shred with two forks\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - (sous-vide recipe).jpg|thumb|300px|right|Vacuum sealed and ready to cook for 24 hours at 70 degrees C.  ''An egg to show scale''\n</gallery>\n\n===Chef's notes===\nRunning low on the 'fridge white wine', I used a mix of [[white wine]], [[sherry]] and [[calvados]]!\n\nBe careful removing such a large (and quite hot) vacuum bag from the sous vide bath. The bottom of my bag split slightly as I lifted it out, luckily only losing a little of the gravy.  Support it as you lift it out!\n===Serving suggestions===\nShred with two forks and serve with [[jacket potatoes]] and a [[salad]] with [[sour cream]] as a dip.\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:Sous vide recipes]]\n[[Category:Sous vide cooking]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#salad #whitewine #stickblender #vacuumbag #potatoes #onions #armagh_bramley_apples #onion #therenownedmrbrownspulledporksousviderecipe #vacuumseal #garlicpowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

Hers was an adapted version of [http://www.bbq-nl.com/2009/07/the-renowned-mr-brown.html the original] (''Dutch'').  I have further adapted [http://www.flickr.com/photos/fotoosvanrobin/6308694585/ hers].\n\nThe [[Meat|meat]] is great as a main meal with [[Vegetables|vegetables]] and [[potatoes]] or with a salad or even as a [[Sandwich|sandwich]] filler. cup  [[Shaoxing rice wine]], [[Sherry|sherry]] or even spirit of your choice\n| 1 [[Onion|onion]], peeled and roughly chopped (or equivalent in [[Spring onions|spring onions]] or [[Leeks|leeks]])\n| 1 [[Apple|apple]], peeled, cored and cubed\n\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental slow roast.jpg|After 4 hours...\nImage:The renowned Mr Brown Pulled Pork - Oriental slow roast marinaded.jpg|Ready to cook\n</gallery>\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan oven 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Mix the [[Spices|spices]], cut deep slashes all over the meat and rub the mixture well into the pork.\n| Place in a [[Lock & Lock]]-style box and [[Refrigerate|refrigerate]] for 24 hours, shaking up now and again.\n| Chop the [[Apple|apple]] and [[Onion|onion]] and place in the base of a [[Baking|baking]] dish\n| Sit the [[Pork|pork]] on top, pour over the [[Wine|wine]] and add a little more rub to the top\n| Cover with [[Tin-foil|tin-foil]] and cook for 4 hours\n}}\n===Serving suggestions===\nShred with two forks and serve in [[Pitta breads|pitta breads]] with a [[Green salad|green salad]].\n===Chef's notes===\nIf you are not to use it all in one go, only shred what you will use straight away, store the remainder in the [[Refrigerator|refrigerator]], unshredded in a [[Lock & Lock box]]. This way it will stay moist. \nFollow the [[RSPCA Think Pig Checklist]] to make sure that your [[Pork|pork]] has come from pigs that have been reared to higher welfare standards.\n{{Template:See-also-pulled-pork}}\n{{Template:PeelingGinger}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Chinese recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Oriental cuisine]]\n[[Category:Pork recipes]]\n[[Category:Cooking with wine]]\n[[Category:FotoosVanRobin recipes]]\n[[Category:Stewed, braised or pot roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#therenownedmrbrownpulledporkoriental #apple #onion #pulledpork #pork #sandwich #pittabreads #wine #coarseseasalt #miseenplace #smokedpaprikapowder </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

This hardens it  an turns it into a large crispy edible [[Taco|taco]]!\n\nYou must use an [[Oven|oven]]-proof bowl and you may have to experiment to find the bowl that produces the best shape.  I've found that  a small and a medium [[Glass|glass]] pyrex bowl work really well.\n\nFill them with the food of your choice, you'll find them to be much stronger than you might imagine.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 1 pack of soft [[Wheat|wheat]] [[Flour tortilla|flour tortilla]] wraps or soft [[Cornmeal|cornmeal]] [[Tortilla|tortilla]] wraps.\n| [[Olive oil]] for spraying for [[Brushing|brushing]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 200\u00b0 C (400\u00b0 F - gas 6), [fan oven 180\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Lightly [[Spray|spray]] or [[Brush|brush]] your [[Oven|oven]]-proof bowls so the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] wrap doesn't stick once it has been [[Baked|baked]].\n| Lightly [[Spray|spray]] the top surface of the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] with a little [[Olive oil|olive oil]], not too much.\n| Push the [[Tortilla|tortilla]] into your bowl so it makes a 'useful' shape.\n| [[Bake]] the [[Tortillas|tortillas]], in the bowls for 6 minutes or until they start to colour.\n| Watch them closely as the time between [[Browning|browning]] and burning is really short!\n| Carefully remove the bowls from the [[Oven|oven]] and invert them over [[Paper towels|paper towels]] and knock the shaped [[Tortilla|tortilla]] out onto the paper towels.\n| They remain soft and pliable while they are still hot so leave them upside down for 15 minutes or so to cool and harden, ready for use.\n| If like me, you don't have enough bowls, you can make these in batches, they keep pretty well for a day or so.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\n[[Image:Edible tortilla bowl.jpg.jpg|thumb|300px|right|Lightly greased and ready to bake]]\n</gallery>\n\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Starters]]\n[[Category:Tapas, mezze and antipasti]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Salad recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n[[Category:Unusual recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortilla #tortillabaskets #spray #flourtortilla #wheat #brush #oliveoil #flour #yellowcornmeal #taco #miseenplace </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

There are many recipes and methods for cooking whole turkeys\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 20778\n|PortionCalories = 1731\n|DatePublished=4th January 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 12\n|Difficulty = 2\n|TotalTime =  5 hours, 30 minutes\n|PrepTime =  1 hour, 30 minutes\n|CookTime =  4 hours\n|Image = [[Image:RoastTurkey_CP.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Perfect!</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Roast turkey doesn't get any better than this!</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The&nbsp;Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[Roast turkey]] usually forms the centrepiece of Thanksgiving in the United States. There are many recipes and methods for cooking whole [[Turkeys|turkeys]]. Below is one of the simplest and therefore one of the most traditional.\n\nCooking [[Turkey|turkey]] and [[Stuffing|stuffing]] involves the risk of salmonella poisoning. To prevent this, cook the [[Turkey|turkey]] to 185 [[Degrees|degrees]] [[Fahrenheit]] and the [[Stuffing|stuffing]] to 165 [[Degrees|degrees]] [[Fahrenheit]]. Also, avoid cross contamination by keeping raw turkey away from all foods and wash your hands thoroughly after handling it.\n\nThe most effective way to measure food temperatures is with a digital [[Meat thermometer|meat thermometer]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 8kg (18 pound) whole [[Turkey|turkey]]\n| &#189; cup [[Butter|butter]], softened\n| 1.5 quarts homemade [[Turkey|turkey]] [[Stock|stock]] or canned [[Chicken stock|chicken stock]]\n| [[Salt|salt]] and [[Freshly ground black pepper|freshly ground black pepper]] to taste\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 160\u00b0 C (325\u00b0 F - gas 3), [fan [[Oven|oven]] 140\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Preheat [[Oven|oven]] to 325 [[Degrees|degrees]] [[Fahrenheit]]. Place the rack in the lowest position of the [[Oven|oven]].\n| Remove the neck and giblets.\n| Rinse the [[Turkey|turkey]] and pat it dry with [[Paper towels|paper towels]].\n| Place the [[Turkey|turkey]], breast side up, on a rack in the [[Roasting pan|roasting pan]]. Rub the skin with softened [[Butter|butter]], and season with [[Salt|salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]].\n| Fill the body cavity with [[Stuffing|stuffing]].\n| Place a [[Meat thermometer|meat thermometer]] in the thickest part of one [[Thigh|thigh]].\n| Position an [[Aluminium foil| aluminium foil]] tent over the [[Turkey|turkey]].\n| Place the [[Turkey|turkey]] in the [[Oven|oven]], and pour two cups of [[Stock|stock]] into the bottom of the [[Roasting pan|roasting pan]].\n| [[Baste]] the entire [[Turkey|turkey]] every 30 minutes with the juices on the bottom of the pan.\n| Add [[Stock|stock]] to the drippings as they become dry, about one to two cups at a time.\n| Remove [[Aluminium foil| aluminium foil]] tent after two and a half hours.\n| [[Roast]] until the [[Meat|meat]] reaches 185 [[Degrees|degrees]] [[Fahrenheit]] and the [[Stuffing|stuffing]] reaches 165 [[Degrees|degrees]] [[Fahrenheit]]. This should take about 4 hours.\n| Serve immediately.\n}}\n==See also==\n* '''[[Meat cooking time calculator Metric|A comprehensive guide to roast meat cooking times]]''' - give the time you want to carve your roast and we'll give you a timed step by step roasting guide\n*[[Stuffing recipes|A large selection of stuffing recipes]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Historic recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Meat recipes]]\n[[Category:Poultry recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#turkey #fahrenheit #degrees #stuffing #stock #roastingpan #traditionalroastturkey #meatthermometer #butter #baste #roast </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

I can see why it's popular!\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 2905\n|PortionCalories = 726\n|DatePublished=31st October 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  50 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  40 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:Tuna Noodle Casserole recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n'''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Noodleishous!</span>'''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I especially love the breadcrumb topping.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:TheJudge|The Judge]] </span></span>\n}}\n[[:Category:I believe I can fry recipes|Julia]] from [[:Category:I believe I can fry recipes|I believe I can fry]], puts this far better than I could:\n\n\"[[Tuna]] [[Noodle|noodle]] [[Casserole|casserole]] is considered a classic by many; it's quick to prepare, super cheap, and easy enough to throw together at any time. For me, it's a recipe that I can make at any time, since I almost ALWAYS have all of the ingredients already in the house.\"\n\nIt's not a recipe that is known to me, maybe that's because I'm not American?  Sound jolly nice though!\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 6oz wide or extra wide [[Egg noodles|egg noodles]]\n| 1 5oz can [[Tuna|tuna]] packed in water, drained and flaked with a fork\n| 1 can condensed [[Cream of mushroom soup|cream of mushroom soup]]\n| &#189; cup [[Milk|milk]]\n| 1 cup [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]], cooked\n| &#190; cup [[Shredded|shredded]] sharp [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]]\n| &#189; cup [[Dried|dried]] [[Bread crumbs|bread crumbs]]\n| 1 tablespoon melted [[Butter|butter]]\n| &#188; cup [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan cheese]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Cook the [[Egg noodles|egg noodles]] according to package directions. Drain and transfer to a large mixing bowl.\n| Cook the [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]]: simply [[Microwave|microwave]] them in a bowl with a few tablespoons of water for 2-3 minutes, covered with [[Cling-film|cling-film]].\n| Add the [[Peas|peas]], [[Tuna|tuna]], [[Cream of mushroom soup|cream of mushroom soup]], [[Milk|milk]], & [[Shredded|shredded]] [[Cheese|cheese]]. Stir until well combined.\n| Transfer to a greased 9x9\" [[Baking|baking]] dish. Toss the [[Bread crumbs|bread crumbs]] with the melted [[Butter|butter]]. Sprinkle evenly atop the [[Casserole|casserole]]. Top with [[Grated|grated]] [[Parmesan]].\n| [[Bake]] in a 350-degree [[Oven|oven]] for 30 minutes. Let [[Rest|rest]] about 5 minutes before serving.\n}}\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Tuna pasta peas oven.jpg|Out of the oven\nImage:Tuna pasta peas mixed up.jpg|Everything mixed, ready for the topping\nImage:Tuna pasta peas pretty.jpg|Tuna, pasta and peas added, how pretty!\n</gallery>\n===Recipe source===\n:Recipe from www.ibelieveicanfry.com/2011/09/tuna-noodle-casserole.html I believe I can fry\n*Her inspiration for this dish:\n*http://pinchmysalt.com/2008/09/19/serious-comfort-tuna-noodle-casserole-recipe/\n===See also===\n* [[Tuna noodle casserole with mushrooms]] - ''my version of this dish''.\n\n{{Template:YoutubePastaDough}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:I believe I can fry recipes]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tunanoodlecasserole #tuna #eggnoodles #grated #shredded #frozenpeas #butter #casserole #breadcrumbs #peas #noodle </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Tuna noodle casserole with mushrooms",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Tuna noodle casserole with mushrooms recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tuna #darksoysauce #grated #sweetcorn #mushrooms #breadcrumbs #frozenpeas #butter #tunanoodlecasserole #pasta #rest \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=This is my variation on Julia's Classic American recipe: Tuna noodle casserole \n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 1574\n|PortionCalories = 393\n|DatePublished=3rd November 2014\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = \n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 1\n|TotalTime =  50 minutes\n|PrepTime =  10 minutes\n|CookTime =  40 minutes\n|Image = [[Image:JPs Tuna Noodle Casserole recipe.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Nicer with normal pasta \ud83e\udd24</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">I would chose macaroni instead, next time.</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:Chef|Jerry, aka Chef]])</span></span>\n}}\nThis is my variation on [[:Category:I believe I can fry recipes|Julia's]] [[Tuna Noodle Casserole|Tuna noodle casserole recipe]].  It is essentially the same but I'm adding it as a unique recipe so I can reproduce it again easily. From the gusto with which our Siamese cats consumed the remains in the preparation bowl, I think it's going to be tasty!\n\nThe changes I've made are to use [[Celebrity_Chefs_on_Desert_Island_Discs#Antonio_Carluccio_-_broadcast_6th_July_2008|Antonio Carluccio's]] '[[Gallery_of_pasta_types|Pappardelle al Funghi Porcini]]' (Durum wheat pasta with porcini mushrooms), more [[tuna]] than [[Tuna Noodle Casserole|Julia's recipe]], sliced [[mushrooms]], [[dark soy sauce]] and [[Mah\u00f3n-Menorca cheese]].\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 175 g (6oz) [[Celebrity_Chefs_on_Desert_Island_Discs#Antonio_Carluccio_-_broadcast_6th_July_2008|Antonio Carluccio's]] '[[Gallery_of_pasta_types|Pappardelle al Funghi Porcini]]' (Durum wheat pasta with porcini mushrooms)\n| 1 400g can [[Tuna|tuna]] packed in water, drained and flaked with a fork - 280g drained weight\n| 1 small can condensed [[Cream of mushroom soup|cream of mushroom soup]]\n| 300 ml [[milk]] (fill the condensed mushroom can with [[milk]] and rinse out the can)\n| 6 large [[button mushrooms]], sliced\n| 1 cup mixed [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]] and frozen [[sweetcorn]], cooked\n| &#189; cup grated [[Mah\u00f3n-Menorca cheese]]\n| 2 tablespoons of [[Dark soy sauce]]\n| [[Salt]] and [[freshly ground black pepper]]\n| &#189; cup [[Dried|dried]] [[Bread crumbs|bread crumbs]]\n| 1 tablespoon melted [[Butter|butter]]\n| &#188; cup [[Grated|grated]] mature [[Mah\u00f3n-Menorca cheese]]\n}}\n===[[Mise en place]]===\n\n* Preheat the [[Oven|oven]] to 180\u00b0 C (350\u00b0 F - gas 4), [fan oven 160\u00b0 C & reduce cooking time by 10 mins per hour]\n<gallery widths=300px heights=300px perrow=5>\nImage:Tuna mushroom pasta casserole.jpg|thumb|240px|right|Ready for the breadcrumbs\nImage:Pappardelle al Funghi Porcini, Durum wheat pasta with porcini mushrooms.jpg|thumb|240px|right|Antonio Carluccio's Pappardelle al Funghi Porcini (Durum wheat pasta with porcini mushrooms)\n</gallery>\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Cook the [[pasta]] for 5 to 6 minutes in salted boiling water.  He say's 3 to 4 minutes but I found the cooking times on all of the pasta in this Carluccio 'gift pack' to be rather too short for my taste.\n| Cook the [[Frozen peas|frozen peas]]: simply [[Microwave|microwave]] them in a bowl with a few tablespoons of water for 2-3 minutes, covered with [[Cling-film|cling-film]].\n| Add the [[Peas|peas]], [[sweetcorn]], [[Tuna|tuna]], sliced [[mushrooms]], [[Cream of mushroom soup|cream of mushroom soup]], [[Milk|milk]], & [[grated]] [[Cheese|cheese]]. Add a few tablespoons of [[dark soy sauce]] a pinch of [[salt]] and a generous pinch of [[black pepper]]. Stir until well combined.\n| Transfer to a greased 9x9\" [[Baking|baking]] dish. Toss the [[Bread crumbs|bread crumbs]] with the melted [[Butter|butter]]. Sprinkle evenly atop the [[Casserole|casserole]]. Top with [[Grated|grated]] [[Mah\u00f3n-Menorca cheese]].\n| [[Bake]] in the top half of a 350-degree [[Oven|oven]] for 40 minutes, covered for the first 30 minutes, remove the lid for the final 10 minutes. Let it [[Rest|rest]] about 5 minutes before serving.\n}}\n===See also===\n* [[Tuna Noodle Casserole]]\n===Chef's notes===\nAs I had a little spare time I made this a good few hours ahead.  If you do this, refrigerate it, covered, and leave the breadcrumb stage until you're ready to bake it.\n\n{{Template:YoutubePastaDough}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Main courses]]\n[[Category:Fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Pasta recipes]]\n[[Category:Sea fish recipes]]\n[[Category:Stews and casseroles]]\n[[Category:Baked or roasted]]\n[[Category:Favourite recipes]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tuna #darksoysauce #grated #sweetcorn #mushrooms #breadcrumbs #frozenpeas #butter #tunanoodlecasserole #pasta #rest </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"

title": "Vegetarian New York truck tortillas",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Vegetarian New York truck tortillas recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#coriander #liquor #springonions #celery #corianderleaves #beans #saucepan #bayleaves #tortillas #onions #guacamole \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=A trip to New York introduced us to their posh food trucks, they were an eye opener about how delicious itinerant food can be\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|DatePublished=27th September 2016\n|Author=Chef\n|ImageComment = Unusual food truck - [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maximus/Minimus Maximus Minimus], not from New York though!\n|Servings = Serves 4\n|Difficulty = 3\n|TotalTime =  2 hours, 15 minutes\n|PrepTime =  15 minutes\n|CookTime =  2 hours\n|TotalCalories = 3694\n|PortionCalories = 923\n|Image = [[Image:Maximus_Minimus_food_truck_Seattle.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\">\n<span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">I just love the food truck</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">5</span>/5 </span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">A superb vegetarian recipe from two lovely people, Nik & Edwina.</span> \n\n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> [[User:PSmith|Paul&nbsp;R&nbsp;Smith]] </span></span>\n}}\nThis recipe is reproduced on [[Cookipedia]] courtesy of [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]].\n\nA trip to New York in early 2013 introduced us to their posh food trucks and stalls \u2013 they were an eye opener about how delicious itinerant food can be, especially the one we ate from on the corner of Wooster and Prince, between Chelsea and the Lower East Side. Also, hats off to all the food truck guys for feeding blacked-out areas of New York at cost price during Hurricane Sandy in October 2012 \n\nThe [[Bean|bean]] mix here is gorgeous; creamy and filling without being stodgy and bloaty, with a lovely clean beany flavour, and the various trimmings go incredibly well with it. Unlike some UK interpretations of [[Tortillas|tortillas]], these are free from the ersatz flavours of [[Refried beans|refried beans]], [[Cumin|cumin]] and [[Garlic|garlic]]. What follows are broad guidelines \u2013 this is mainly about the [[Black bean|black bean]] recipe.\n{{RecipeIngredients\n\n| 8 [[Soft corn tortillas|soft corn tortillas]] \n}}\n====the beans ====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 200g [[Black beans|black beans]], soaked for 2 hours and drained \n| 2 medium [[Carrots|carrots]], peeled and quartered \n| 3 sticks of [[Celery|celery]] sliced lengthways and cut in two \n| 2 [[Onions|onions]], halved \n| large bunch of [[Coriander|coriander]] stalks, tied together with string \n| 2 [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] \n| 4 small [[Spring onions|spring onions]], finely chopped \n| 1 tablespoon powdered [[Coriander|coriander]] \n| [[Salt]] and [[Pepper|pepper]] \n| 2 tablespoons chopped [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]]\n}}\n====the [[Guacamole|guacamole]]==== \n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 2 ripe [[Avocados|avocados]], [[Mashed|mashed]] \n| 1 teaspoon [[Cayenne|cayenne]] \n| [[Juice|juice]] of a [[Lime|lime]] \n| [[Sea Salt|sea salt]] \n}}\n====to serve====\n{{RecipeIngredientsNB\n| 80g [[Cheddar cheese|cheddar cheese]], [[grated]] \n| 140ml [[Sour cream]] \n| 100g [[Iceberg lettuce|iceberg lettuce]], roughly sliced  \n| Chopped mild [[Red chillies|red chillies]], deseeded,  or pickled [[Chillies|chillies]] (San Marcos [[Pickled]] [[Chipotle]] is especially good)\n| 2 halved [[Limes|limes]]\n}}\n\n===Method===\n{{RecipeMethod\n\n| Put the soaked and drained [[Beans|beans]], [[Carrot|carrot]], [[Celery|celery]], [[Onions|onions]], [[Bay leaves|bay leaves]] and [[Coriander|coriander]] stalks into a large lidded [[Saucepan|saucepan]], and top up with just enough water to cover everything.\n| Place on a low heat and bring to the [[Boil|boil]].\n| Cook gently for 90 -120 minutes until the beans are tender.\n| Drain and reserve the cooking [[Liquor|liquor]]. Pick out and discard the carrot, celery, onions, [[Bay|bay]] leaves and coriander stalks. \n| Return the drained [[Beans|beans]] to the large [[Saucepan|saucepan]], add 3 tablespoons of the cooking [[Liquor|liquor]], the [[Spring onions|spring onions]], the [[Coriander powder|coriander powder]], and season well. Cook gently for 8 minutes.\n| Check seasoning again, and add a little more liquor if it looks too dry \u2013 the mixture should be very slightly runny.\n| Resist any temptation to [[Mash|mash]], these beans are meant to be kept whole.\n| Stir in the [[Coriander leaves|coriander leaves]].\n| Set aside and keep warm.\n| Warm through the [[Tortillas|tortillas]], then bring everything to the table and let everyone assemble their own wraps and enjoy.\n| Y'all have a nice day now!\n}}\n===Variations===\nFor a [[Vegan|vegan]] version, just omit the [[Cheese|cheese]] and the [[Cream|cream]] use for the topping.\n==See also==\n\n* Another of [[Nik and Edwina's Cookbook]], based largely upon this recipe: [[Deconstructed tortilla salad]]\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:British recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Spicy recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Grain and bean recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Nik and Edwina's Cookbook recipes]]\n[[Category:Boiled or simmered]]\n[[Category:Recipes from other sites]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#coriander #liquor #springonions #celery #corianderleaves #beans #saucepan #bayleaves #tortillas #onions #guacamole </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
                    }

title": "Wheat flour tortilla recipe",
                "revisions": [
                    {
                        "contentformat": "text/x-wiki",
                        "contentmodel": "wikitext",
                        "*": "<!-- seo -->\n{{#seo:\n|title=Wheat flour tortilla, a vegetarian recipe\n|titlemode=replace\n|keywords=#tortillapress #shortening #dough #griddle #fat #wheatflourtortillarecipe #masaharina #vegetableshortening #lard #hand #grilled \n|hashtagrev=032020\n|description=The are cheap to buy, but not expensive and much nicer when homemade. We also have a good recipe for corn tortillas that uses masa harina for that\n}}\n<!-- /seo -->\n\n{{Template:CookTools}}\n{{recipesummary\n|TotalCalories = 3813\n|PortionCalories = 635\n|DatePublished=12th April 2013\n|Author=JuliaBalbilla\n|Servings = Serves 6 \n |Difficulty = 3\n |TotalTime = 45 minutes\n |PrepTime = 30 minutes\n |CookTime = 15 minutes\n |Image = [[Image:Wheat flour tortillas.jpg|alt=Electus]]\n<span class=\"review\"> <span class=\"reviewHeader\">\n====Best recipe review====\n</span>\n''<span class=\"reviewTitle\">Fun to make</span>''\n\n<span style=\"line-height:180%\"><span style=\"font-size:180%;\"><span class=\"reviewScore\">4</span>/5</span>\n\n<span class=\"reviewDesc\">Not too difficult either</span>\n \n<span class=\"reviewAuthor\"> - [[User:PSmith]] </span></span>\n}}\n\nThe are cheap to buy, but not expensive and much nicer when homemade.\n\nWe also have a good recipe for [[Corn tortillas|corn tortillas]] that uses [[Masa harina|masa harina]] for that real authentic taste.\n\n{{RecipeIngredients\n| 800 g [[Plain flour|plain flour]], sifted.\n| &frac12; teaspoon [[Salt|salt]].\n| 100 ml [[Hand|hand]]-hot water\n| 100 g [[Vegetable shortening]]\n}}\n===Method===\n\n{{RecipeMethod\n| Rub the [[Flour|flour]], [[Salt|salt]] and [[Shortening|shortening]] together unti it resembles fine [[Breadcrumbs|breadcrumbs]].\n| Little by little add the water and mix to a [[Dough|dough]].\n| Cover with a damp cloth and leave for 20 minutes.\n| Divide into golf-ball sized balls or slightly larger.\n| Roll out on a floured worktop.\n| Cook for about a minute on a hot [[Tava|tava]] or [[Griddle|griddle]] pan until they puff up.\n}}\n===Chef's notes===\n[[Vegetable]] [[Shortening|shortening]] is a solid vegetable [[Fat|fat]] such as Crisco or Trex.  [[Lard]] could be used without any problems but the recipe would no longer be vegetarian.\n===Chef's note===\nIf you don't have a [[tortilla press]], use 2 chopping boards or just two sheets of wood as a substitute.  Place ball of [[dough]] between two non-stick surfaces such as small squares of [[Bake-O-Glide]] and stand on them!\n===Suppliers===\nSee the [[Tortilla Press]] page for UK suppliers.\n{{Tortillas-See also}}\n{{RecipeLine}}\n[[Category:Recipes]]\n[[Category:Accompaniments]]\n[[Category:Bread and baking]]\n[[Category:Latin American recipes]]\n[[Category:Mexican recipes]]\n[[Category:Snacks and light bites]]\n[[Category:Tex-Mex recipes]]\n[[Category:North American recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetable recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegetarian recipes]]\n[[Category:Vegan recipes]]\n[[Category:Pan fried]][[Category:Grilled, griddled or barbecued]]\n\n<!-- footer hashtags --><code 'hashtagrev:032020'>#tortillapress #shortening #dough #griddle #fat #wheatflourtortillarecipe #masaharina #vegetableshortening #lard #hand #grilled </code><!-- /footer_hashtags -->"
